The Khateeb's Sneezing and the Role of Intention
Ruling on effectiveness of intention in khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to differentiate between valid and invalid utterances during the Friday khutbah.

Core Idea
Intention determines whether a khateeb's speech remains part of the khutbah or breaks it.

A khateeb's every word during the Friday khutbah carries weight. But what happens when a natural action like sneezing interjects? The same utterance—'Alhamdulillah'—can either uphold or invalidate the prayer. This teaching explores how the maxim 'actions are judged by intentions' resolves this apparent contradiction, illustrating the centrality of niyyah in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
State the governing maxim
Recall the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'—actions are judged by intentions. Recognize that this maxim governs acts of worship where intention distinguishes ibadah from mere habit.
This is a major (kubra) maxim of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the khutbah as a conditioned act
The Friday khutbah is a condition (shart) for Salat al-Jumu'ah. It requires specific content: praise of Allah, salawat, and admonition. Any speech not intended as part of the sermon can break it.
The khateeb must maintain the intended purpose of the khutbah.
3
Apply the maxim to the utterance
Take the furu' case: 'Alhamdulillah' can be either part of the intended khutbah (praise within the sermon) or a habitual response to sneezing. The intended purpose—not the mere wording—determines the ruling.
The same words have different legal effects based on niyyah.
4
Derive the ruling
If the khateeb intended the words as part of the sermon, the khutbah remains valid (sahih). If he intended to respond to the sneeze, the utterance is extraneous and invalidates the khutbah (batil).
This demonstrates the practical application of the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَطَسَ الْخَطِيبُ، فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ الْخُطْبَةَ صَحَّتْ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحَمْدَ لِلْعُطَاسِ لَمْ تَصِحَّ.
The khateeb sneezed, and he said, 'Alhamdulillah.' If he intended the khutbah, it is valid; if he intended praise for the sneeze, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses the Friday khutbah (sermon). The khateeb is required to deliver specific words; if he says 'Alhamdulillah' during the khutbah, its validity depends on intention. If he says it with the intention of continuing the khutbah (as a part of the sermon), the khutbah remains valid. However, if he says it purely as a response to his own sneeze (i.e., out of habit), then the khutbah becomes invalid because the speech was not part of the intended sermon. This illustrates how the same utterance can either uphold or break the prayer depending on intention.

Key Terms
خطيب (khatib): The person delivering the Friday sermon (khutbah).
الخُطْبَة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered by the khatib before the prayer.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; the mental purpose behind an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the khateeb says 'Alhamdulillah' during the khutbah with the intention of praising Allah as part of the sermon, what is the ruling?
A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Makruh
D) Must repeat

Key Takeaway
The same utterance can either validate or invalidate the khutbah based solely on the khateeb's intention.

Intention in Slaughter: Saying Alhamdulillah After a Sneeze
Ruling on slaughterer saying Alhamdulillah after sneeze during slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that intention (niyyah) determines the legal status of an utterance in the context of the condition of tasmiyah during slaughter.

Core Idea
The ruling on the meat depends on whether 'Alhamdulillah' was intended as tasmiyah or as praise for the sneeze.

This passage presents a subtle case from Hanafi fiqh where the same words ('Alhamdulillah') can either fulfill the condition of tasmiyah or not, solely based on the intention of the slaughterer. Understanding this requires grasping how intention (niyyah) interacts with verbal conditions (shurut).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Slaughter requires the condition of tasmiyah (saying Bismillah or similar) at the time of slaughter. Identify what the condition requires: an invocation (dhikr) that includes the name of Allah.
Tasmiyah is a shart, not a rukn, in Hanafi law.
2
Recognize the ambiguous utterance
The utterance 'Alhamdulillah' is a form of praise but can also function as a tasmiyah if intended as such. Note that the words themselves can serve both purposes legally.
Tasmiyah is not restricted to the exact phrase 'Bismillah'.
3
Apply the principle of intention
The Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (acts are judged by intentions) governs this case. The ruling hinges on what the speaker intended — tasmiyah or mere praise.
Intention is an internal state that must be inferred from context.
4
Derive the two outcomes
If he intended it as tasmiyah, the condition is fulfilled and the meat is halal. If he intended it merely as a response to sneezing, the condition is not fulfilled and the meat is haram.
If doubt exists about intention, the default is that tasmiyah was not intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذَبَحَ فَعَطَسَ، فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ التَّسْمِيَةَ حَلَّ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحَمْدَ لِلْعُطَاسِ لَمْ يَحِلَّ.
He slaughtered and then sneezed, and he said, 'Alhamdulillah.' If he intended the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah), it becomes halal; if he intended praise for the sneeze, it does not become halal.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') during slaughter. If the slaughterer is in the act of slaughtering and sneezes, then says 'Alhamdulillah', the ruling depends on intention. If he intends the words 'Alhamdulillah' as the required tasmiyah (since tasmiyah can be expressed in different forms), then the slaughter is valid and the meat is halal. If he intends it as a response to the sneeze without intending tasmiyah, then the slaughter is invalid because the required invocation was not made with proper intention. This demonstrates the principle that even proper words require the correct intention to fulfill their legal purpose.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (or similar) at the time of slaughter to make the meat halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What determines whether 'Alhamdulillah' said during slaughter fulfills the requirement of tasmiyah?
A) The wording of the utterance
B) The intention of the slaughterer
C) The volume of the utterance
D) The time it is said relative to the cut

Key Takeaway
The validity of tasmiyah in slaughter depends on the utterance being intended as the required invocation, not merely on the words themselves.

Applications of the Maxim on Speech: Oaths, Prostration, and Vocative
Applying the qawida about speech requiring intention to furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-kalam ma kana bi al-qasd' to furuat involving oaths, prostration, and grammatical intent, and identify the mufta bihi position in each case.

Core Idea
Speech requires intention: an oath is not broken by speaking to a sleeper, and animal recitation does not obligate prostration.

In this lesson, we examine a central Hanafi legal maxim: that speech (kalam) is only considered such when done with intention (qasd). The author applies this to three distinct furuat: oaths, prostration of recitation, and Arabic grammatical rules. Each application demonstrates how intention transforms a seemingly similar action into different rulings. We will walk through each branch, noting the relied-upon Hanafi positions and the internal ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
The qawida is that speech is defined by intention. It governs all speech acts in fiqh, including oaths, ibadat, and linguistic interpretation.
The maxim is general, but its application varies based on context.
2
Analyze the oath scenario: sleeping addressee
Consider whether speaking to a sleeping person who hears breaks an oath. Note the difference of opinion: some say yes, the mashayikh say no unless the sleeper is awakened.
The key is that the sleeper is not attentive; intention alone is insufficient without a qualified addressee.
3
Analyze the prostration scenario: hearing from an animal vs. a person
Determine when hearing the verse of prostration obliges sujud. The reciter must have legal capacity (ahliyyah). Animals lack it, so prostration is not wajib; sleeping and intoxicated persons have capacity, so it is wajib.
Distinguish between the reciter's state and the hearer's obligation.
4
Analyze the linguistic scenarios: vocative and proper nouns
See how intention determines whether an indefinite noun in the vocative becomes definite or remains indefinite. Similarly, a proper noun derived from an attribute takes the definite article if the attribute is intended.
These grammatical rules are used in legal interpretation to determine the scope of a text.
5
Determine the mufta bihi in each case
For each furu, identify the relied-upon Hanafi position. For the oath case, the mashayikh's view is followed; for prostration, the relied-upon opinion is that hearing from a sleeper obliges, from an animal does not.
The fatwa hierarchy must be observed: later authorities (mashayikh) often settle ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفَرَّعْ عَلَى ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ مَا إِذَا حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلِّمُهُ، فَكَلَّمَهُ نَائِمَا بِحَيْثُ يَسْمَعُ، فَإِنَّهُ يَحْنَثُ، وَ فِي بَعْضِ رَوَايَاتِ الْمَبْسُوْطِ شُرِطَ أَنْ يُوْقِظَهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ مَشَائِخُنَا، لَأَنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَتَنَبَّهُ كَانَ كَمَا إِذَا نَادَاهُ مِنْ بَعِيدٍ وَهُوَ بِحَيْثُ لَا يَسْمَعُ صَوْتَهُ كَمَا فِي الْهِدَايَةِ وَالحَاصِلُ أنَّهُ قَدْ اخْتَلَفَ التَّصْحِيحُ فِيهَا، كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الشَّرْح وَلَمْ أرَ إلى الآن حُكم مَا إِذَا كَلَّمَهُ مُعْمى عَلَيْهِ [؟]، أَوْ مَجْنُوْنَا ، أَوْ سَكْرَانَ. وَلَوْ سَمِعَ آيَةَ السَّجْدَةِ مِنْ حَيَوَانِ صَرَّحُوْا بِعَدَمِ وُجُوْبِهَا عَلَى الْمُخْتَارِ لِعَدَمِ أَهْلِيَةِ الْقَارِيْ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا سَمِعَهَا مِنْ جُنُبِ ، أَوْ حَائِضِ، وَالسَّمَاعُ مِنَ الْمَجْنُونِ لَا يُوجِبُهَا، وَ مِنَ النَّائِمِ يُوْجِبُهَا عَلَى الْمُخْتَارِ، وَكَذَا تَجِبُ بِسَمَاعِهَا مِنْ سَكْرَانَ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ الْمُنَادَى النَّكِرَةُ إنْ قَصَدَ نِدَاءَ وَاحِدٍ بِعَيْنِهُ يُعَرَّفَ، وَوَجَبَ بِنَاؤُهُ عَلَى الفم، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَتَعَرَّف، وَأَعْرِبَ بِالنَّصَبِ. وَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ الْعَلَمُ الْمَنْقُولُ مِنْ صِفَةٍ إِنْ قَصَدَ بِه لَمْحَ الصَّفَةِ الْمَنْقُولِ مِنْهَا أَدْخِلَ فِيهِ الأَلِفُ وَاللَّامُ، وَإِلَّا فَلَا، وَفُرُوْعُ ذَلِكَ كَثِيرَةٌ .
And he derived from that in fiqh: when he swears not to speak to him, and then he speaks to him while he is sleeping such that he hears, then he breaks the oath. And in some narrations of al-Mabsut, it is conditioned that he wakes him, and upon it are our mashayikh, because if he does not become alert, it is like when he calls him from afar while he is in a state that he does not hear his voice, as in al-Hidayah. And the conclusion is that the verification has differed in it, as we explained in the commentary, and I have not yet seen the ruling when he speaks to one who is unconscious, or insane, or intoxicated. And if he hears the verse of prostration from an animal, they explicitly stated its non-obligation on the relied-upon opinion due to the lack of eligibility of the reciter, contrary to when he hears it from a junub or a menstruating woman. And hearing from an insane person does not oblige it, and from a sleeping person obliges it on the relied-upon opinion, and likewise it is obligatory by hearing it from an intoxicated person. And from that [maxim] is the indefinite vocative: if he intends to call a specific person, it is definite and must be built on damma; otherwise it remains indefinite and is put in the accusative. And from that is the proper noun transferred from an attribute: if by it he intends the implication of the attribute from which it is transferred, the definite article is entered, otherwise not. And its branches are many.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage applies a fundamental qawida (legal maxim) regarding speech: that for an utterance to be considered communicative speech (kalam), it must be done with intention (qasd). The author presents three applications. First, in the context of an oath: if a person swears not to speak to someone and then speaks to that person while he is asleep but audible, there is a difference of opinion. According to the majority (mashayikh), it does not break the oath unless the sleeping person is awakened, because without wakefulness, the speech does not fulfill the condition of intended address—similar to calling someone from afar who cannot hear. Second, regarding hearing the Qur'anic verse of prostration: if an animal recites it, since the animal lacks eligibility (ahliyyah) to be a reciter, prostration is not wajib on the hearer. However, hearing from a sleeping person does oblige prostration on the relied-upon opinion, because the sleeping person's recitation is considered his action (though unconscious). Hearing from an insane person does not oblige prostration due to lack of eligibility, while from an intoxicated person it does oblige. Third, in Arabic grammar as a legal tool: the indefinite vocative (mundā nakira) is definite if a specific person is intended and thus built on damma; otherwise it remains indefinite and is mansub. Similarly, a proper noun derived from an attribute (like 'al-Hārith') takes the definite article if the attribute is intended, otherwise not. These branches show how intention (qasd) governs legal and linguistic rulings.

Key Terms
كلام (kalam): Speech that conveys meaning with intention; not mere sound
حانث (hanith): One who breaks his oath
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; eligibility to perform acts with legal effect
منادى نكرة (mundā nakira): An indefinite noun used in vocative; its grammatical status depends on intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a person swears not to speak to Zaid, and then speaks to Zaid while Zaid is asleep but hears, does the oath break?
A) Yes, because the sleeping person heard the speech
B) No, unless the sleeping person is awakened
C) Yes, if the speaker intended to speak
D) No, never

Key Takeaway
Intention (qasd) is the defining factor for speech in Hanafi law, affecting oaths, worship, and linguistic interpretation.

Applying the Maxim: Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt in Purification
Expansion of maxim with a furu' from Fath al-Qadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to the case of an impure garment with unknown impurity location, and state the ruling regarding taharri.

Core Idea
Washing one edge of a certainly impure garment with unknown spot renders it pure; certainty is not overturned by doubt.

Imagine you know your garment is impure, but you cannot pinpoint where. How do you proceed? Hanafi jurists apply the cardinal maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt) to this scenario. In this lesson, we explore a classic furu' from Fath al-Qadir and explain why washing one edge is sufficient, and why taharri (effort to locate) has no effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
State the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt). This is a primary (kubra) maxim governing many fiqh rulings.
This maxim is the foundation of the ruling.
2
Understand the factual scenario
The garment is certainly known to be impure, but the exact location of the impurity is unknown. The person cannot remove it from the specific spot.
The certainty of impurity exists initially.
3
Apply the maxim after washing
When the person washes one edge of the garment, doubt arises: was the impurity on that washed spot? Since the original state of the garment was purity (before the impurity), that original purity is presumed to have returned after washing. The doubt does not overturn the original purity.
The ruling: the garment is pure, regardless of taharri.
4
Note the role of taharri
Taharri (effort to locate) has no effect in this ruling. Washing any portion suffices, with or without taharri.
This is explicitly stated in the source.
5
Consider the exception
If later it becomes known with certainty that the impurity was in a different part (not the washed edge), then the certainty of impurity overcomes the previous doubt, and all prayers performed in that garment must be repeated.
This is the other side of the same maxim: later certainty removes earlier doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي فَتحِ الْقَدِيرِ مِنْ بَابِ الْأَنْجَاسِ مَا يُوْضِحُهَا فَنَسُوقُ عِبَارَتَهُ بِتَمَامِهَا قَوْلُهُ تَطْهِيرُ النِّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ : مُقَيَّدٌ بِالإمْكَان وَأَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ يَتَمَكَّنْ مِنَ الْإِزَالَةِ لِخَفَاءِ خُصُوْصِ الْمَحَلِّ الْمُصَابِ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِتَنَجَسِ التَّوبِ قِبْلَ: الْوَاجِبُ غَسْلُ طَرْفِ مِنْهُ فَإِنْ غَسَلَهُ بِتَحَرُ اوْ بِلَا تَحَرِّ طَهُرَ . وَذِكْرُ الْوَجْهِ يُبَيِّنُ أَنْ لَا أَثْرَ لِلتَّحَرِّى وَهُوَ أَنْ يُغْسِلَ بَعْضَهُ مَعَ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ طَهَارَةُ الثَّوْبِ وَقَعَ الشَّكُ فِي قِيَامِ النِّجَاسَةِ لِإِحْتِمَالِ كَوْنِ الْمَغْسُوْلِ مَحَلَّهَا فَلَا يُقْضَى بِالنَّجَاسَةِ بِالشَّكَ كَذَا أَوْرَدَهُ الإِسْتيْجَانِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ الجَامِعِ الكَبِيرِ ترجمہ: اور فتح القدیر کے باب الانجاس میں وہ مسئلہ ہے جس سے اس کی وضاحت ہوتی ہے تو ہم اس کی پوری عبارت پیش کرتے ہیں صاحب ہدایہ کا قول تظہیر النجاسۃ واجب ( نجاست سے پاک کرنا واجب ہے) یہ امکان کی قید کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور جب کوئی نجاست لگنے کی خاص جگہ کے مخفی ہونے کی وجہ سے اسے زائل نہ کر سکتا ہو حالانکہ کپڑے کا نا پاک ہونا معلوم ہو تو کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کے کسی ایک کنارے کا دھونا واجب ہے لہذا اگر اس نے تحری کر کے یا بغیر تحری کے اسے دھویا تو وہ پاک ہو گیا اور کوئی کنارہ دھو دینے سے کپڑے کے پاک ہو جانے کی وجہ کا ذکر کرنا اس بات کا پتہ دیتا ہے کہ تحری کا اس میں کوئی اثر نہیں ہے اور وہ ( وجہ ) یہ ہے کہ اس کے بعض حصہ کو دھو تا با وجود اس کے کہ کپڑے کی پاکی اصل ہے نجاست کے باقی رہنے میں شک پیدا کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ دھلے ہوئے حصہ میں احتمال ہے کہ وہی اس (نجاست ) کی جگہ ہو تو شک کی وجہ سے نجاست کا فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا علامہ اسمیجائی نے شرح الجامع الکبیر میں بیان فرماتے ہوئے اس طرح بیان کیا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ قاعدہ کی وضاحت کے لئے اس مسئلہ کے متعلق فتح القدیر کی کئی عبارتیں پیش فرمائی ہے چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں نجاست کو پاک کرن حتی الامکان واجب ہے لیکن اگر کسی ایک شخص کو کپڑے کا ناپاک ہونا یقینی ہے لیکن جس جگہ نجاست لگی ہے اس کا خصوصی طور پر علم نہیں ہے کہ کہاں ہے لہذا وہ شخص اس طرح نجاست کو زائل کس طرح کرے تو ایسی صورت میں بعض فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک کنارہ کو دھونا کافی ہے اگر اس کے کنارے کو تحری کے ساتھ یا بغیر تحری کے دھولیا تو ایسی صورت میں کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا اور اس صورت میں طرف ثوب کو دھونے کے بعد طہار ثوب کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصل چیز کپڑے کا پاک ہونا ہے ایک کنارے کو دھونے کے بعد طہارت یا عدم طہارت کے بارے میں شک ہے کہ بقیہ کپڑے میں نجاست باقی ہے یا نہیں لہذا محض شک کی وجہ سے طہارت زائل نہ ہوگی اس لئے اس کپڑے کو پاک ہی کہا جائے گا اور اس میں نماز درست ہو جائے گی البتہ اگر بعد میں یقین کے ساتھ معلوم ہو گیا کہ نا پا کی دھوئے گئے کنارہ کے علاوہ میں تھی تو چونکہ نا پاکی کا یقین ہو گیا اس لئے اس کپڑے میں پڑھی گئی تمام نمازوں کا اعادہ واجب ہوگا علامہ اسیجائی نے شرح الجامع الکبیر میں اسی طرح بیان کیا ہے۔
In Fath al-Qadir, from the chapter on impurities, there is something that clarifies it. So we present his statement in full: His statement: 'Cleansing impurity is obligatory' is restricted by possibility. But if he cannot remove it due to the concealment of the specific spot of the impurity, while knowing that the garment is impure before? The obligatory is washing a portion of it. If he washes it with effort or without effort, it becomes pure. Mentioning the face explains that there is no effect for effort, and that is that he washes some of it while the original is the purity of the garment. Doubt arises about the persistence of the impurity because of the possibility that the washed part is its location, so impurity is not judged by doubt. Thus al-Isbiji recorded it in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir. Translation: And in Fath al-Qadir, from the chapter of impurities, is the issue that clarifies it, so we present his entire statement. The author of al-Hidayah said: 'Purifying impurity is obligatory'—this is restricted by possibility. When one cannot remove it due to the concealment of the specific place of the impurity, while the garment's impurity is known, it is said that washing one of its edges is obligatory. So if he washes it with taharri or without taharri, it becomes pure. Mentioning the reason shows that taharri has no effect. And that reason is that he washes some part of it, and despite the original purity of the garment, doubt arises about the persistence of impurity because the washed part might be its location. So impurity is not ruled due to doubt. Al-Isbiji stated similarly in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir. Explanation: For the clarification of the mentioned ruling, several passages from Fath al-Qadir have been presented. So they say: Removing impurity is obligatory as much as possible. But if a person is certain that his garment is impure but does not specifically know where the impurity is, then how can he remove it? In such a case, some jurists say that washing one edge is sufficient. If he washes that edge with taharri or without, the garment becomes pure. The reason for the garment's purity after washing one edge is that the original state is purity. After washing one edge, there is doubt about whether the impurity remains on the rest of the garment or not. Therefore, purity is not removed by mere doubt. So the garment is considered pure, and prayers performed in it are valid. However, if it later becomes known with certainty that the impurity was in a part other than the washed edge, then since impurity is certain, all prayers performed in that garment must be repeated. Al-Isbiji stated similarly in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an expansive application of the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' from Fath al-Qadir and its Urdu commentary. The case is a garment known to be impure but the exact spot of impurity is unknown. The ruling: washing one edge of the garment suffices, and the garment becomes pure. The reasoning: before washing, the garment is certainly impure (but location unknown). After washing one edge, doubt arises whether the impurity was on the washed spot or elsewhere. Since the original state of the garment (before impurity) was purity, that original ruling persists by the maxim. Thus the garment is deemed pure. The commentator emphasizes that taharri (effort to locate) has no effect in this ruling; the mere fact of washing one part creates doubt that the impurity may have been removed, and doubt does not remove the original purity. However, if certainty later arises that the impurity was elsewhere, the prayers must be repeated because certainty overcomes doubt. This illustrates the Hanafi position that original presumptions (istishab) are strong and not easily overturned.

Key Terms
تحري (taharri): Effort or attempt to determine the location of impurity through reasoning or investigation
نجاسة (najasa): Impurity that requires removal for validity of worship
طهارة (tahara): Purity from legal impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a garment certainly impure but with unknown location of impurity, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding taharri (effort to locate)?
A) Taharri is necessary; the person must try to locate the impurity before washing.
B) Taharri has no effect; washing one edge suffices with or without taharri.
C) Taharri is only required if the impurity is from blood.
D) Taharri is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' allows a garment with unknown impurity location to be purified by washing one edge, even without locating the exact spot.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
The Maxim 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt' Applied to Unknown Impurity Location
Applying 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to unknown impurity location with a Siyar parallel and critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to cases of unknown impurity location and to parallel cases in siyar, and evaluate the internal Hanafi critique regarding its application.

Core Idea
Certainty of purity is not removed by doubt of impurity location; washing one edge suffices.

This passage from Fath al-Qadir addresses a practical problem: you are certain your garment is impure but do not know where. How can you purify it without washing the whole garment? The Hanafi answer, based on the first major maxim of Islamic law, demonstrates how doubt does not overturn certainty. The discussion extends to a parallel in the law of war, then faces a critical objection from within the school—inviting you to weigh the reasoning yourself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Read the initial ruling: washing one edge of the garment is obligatory and suffices. Note that it applies when the impurity location is unknown but impurity existence is certain. The basis is the legal principle that original purity is certain.
The ruling does not require taharrī (scrutiny) – any edge works.
2
Understand the maxim's application
The justification: the garment was originally pure (certain). After washing one edge, doubt remains whether the impurity was on that edge. Since certainty is not removed by doubt, the garment is considered pure.
This is a direct application of 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك'.
3
Analyze the analogy from Siyar
The author draws a parallel from al-Siyar al-Kabir: a conquered fort contains a dhimmi whose identity is unknown. Killing all is haram due to certainty of the dhimmi's presence. If some are killed or removed, doubt about the dhimmi remains, so killing the rest becomes permissible. Similarly, washing one edge creates doubt about impurity removal, so the original purity prevails.
This is a qiyas across different chapters (Tahara and Siyar) using the same underlying maxim.
4
Note the exception when impurity is later discovered
al-Khulasa states: if after praying with the garment, impurity appears on a different edge, repetition of prayers is wajib. Reason: certainty of impurity on that edge returns, which overrides the previous doubt.
This istithnā' demonstrates that the maxim applies only as long as doubt remains; once certainty returns, the ruling reverses.
5
Evaluate the commentator's critique
The commentator finds the reasoning problematic: before washing, there was certainty of impurity. Washing one edge creates doubt about removal, but doubt cannot remove prior certainty. He prefers the precaution of washing the whole garment (from al-Zahiriyya). This is an internal Hanafi debate.
The mufta bihi remains the original position (washing one edge) as per al-Hidayah, but the critique is noted for advanced study.

الْمُصَابِ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِتَنَجَسِ التَّوبِ قِبْلَ: الْوَاجِبُ غَسْلُ طَرْفِ مِنْهُ فَإِنْ غَسَلَهُ بِتَحَرُ اوْ بِلَا تَحَرِّ طَهُرَ . وَذِكْرُ الْوَجْهِ يُبَيِّنُ أَنْ لَا أَثْرَ لِلتَّحَرِّى وَهُوَ أَنْ يُغْسِلَ بَعْضَهُ مَعَ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ طَهَارَةُ الثَّوْبِ وَقَعَ الشَّكُ فِي قِيَامِ النِّجَاسَةِ لِإِحْتِمَالِ كَوْنِ الْمَغْسُوْلِ مَحَلَّهَا فَلَا يُقْضَى بِالنَّجَاسَةِ بِالشَّكَ كَذَا أَوْرَدَهُ الإِسْتيْجَانِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ الجَامِعِ الكَبِيرِ
ترجمہ: اور فتح القدیر کے باب الانجاس میں وہ مسئلہ ہے جس سے اس کی وضاحت ہوتی ہے تو ہم اس کی پوری عبارت پیش کرتے ہیں صاحب ہدایہ کا قول تظہیر النجاسۃ واجب ( نجاست سے پاک کرنا واجب ہے) یہ امکان کی قید کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور جب کوئی نجاست لگنے کی خاص جگہ کے مخفی ہونے کی وجہ سے اسے زائل نہ کر سکتا ہو حالانکہ کپڑے کا نا پاک ہونا معلوم ہو تو کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کے کسی ایک کنارے کا دھونا واجب ہے لہذا اگر اس نے تحری کر کے یا بغیر تحری کے اسے دھویا تو وہ پاک ہو گیا اور کوئی کنارہ دھو دینے سے کپڑے کے پاک ہو جانے کی وجہ کا ذکر کرنا اس بات کا پتہ دیتا ہے کہ تحری کا اس میں کوئی اثر نہیں ہے اور وہ ( وجہ ) یہ ہے کہ اس کے بعض حصہ کو دھو تا با وجود اس کے کہ کپڑے کی پاکی اصل ہے نجاست کے باقی رہنے میں شک پیدا کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ دھلے ہوئے حصہ میں احتمال ہے کہ وہی اس (نجاست ) کی جگہ ہو تو شک کی وجہ سے نجاست کا فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا علامہ اسمیجائی نے شرح الجامع الکبیر میں بیان فرماتے ہوئے اس طرح بیان کیا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ قاعدہ کی وضاحت کے لئے اس مسئلہ کے متعلق فتح القدیر کی کئی عبارتیں پیش فرمائی ہے چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں نجاست کو پاک کرن حتی الامکان واجب ہے لیکن اگر کسی ایک شخص کو کپڑے کا ناپاک ہونا یقینی ہے لیکن جس جگہ نجاست لگی ہے اس کا خصوصی طور پر علم نہیں ہے کہ کہاں ہے لہذا وہ شخص اس طرح نجاست کو زائل کس طرح کرے تو ایسی صورت میں بعض فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک کنارہ کو دھونا کافی ہے اگر اس کے کنارے کو تحری کے ساتھ یا بغیر تحری کے دھولیا تو ایسی صورت میں کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا اور اس صورت میں طرف ثوب کو دھونے کے بعد طہار ثوب کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصل چیز کپڑے کا پاک ہونا ہے ایک کنارے کو دھونے کے بعد طہارت یا عدم طہارت کے بارے میں شک ہے کہ بقیہ کپڑے میں نجاست باقی ہے یا نہیں لہذا محض شک کی وجہ سے طہارت زائل نہ ہوگی اس لئے اس کپڑے کو پاک ہی کہا جائے گا اور اس میں نماز درست ہو جائے گی البتہ اگر بعد میں یقین کے ساتھ معلوم ہو گیا کہ نا پا کی دھوئے گئے کنارہ کے علاوہ میں تھی تو چونکہ نا پاکی کا یقین ہو گیا اس لئے اس کپڑے میں پڑھی گئی تمام نمازوں کا اعادہ واجب ہوگا علامہ اسیجائی نے شرح الجامع الکبیر میں اسی طرح بیان کیا ہے۔
✩✩✩
قَالَ : وَسَمِعْتُ الْإِمَامَ تَاجَ الدِّيْنِ أَحْمَدَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ يَقُوْلُهُ وَيَقِيْسُهُ عَلَى مَسْأَلَةٍ فِي السِّيرِ الكَبيرِ هِيَ إِذَا فَتَحْنَا حِصْنَا وَ فِيهِمْ ذِمّى لَا يُعْرَفْ لَا يَجُوْزُ قَتْلُهُمْ لِقِيَامِ الْمَانِعِ بِيَقِيْنِ فَلَوْ قُتِلَ الْبَعْضُ أَوْ أَخْرِجَ حَلَّ قَتْلُ الْبَاقِي لِلشَّكَ فِي قِيَامِ الْمُحْرِمِ كَذَا هُنَا. 
ترجمه: وہ فرماتے ہیں اور میں نے امام تاج الدین احمد بن عبد العزیز کو یہ مسئلہ بیان فرماتے ہوئے سنا ہے اور وہ اسے السیر الکبیر کے ایک مسئلہ پر قیاس کرتے تھے وہ یہ کہ جب ہم کوئی قلع فتح کریں اور اس میں کوئی غیر معروف ڈمی بھی ہو تو بالیقین مانع کے ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کا قتل جائز نہیں ہے ہاں اگر بعض کو قتل کر دیا گیا یا نکال دیا گیا تو محرم کے موجود ہونے میں شک کی وجہ سے باقی کا قتل کر دینا حلال ہوگا تو ایسا ہی یہاں پر ہے۔ 
تشریح : امام تاج الدین احمد بن عبد العزیز نے فرمایا کہ جب ہم کسی قلعہ کو فتح کریں اور ان میں ڈمی ہو لیکن معلوم نہ ہو کہ کون ہے تو ایسی صورت میں ان تمام اہل قلعہ کا قتل عام جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ذمی کا قتل جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اس کا موجود ہونا یقین میں مانع ہے اور اگر کسی ایک کو قتل کر دیا گیا یا کوئی ایک بھاگ گیا تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ جو امی تھا وہی مقتول یا مغرور ہو اب مانع قتل ( ذمی) کے موجود رہنے میں شک ہوا اور اور پہلے سے قبل بالیقین درست ہے اس لئے مائع کے شک کی وجہ سے قتل نا جائز نہ ہوگا بلکہ اب قتل درست ہو جائے گا۔
وَفِي الْخُلَاصَةِ بَعْدَ مَا ذَكَرَهُ مُجَرَّداً عَنِ التَّعْلِيلِ فَلَوْ صَلَّى مَعَهُ صَلوةٌ ثُمَّ ظَهَرَتِ النِّجَاسَةُ فِي طَرْفِ اخَرَ تَجِبُ إعَادَةُ مَاصَلى إنتهى . وَفِي الظَّهِيْرِيَّةِ ثَوْبٌ فِيْهِ نِجَاسَةٌ لَا يُدْرَى مَكَانُهَا يُعْسَلُ القوبُ كُلُّه إنتهى وَهُوَ الاحْتِيَاطُ وَذَلِكَ التَّعْلِيلُ مُشْكِلٌ عِنْدِي فَإِنَّ غَسْلَ طَرْفِ يُوْجِبُ الشَّكَ فِي طُهْرِ الثَّوْبِ بَعْدَ الْيَقِيْنِ بِنِجَاسَتِهِ قَبْلُ وَحَاصِلُهُ إِنْ شَكٍّ فِي الْإِزَالَةِ بَعْدَ تَيَقُنِ قِيَامِ النِّجَاسَةِ وَالشَّكُ لَا يَرْفَعُ الْمُتَيَقَّنَ قَبْلَهُ. 
ترجمہ: اور خلاصہ میں اس مسئلہ کو بغیر علت کے ذکر کرنے کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اس میں نماز پڑھ لی پھر دوسرے کنارہ میں نجاست ظاہر ہوئی تو پڑھی ہوئی نمازوں کا اعادہ واجب ہے خلاصہ کی بات پوری ہوئی اور ظہیر یہ میں ہے کہ کسی کپڑے میں نجاست لگی ہوئی ہو اور اس کی جگہ معلوم نہ ہو تو پورا کپڑا دھویا جائے گا ظہیر یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا اور یہ احتیاط ہے اور میرے نزدیک وہ علت محل نظر ہے اس لئے کہ کسی ایک کنارہ کا دھودینا پہلے سے لگی نجاست کے یقین کے بعد اس کپڑے کی پاکی میں شک کو پیدا کرتا ہے اور اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قیام نجاست کے یقین کے بعد اس کے زائل ہونے میں شک ہوا ہے اور شک اپنے سے پہلے یقین کو زائل نہیں کرتا ۔ تشریح سابقہ مسلہ کو بلا تعلیل ذکر کرنے کے بعد صاحب خلاصہ نے یہ مسئلہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ ایک شخص نے سابقہ مسئلہ کے حکم کے مطابق کپڑے کے ایک کنارے کو پاک کر کے نماز پڑھ لی پھر نماز پڑھنے کے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ جس کنارو
The issue with knowledge of the impurity of the garment before: the obligatory is to wash one edge of it. If he washes it with scrutiny or without scrutiny, it becomes pure. Mentioning the reason shows that scrutiny has no effect; it is that he washes some part while the original is the purity of the garment, doubt arises about the existence of impurity because of the possibility that the washed part is its location, so impurity is not judged due to doubt. Thus al-Istijani narrated it in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir... [continues with Urdu translations]
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a legal discussion applying the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (certainty is not removed by doubt). The issue: a person knows his garment is impure but does not know the exact location of the impurity. According to some jurists, it is obligatory to wash one edge of the garment. After washing that edge, the garment is considered pure because the original presumption is purity, and doubt about impurity remaining does not override that certainty. The author explains that this ruling is based on the principle that doubt does not remove certainty. He then mentions a parallel case from al-Siyar al-Kabir: when conquering a fort that contains a dhimmi (non-Muslim under protection) whose identity is unknown, it is not permissible to kill all inhabitants because of the certainty that a dhimmi is present. However, if some are killed or removed, then killing the rest becomes permissible due to doubt about the continued existence of the dhimmi. Finally, the commentator notes that in al-Khulasa, the ruling is stated without reasoning, adding that if someone prayed with the garment and later impurity appears on another part, he must repeat all prayers. In al-Zahiriyya, it says the entire garment must be washed as a precaution. The commentator then criticizes the reasoning of washing only one edge, arguing that since there was prior certainty of impurity, washing one edge creates doubt about removal, and doubt cannot remove prior certainty, so the whole garment should be washed.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Scrutiny or trying one's best to locate the impurity before washing
الطرف (al-tarf): An edge or side of the garment
المانع (al-mani'): A preventer of permissibility; here, the presence of a dhimmi prevents killing all inhabitants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling presented in this passage, what is required if a person knows his garment is impure but does not know the exact location of the impurity?
A) He must wash the entire garment.
B) He must wash one edge of the garment, and it becomes pure.
C) He must perform taharrī to find the impurity and wash that spot.
D) He cannot pray in that garment until the impurity is discovered.

Key Takeaway
Certainty of purity is not removed by doubt about impurity removal; washing one edge of an impure garment with unknown spot suffices for purification.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Applying 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt' to Tayammum and Wudu Cases
Additional furuat from Khizanah and Bazzaziyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-yaqin la yuzalu bi al-shakk' to resolve cases of doubt in tayammum, wudu, and post-wudu moisture, and distinguish when a legal stratagem (hila) is permissible.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails: tayammum over doubt, missed limb rule, and sprinkling water only when doubt is chronic.

This lesson expands the application of the foundational maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك) to practical scenarios from the Hanafi works Al-Khizanah al-Akmal and Al-Bazzaziyyah. These rulings guide the mufti in taharah when doubt arises about tayammum, wudu completeness, or post-wudu moisture. Understanding these applications equips you to issue fatwas in cases of waswasah and chronic doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the certainty and the doubt
For each case, determine what is certain (yaqin) and what is doubtful (shakk). The certain state is the starting point.
Certainty can be about tayammum, hadath, or the sequence of events.
2
Apply the maxim
The certain state persists until the doubt is resolved by evidence. This is istishab (presumption of continuity).
Example: certainty of tayammum overrides doubt of hadath.
3
Distinguish rare vs frequent doubt
When post-wudu moisture is rare (first time or occasional), the doubt is treated as significant: wash and repeat wudu. When frequent and uncertain in nature, the doubt is ignored to avoid hardship.
This distinction prevents fall into waswasah.
4
Recognize the limit of the legal stratagem
The sprinkling water hila only works when the moisture is frequent and its nature unknown. If a long time has passed since wudu or if one is certain it is urine, no stratagem benefits; full purification is required.
The hila is a concession, not a loophole.
5
Synthesize the pattern
All these rulings implement the same principle: certainty is preserved unless overcome by stronger certainty or specific evidence. The maxim operates contextually based on frequency and knowledge.
The pattern shows how Hanafi fiqh balances legal principle with practical ease.

الْوُضُوْءِ وَلَوْتَيَقَّنَ الطَّهَارَةَ وَالْحَدَثَتْ وَشَكٍّ فِي السَّابِقِ فَهُوَ مُتَطَهَّرٌ وَفِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَغْسِلْ عُضْوا لَكِنَّهُ لَا يَعْلَمُ بِعَيْنِهِ غَسَلَ يَلْتَفِتُ إِلَيْهِ وَيَنْضِحُ فَرْجَهُ وَإِزَارَهُ بِالْمَاءِ قَطْعًا لِلْوَسْوَسَةِ وَإِذَا بَعْدَ عَهْدُهُ عَنِ الْوُضُوْءِ أَوْعَلِمَ أَنَّهُ بَوْلٌ لَا تَنْفَعَهُ الْحِيْلَةُ إنْتَهى. ترجمه : اور خزانہ الامل میں ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کو تیم کا یقین ہو اور حدث میں شک ہوتو وہ اپنے تیم پر باقی ہے اور ایسے ہی اگر اسے حدث کا یقین ہو اور تیم میں شک ہو تو یقین کو اختیار کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ وضو میں نے اور ا کر کسی کو طہارت وحدت (دونوں) کا یقین ہو اور سابق میں شک ہو تو وہ منتظہر و با وضو ہے اور بزاز یہ میں ہے کہ کی کو معلوم ہے کہ اس نے کوئی ایک عضو نہیں دھو یا لیکن وہ متعین طور پر معلوم نہیں تو وہ اپنے بائیں ہی کو دھوئے لئے کہ وہ آخر عمل ہے۔ کسی نے وضو کے بعد اپنے عضو مخصوص سے ترادث بہتی ہوئی دیکھی تو وہ وضو ٹالے اور اگر یہ صورت اے بار پیش آتی ہو اور یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ وہ پیشاب سے یا پانی کی وجہ سے ہے تو اس طرف توجہ نہ دے اور وسوسہ کو دور کرنے کے لئے اپنی شرمگاہ اور پاجامے پر پانی کے چھینٹے دیدے اور اگر وضو کئے ہوئے کافی وقت گذر گیا یا اسے معلوم ہو کہ وہ پیشاب ہی ہے تو اس کے لئے یہ حیلہ کارآمد نہیں ہے بزازیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ تشریح : خزائتہ الاکل میں ہے کہ اگر کسی شخصکو یقینی طور پر معلوم ہے کہ اس نے تم کیا تھالیکن بعدث ہو یا نہیں تو اس کو تیم قرار دیں گے۔ لو إستيقن بالحدث : ایک شخص کو یہ تو معلوم ہے کہ وہ بے وضو ہے لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ اس نے تیر کا تھا نہیں تو اس کو یقین کی وجہ سے بے وضو قر ار دیں گے۔ ولو تيقن الطهارة و الحدث: ایک شخص کو یقین ہے کہ وہ با وضو ہے اور یہ بھی یقین ہے کہ شرح حموی میں ہے۔ في البزازية: بزازیہ میں ہے کہ ایک شخص کو یقین ہے کہ اس نے ایک عضو ہو تا ترک کر دیا ہے لیکن ان کو بالیقین معلوم نہیں کہ کونسا عضو نہیں دھویا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنا بایاں پیر دھولے اس بنا پر کہو آخری عمل ہے ۔ رأی البسلة : ایک شخص نے وضو کیا اور وضو کے بعد اس کو محسوس ہوا کہ شرمگاہ سے تری نکل رہی ہے تو ہیں میرے میں اس پر ضروری ہے کہ وہ ترکی کو دھولے اور وضو کا استنجاء بہت پہلے کیا ہے یا اس کو یقین ہے کہ وہ ترکی پیشاب تنی ہے ذکر سے نکلی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں کوئی حیلہ مفید نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس پر پیشاب دھو کر وضو کر تالا زم ہوگا۔
And in Al-Khizanah al-Akmal: If one is certain of tayammum and doubts hadath, he remains on his tayammum. Similarly, if he is certain of hadath and doubts tayammum, certainty is taken, as in wudu. And if one is certain of both purity and hadath and doubts which came first, he is pure. And in Al-Bazzaziyyah: If he knows he did not wash one limb but does not know which, he washes his left foot because it is the last action. He saw moisture after wudu flowing from his penis; he repeats. And if it happens frequently and he does not know whether it is urine or water, he pays no attention and sprinkles water on his private part and garment to cut off waswasah. And if a long time has passed since his wudu or he knows it is urine, the stratagem does not benefit him. End. Translation: And in Khizanah al-Akmal: If a person is certain of tayammum and doubts hadath, he remains on his tayammum. Similarly, if he is certain of hadath and doubts tayammum, certainty is adopted, as in wudu. And if one is certain of both purity and hadath and doubts which is earlier, he is pure and with wudu. And in Bazzaziyyah: If one knows he did not wash one limb but does not know which, he washes his left foot because it is the last action. Someone after wudu saw moisture flowing from his private part; he renews wudu. And if this happens frequently and he does not know whether it is urine or water, he does not pay attention and sprinkles water on his private part and garment to remove waswasah. And if a long time has passed since wudu or he knows it is urine, this stratagem is not useful. The text from Bazzaziyyah ends. Commentary: In Khizanah al-Akmal: If a person knows with certainty that he performed tayammum but doubts whether hadath occurred, he is considered in the state of tayammum. If he is certain of hadath: a person knows he is without wudu but does not know whether he performed tayammum, he is declared without wudu due to certainty. And if he is certain of both purity and hadath: a person is certain he has wudu and also certain that hadath occurred, but does not know whether wudu came first or hadath came first and wudu later, then in such a case he is considered pure. However, Allamah Jamui has detailed this issue in Sharh Hamawi. In Al-Bazzaziyyah: A person is certain that he omitted one limb but does not know with certainty which limb he did not wash, then the ruling is that he washes his left foot on the basis that it is the last action. He saw moisture: A person performed wudu and after wudu felt moisture coming out of his private part, then in this case it is necessary for him to wash that moisture and repeat wudu. This is the case when it happens occasionally. And if it happens frequently: A person often feels moisture on his private part but is not sure whether it is urine or water from istinja, then in such a case the ruling is that he should not pay attention to it and should sprinkle water on his private part and garment to eliminate waswasah. This is as narrated in hadith. And if a long time has passed: A person performed wudu or istinja long ago, or he is certain that the moisture is urine coming from the penis, then in such a case no stratagem will be useful; rather, he must wash the urine and perform wudu.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage continues the application of the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' with additional rulings from Al-Khizanah al-Akmal and Al-Bazzaziyyah. From Khizanah: (1) Certainty of tayammum overrides doubt of hadath. (2) Certainty of hadath overrides doubt of tayammum. (3) If certainty of both purity and impurity exist but sequence is unknown, purity prevails (istishab). From Bazzaziyyah: (4) If one knows he missed a limb but not which, he washes the left foot because it is the last obligatory limb. (5) If after wudu one sees moisture but is uncertain, if it is the first time or rare, he must wash and repeat wudu. (6) If it happens frequently, he ignores it and sprinkles water to counter waswasah, based on a hadith. (7) If a long time has passed after wudu or he is sure it is urine, the sprinkling trick does not work; he must purify properly. These rulings show how the maxim is applied differently based on frequency, certainty, and practical ease.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-ḥīlah): A legal stratagem; here, sprinkling water to avoid repeating wudu in case of frequent doubt.
الوسوسة (al-waswasah): Whisperings of Shaytan causing irrational doubt; here, addressed by sprinkling water to dismiss it.
الاستصحاب (al-istiṣḥāb): Presumption of continuity; the certain state remains until proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if after wudu he frequently sees moisture but is unsure if it is urine or water?
A) He must repeat wudu every time.
B) He should ignore it and sprinkle water on his private part and garment.
C) He should assume it is urine and repeat wudu.
D) He should perform tayammum instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' is applied contextually: it preserves the certain state unless the doubt is infrequent or certain to be a nullifier; the legal stratagem of sprinkling water is only for frequent, uncertain moisture to combat waswasah.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Applying the Maxim of Certainty to Doubts in Purity
Application of the maxim to six furuat in taharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' to six distinct scenarios of doubt in taharah, identify the ruling for each, and explain the role of frequency in determining the operative ruling for fatwa.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails over doubt in purity; frequent doubt is ignored, rare doubt requires precaution.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a series of practical scenarios where a person is uncertain about their state of purity. The Hanafi jurists apply the foundational maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك) to determine the ruling. Understanding these applications is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas on common purity-related doubts, especially those involving waswasah (whisperings).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core doubt
For each case in the passage, identify what the person is certain of and what they doubt. The ruling hinges on which state is established with certainty.
Certainty (yaqeen) is given precedence over doubt (shakk) in all cases.
2
Apply the maxim
Decide whether the doubt can override the certainty. The maxim dictates that the certain state remains unless overridden by another certainty.
The only exception is when the doubt is frequent and causes waswasah – then a different rule applies.
3
Distinguish rare vs. frequent occurrence
Note whether the doubt (e.g., moisture) is rare or frequent. Rare occurrence requires repeating wudu; frequent doubt is ignored and a stratagem (hilah) is prescribed to counter waswasah.
This distinction is crucial for the mufti to determine the correct fatwa.
4
Determine the operative ruling for fatwa
Based on the maxim and the frequency, state the ruling: either wudu is required, or it is not, and whether a hilah applies.
The passage cites al-Bazzaziyyah and other sources; these are relied upon in later fatwa collections.

شخص کو اکثر یہ محسوس ہوتا ہے کہ شرمگاہ پر تری ہے لیکن اس کو یقین نہیں ہے ؟ وہ پیشاب ہے یا استنجے کا پانی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں اس کے لئے یہ حکم ہے کہ اس کی طرف التفات نہ کرے اور اپنی شرمگاہ پر اور پائجامہ پر تصنیف میں مار دے تا کہ وسوسہ ختم ہو جائے ۔ هكذا ورد في الحديث و إذا بعد عهد : ایک شخص نے وضو یا استنجاء بہت پہلے کیا ہے یا اس کو یقین ہے کہ وہ ترکی پیشاب تنی ہے ذکر سے نکلی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں کوئی حیلہ مفید نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس پر پیشاب دھو کر وضو کر تالا زم ہوگا۔
And similarly, if one is certain of hadath and doubts tayammum, certainty is taken as in wudu. And if one is certain of both taharah and hadath and doubts the precedence, he is considered pure and with wudu. In al-Bazzaziyyah: if one knows he omitted washing one limb but does not know which specifically, he washes his left foot because it is the last act. Someone after wudu sees moisture dripping from his private part, then he must repeat wudu. If this happens rarely and it is not known whether it is urine or water, he should not pay attention and should sprinkle water on his private part and trousers to remove waswasah. If a long time has passed since wudu or he knows it is urine, then this stratagem is not effective. Al-Bazzaziyyah's statement is complete. Explanation: In Khazanat al-Akmal: if a person knows with certainty that he performed tayammum but doubts whether hadath occurred or not, we will consider him in a state of tayammum. Lou Istaqana bil-Hadath: a person knows he is without wudu but does not know if he performed tayammum, then due to certainty he is considered without wudu. Wa law tayaqqana al-taharah wa al-hadath: a person is certain he has wudu and also certain that hadath occurred, but does not know which came first, then he is considered pure, though Allamah Jamooi has details in Sharh Hamawi. Fi al-Bazzaziyyah: a person is certain he omitted washing one limb but does not know which, so he washes his left foot because it is the last act. Ra'ya al-baslah: a person performed wudu and after wudu felt moisture exiting from the private part, then it is necessary for him to wash that moisture and repeat wudu, this is when it happens rarely. Wa in kana ya'ruduhu kathiran: if a person frequently feels moisture on his private part but is not sure if it is urine or water from istinja, then he should not pay attention and should sprinkle water on his private part and trousers to remove waswasah. Thus it is in the hadith. Wa idha ba'ada 'ahd: if a person performed wudu or istinja a long time ago or he is certain that the moisture is urine from the penis, then no stratagem will be useful, rather he must wash the urine and perform wudu.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage illustrates the Hanafi application of the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' to various scenarios in taharah. The author lists multiple cases: when doubt arises about the order of purity and impurity, the original state of purity is presumed; if uncertain about which limb was missed, the last act is repeated; for waswasah from frequent moisture, the Sharīʿah prescribes a stratagem of sprinkling water to dispel doubt. The ruling hinges on whether the occurrence is rare or frequent. The passage also distinguishes between situations where the doubt is about the existence of impurity vs. the order of events. The principle is that certainty (yaqeen) is given precedence over doubt (shakk).

Key Terms
يقين (yaqeen): Certainty, the absence of doubt; in this text it refers to established knowledge without contrary evidence.
شك (shakk): Doubt, equal possibility of two states; here it refers to uncertainty about the occurrence of purity or impurity.
حدث (hadath): State of ritual impurity that breaks wudu (minor hadath) or requires ghusl (major hadath). Here refers to minor hadath.
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity, either from hadath (wudu/ghusl) or from najasah (impurity). In this passage, it refers to the state of being free from hadath.
حيلة (hilah): A stratagem or permissible legal trick to avoid a ruling without violating the Shari'ah; in this context, sprinkling water to dispel waswasah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person frequently feels moisture after wudu but is unsure whether it is urine or water, what should he do?
A) He must wash the area and repeat wudu every time.
B) He should ignore the moisture and sprinkle water on his private parts to counter waswasah.
C) He must perform ghusl.
D) He should seek medical advice before praying.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' governs all purity rulings, but the frequency of doubt (rare vs. frequent) determines whether wudu is broken or a stratagem is used.

Debt Claim After Proven Payment: Applying the Maxim
Furu' application of the maxim to a debt dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to evaluate a creditor's claim after proven payment in a debt dispute and identify the required specification of timing.

Core Idea
Once payment is proven, the debt is presumed discharged; a new claim must be proven as new.

In this passage, we see a practical furu' (branch) of the major maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt'. The scenario involves a creditor (Zayd) and debtor (Amr) where payment or discharge has already been proven by the debtor. When the creditor later brings a claim for the same amount, the legal presumption works in favor of the debtor. Understanding this application is crucial for a mufti when assessing evidence in financial disputes to prevent double liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original state and ruling
Start by noting that the initial debt of 1,000 is admitted by Amr. Then Amr proves he paid or was discharged. This establishes a new state: the debt is cleared. The ruling is that Amr is free from liability.
The original state (al-asl) is that the debt existed. After proof of payment, the new state (al-asl al-mustashab) is that the debt is discharged.
2
Analyze the creditor's new claim and its evidence
Zayd then presents evidence (bayyinah) that he has 1,000 against Amr. This creates a conflict: is it the same debt or a new one? The evidence does not specify timing, so there is doubt.
3
Apply the maxim اليقين لا يزول بالشك
The certainty (yaqin) is that the debt was discharged. The doubt (shakk) is whether the new claim refers to the same debt or a different one. Certainty cannot be overturned by doubt. Therefore, the creditor's claim is not accepted unless he removes the doubt by specifying that the debt is new (hadithah) after the payment.
The parallel maxim 'الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان' also supports this: the last known state (discharge) continues until proven otherwise.
4
Determine the ruling for the mufti
The mufta bihi ruling is that the creditor's evidence is rejected unless the witnesses explicitly state that the debt arose after the payment or discharge. If they specify that it is a new debt, then the creditor's claim is accepted and the debtor becomes liable again.
This protects the debtor from being sued twice for the same debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ فُرُوعِ ذَلِكَ مَالَوْ كَانَ لِزَيْدِ عَلى عَمْرٍو وَألْفَ مَثَلًا فَبَرْهَنَّ عَمْرُو عَلَى الْأَدَاءِ أَو الإِبْرَاءِ فَبَرْهَنَ زَيْدٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَهُ عَلَيْهِ ألْفًا لَمْ تُقْبَلْ حَتى يُبَرِّهِنَ أَنَّهَا حَادِثَةٌ بَعْدَ الأَدَاءِ أَوِ الإِبْرَاءِ.

ترجمہ: اور اس کی جزئیات میں سے یہ ہے کہ اگر زید کے عمرہ کے ذمہ مثلا ہزار روپے ہوں اور عمرو ادا کئے جانے یا بری کئے جانے پر بینہ پیش کرے اور زید اس پر بینہ پیش کرے کہ اس (زید) کے اس (عمرو) پر ایک ہزار روپے ہیں تو زید کے بینہ قبول نہیں کئے جائیں گے یہاں تک کہ وہ بینہ پیش کر دے کہ یہ ہزار ان ہزار کے ادا کئے جانے یا بری کئے جانے کے بعد کے ہیں۔

تشریح : بقاء ما كان على ماکان والے ضابطہ پر تفریح ہے زید کے عمرو کے ذمہ مثلاً ایک ہزار روپے ہیں اور عمرہ کو ان ایک ہزار کا اقرار بھی ہے البتہ زید کے طلب پر عمر و اس بات پر بینہ پیش کر دیتا ہے کہ اس نے وہ ایک ہررا روپے زید کوادا کر دیئے تھے یا زید نے بری کر دیا تھا تو اس صورت میں عمرو کو بری قرار دیا جائے گا اگر اس کے بعد زید بیہ پیش کرے اور بینہ یہ گواہی دے کہ زید کا عمرو کے ذمہ ایک ہزار روپے ہیں تو صرف اتنی گواہی سے عمرہ کا ذمہ مشغول نہیں ہو گا اس وجہ سے کہ اب یہ احتمال پیدا ہو گیا ہے کہ ان ہی پیسے کا دعوی کر رہا ہے یا ان کے علاوہ کسی اور کا ته اگر زیر کابینہ اس بات کی صراحت کریں کہ عمرہ کے ذمہ زید کے پہلے ایک ہزار کے علاوہ اور ایک ہزار ہیں تو پھر زید کے یہ بینہ جحت قطیہ ہیں اور اب عمر و مشغول الذمہ ہو گا۔
From its branches: if Zayd has a thousand against Amr, for example, and Amr proves payment or discharge, then Zayd proves that he has a thousand against him, it is not accepted until he proves that it is a new debt after the payment or discharge.

Translation: Among its particular applications: if Zayd has, e.g., a thousand rupees owed by Amr, and Amr presents evidence of payment or discharge, and Zayd presents evidence that he (Zayd) has a thousand against him (Amr), then Zayd's evidence is not accepted until he presents evidence that this thousand is subsequent to that payment or discharge.

Explanation: This is a branch of the principle 'what was remains as it was'. Zayd has a thousand rupees on Amr's liability, and Amr acknowledges this thousand. However, upon Zayd's demand, Amr presents evidence that he paid those thousand rupees to Zayd or that Zayd discharged him. In that case, Amr is considered free of liability. If after that Zayd presents evidence and witnesses testify that Zayd has a thousand rupees against Amr, then this testimony alone does not make Amr liable, because now there arises the possibility that he is claiming the same money or something else. If the witnesses explicitly state that Amr owes Zayd another thousand beyond the earlier one, then Zayd's evidence is conclusive and Amr becomes liable.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This is a furu' (branch) of the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt'. Here, the original state is that the debt is discharged once payment or discharge is proven. If the creditor later claims a debt, the presumption is that it is the same debt (since the original state of being debt-free is established). Therefore, the creditor must prove that this debt is a new one arising after the payment, otherwise his claim is not accepted. This protects the debtor from being sued twice for the same debt. The ruling is based on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity).

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence or proof, typically two witnesses; in this context, legal evidence to establish a claim.
دين (dayn): Debt, a financial obligation owed by one person to another.
أداء (ada'): Payment, the act of fulfilling a debt.
إبراء (ibra'): Discharge, the act of the creditor releasing the debtor from liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a debtor proves he paid a debt, and then the creditor presents evidence that the debtor owes him the same amount, what is the ruling?
A) The creditor's evidence is accepted because proof of debt is stronger.
B) The creditor's evidence is not accepted unless he proves the debt is new.
C) The debtor must pay again because the creditor has witnesses.
D) The case is dismissed due to conflicting evidence.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' protects a debtor from being held liable for a debt that may have already been discharged, unless the creditor proves the debt is new.

Applying 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt' to Impurity Cases
Expansion probe of the maxim via two furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to cases of doubt about impurity in water and road mud, and identify the istithna based on frequency of use.

Core Idea
Certainty of purity persists until impurity is known; frequency of contact can shift the default.

This lesson examines a classic application of the major maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to matters of purity. The source text presents two illustrative furuat: a public water tank and road mud. By analyzing these cases, you will see how the Hanafi school balances the presumption of purity with practical realities, and how an exception arises for infrequent users of road mud.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Understand that the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' is one of the five major (kubra) maxims. It establishes that what is certain remains certain until contrary is proven.
This maxim is foundational in Hanafi fiqh, especially in purity (taharah).
2
Identify the asl (default presumption)
In matters of purity, the default is that everything is pure (istishab al-taharah). Doubt about impurity does not negate this asl.
The asl is based on the Quranic principle 'He created for you all that is in the earth' (2:29).
3
Apply to the water tank case
Imam Muhammad's example: children and slaves draw water with dirty hands and jars, yet wudu is permissible until impurity is known. The asl of purity remains despite high probability of contamination.
This shows that mere possibility does not override certainty.
4
Apply to road mud with the exception
For a frequent walker, road mud is pure due to hardship (mashaqqa) of constant checking. For an occasional walker, it remains impure because no hardship exists, so the default (that road mud is often contaminated) applies.
This introduces the complementary maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir'.
5
Synthesize: the role of frequency and hardship
The maxim is not absolute; it is restricted when hardship arises. A mufti must balance the principles: apply the kubra maxim first, then check if another maxim (like mashaqqa) creates an exception.
This synthesis is crucial for fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَشَكَ فِي وجُوْدِ النَّجِسِ فَالأَصْلُ بَقَاءُ الطَّهَارَةِ وَلِذَا قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ حَوْضٌ تَعْلَا مِنْهُ الصَّغَارُ وَالْعَبِيدُ بِالأَيْدِى الدَّنِسَةِ وَالْجِرَارِ الْوَسِخَةِ يَجُوْزُ الْوُضُوْءُ مِنْهُ مَالَمْ يُعْلَمُ بِهِ نِجَاسَةٌ وَلِذَا افْتَوْا بِطَهَارَةِ طِيْنِ الطَّرُقَاتِ.

ترجمہ: اگر کسی کو نجاست کے پائے جانے میں شک ہوا تو اصل طہارت کا باقی رہنا ہے اس لئے امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ کوئی خوشی ہے جس میں سے چھوٹے بچے اور غلام میلے کچیلے ہاتھوں اور گندے مشکوں سے پانی بھرتے ہیں تو اس سے وضو جائز ہے جب تک کہ اس میں نجاست کا علم نہ ہو اسی لئے فقہاء نے راستوں کی کیچڑ کے پاک ہونے کا فتوی دیا ہے۔

تشریح : بقاء ما كان على ماکان والے ضابطہ پر تفریح ہے شک فی وجود النجس : اصل اشیاء میں حلت اور پاک ہونا ہے لہذا جہاں کہیں شک ہو جائے تو اس شک کی وجہ سے اس شئے کو استعمال سے نہیں روکا جائے گا اور وہ شئے پاک ہوگی۔ اسی وجہ سے امام محمد نے فرمایا کوئی حوض یا کنواں ایسا ہے جس پر ہر طرح کے لوگ آتے ہیں اچھے برے، بچے غلام اور گندے وغیرہ تو جب تک یہ نہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس میں ناپاکی گرمی ہوئی ہے اس وقت تک اس کے پانی کے استعمال سے گریز نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ولو افتوا بطهارة: راستہ کے کیچڑ کو فقہاء نے اس شخص کے حق میں پاک کہا ہے جو راستہ میں اکثر چلتا پھرتا ہے اور اگر کبھی کبھار جاتا ہے تو راستہ کا کیچڑ اس کے حق میں ناپاک رہے گا۔
If one doubts the existence of impurity, the original state is the continuation of purity. That is why Muhammad said: A tank from which children and slaves draw water with dirty hands and dirty jars, wudu from it is permissible as long as impurity is not known. That is why they gave fatwa of purity of road mud.

Translation: If someone doubts the presence of impurity, the principle is that purity remains. Therefore, Imam Muhammad said: There is a tank from which small children and slaves draw water with dirty hands and dirty jars; wudu from it is permissible as long as impurity is not known. For this reason, the jurists gave a fatwa on the purity of road mud.

Explanation: This is a branch of the principle 'what was remains as it was'. Doubt about the existence of impurity: the original state of things is permissibility and purity. Therefore, wherever there is doubt, that thing is not prevented from use due to that doubt, and it remains pure. For this reason, Imam Muhammad said: There is a tank or well to which all kinds of people come, good and bad, children, slaves, dirty, etc. As long as it is not known that impurity has fallen into it, its water may not be avoided. And they gave fatwa on purity: The jurists declared road mud pure for the person who frequently walks on the road; but if he goes occasionally, the road mud remains impure for him.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage applies the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' to matters of impurity (najasah). The default assumption is that all things are pure (istishab al-taharah). Imam Muhammad's example of the public tank illustrates that even with a high probability of contamination due to dirty hands and vessels, the water remains pure until actual impurity is known. Similarly, road mud is considered pure for those who frequently walk, as the original state is purity and constant exposure would otherwise create hardship. However, for someone who rarely walks, the mud is considered impure because the doubt is stronger? Actually the text indicates that for the frequent walker, the mud is deemed pure due to necessity and the principle, but for the occasional passerby, it remains impure. This is a nuanced application of the maxim, balancing purity presumptions with practical need.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity, ritually unclean substance (e.g., urine, blood, wine). In this passage, it refers to any physical impurity that prevents validity of prayer.
أصل (asl): The original presumption; in this context, the default ruling that things are pure.
طين الطرقات (teen al-turuqat): Mud from roads and pathways, which may be contaminated with impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, for whom is road mud considered pure?
A) All pedestrians.
B) Frequent walkers.
C) Occasional walkers.
D) Only those who perform wudu from it.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' preserves purity in uncertain cases, but is balanced by the maxim of hardship for frequent exposure.
