8 min
Applying 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt' to Fasting and Marital Claims
Applying the qawida 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to fasting doubts and spousal claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to determine rulings in cases of doubt in fasting and the burden of proof in marital disputes.

Core Idea
Certainty overrides doubt: the original state is presumed to continue until a change is proven.

This lesson examines how the great Hanafi maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' governs rulings when doubt arises. Whether you are uncertain about the break of dawn while fasting or disputing financial and marital claims, the same principle applies: the original certain state prevails. We will see its application across multiple fiqh chapters, understanding how the asl (original state) determines both the validity of acts and the burden of proof.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Begin with the Arabic text 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' and its translation 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.' Understand that this means a certain state continues until a change is certain.
This is one of the five major maxims in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the original state (asl) in each scenario
For each furu' (case), determine which state is certain. Examples: for dawn doubt, the asl is that night continues; for sunset doubt, the asl is that day continues; for maintenance claims, the asl is that the debt remains in the husband's liability.
The asl is always the state of certainty that existed before doubt arose.
3
Apply the maxim to resolve doubt
Using the asl, determine the ruling. If doubt does not reach certainty, the asl prevails. For fasting: fast remains valid if doubt about dawn. For marital disputes: the party whose claim aligns with the asl is believed.
Exceptions occur when doubt reaches strong presumption (ghalabah al-dhann).
4
Note exceptions and nuances
If a person has a strong presumption that dawn has broken, then it is better not to eat. If they eat and it later becomes clear, qada is required. Also, in sunset doubt, kaffara is not obligatory due to the remaining possibility.
Imam Abu Hanifa's narration on sinfulness when eyesight is weak, etc.
5
Derive the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
For day-to-day fatwa, the relied-upon position is that the fast is valid if doubt existed, and no kaffara for breaking it in doubt. For marital disputes, the qawl is given to the one whose statement matches the asl.
Tarjih is based on the maxim and later Hanafi authorities like Ibn Nujaym.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے اس لئے کہ اصل رات کا باقی رہنا ہے اور ایسا ہی وقوف میں ہے اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ شک کی صورت میں نہ کھائے اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ شک کی صورت میں کھانے والا گناہ گار ہے جب اس کی نظر کمزور ہو یا چاندنی رات ہو یا آسمان ابر آلود ہو یا وہ ایسی جگہ ہو جہاں طلوع فجر کا پتہ نہ چل سکے اور اگر صبح صادق طلوع ہونے کا غالب گمان ہو تو تھائے ہی نہیں اگر پھر بھی کھا لیا تو اگر بعد میں کچھ واضح نہ ہوا تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس پر قضاء نہیں ہے اور اگر واضح ہوا کہ اس نے اس (طلوع صبح صادق) کے بعد کھایا ہے تو قضاء کرے اور کفارہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر غروب آفتاب میں شک ہو تو کچھ نہ کھائے اس لئے کہ اصل دن کا باقی رہنا ہے پھر اگر اس نے کھالیا اور بعد میں کچھ ظاہر نہ ہوا تو قضاء کرے اور کفارہ کے بارے میں دو روایتیں ہیں اور اس کی پوری تفصیل شرح کے کتاب الصوم میں ہے۔ تشریح رات کا آخری حصہ تھا اور یہ شک تھا کہ صبح صادق ہوئی یا نہیں تو اس کا اس دن کا روزہ درست ہے کیونکہ اصل رات کا باقی رہنا ہے اور صبح صادق کے بارے میں شک ہے اور رات کا ہونا یقینی ہے تو محض شک کی وجہ سے روزہ پر کوئی اثر نہ پڑے گا۔ وكذا في الموقوف: حج کے موقع پر کسی شخص نے وقوف عرفہ میں رات کو جا کر قیام کیا اور رات کا آخری حصہ تھا تو اس کو شک ہو گیا کہ صبح صادق تو نہ ہو گئی ہو تو محض شک کی وجہ سے وقوف باطل نہ ہوگا۔ والأفضل ان لا ياكل: کسی شخص کو صبح صادق کے ہونے یا نہ ہونے میں شک ہو تو ایسی صورت میں نہ کھانا ہی افضل ہے حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے اس صورت میں کھانا برا ہے کی روایت منقول ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں روزہ نہ رہنے کا بھی احتمال ہے اور یہ شک عموماً جب ہوتا ہے جب کسی کی بینائی کمزور ہو کہ اسے صبح صادق کا پتہ ہی نہ چلے یا چاندنی رات ہو یا ابر آلود ہو تو رات اور صبح کا فرق معلوم نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح اگر کوئی ایسی جگہ، مکان ، کمرہ یا ٹرین وغیرہ میں ہو جہاں دن اور رات کا فرق ہی معلوم نہ ہو پاتا ہو بہر حال شک کی صورت میں سحری کھانا خلاف احتیاط ہے۔ و إن غلب على ظنه : کسی شخص کو یہ گمان غالب ہو کہ اس نے سحری کھائی البتہ صبح صادق ہو گئی ہے حالانکہ صبح نہیں ہوئی ہے تو جب کسی کو غالب گمان یہ ہوکہ صبح ہو چکی ہے تو نہ کھانا چاہئے۔ فإن أكل لم يستين له شيء: صبح صادق کا غالب گمان تھا لیکن پھر بھی سحری کھائی لیکن اس کی نظر میں فرق تھا صبح نظر نہیں آئی تو اس پر قضاء لازم ہے کفارہ نہیں ہے اگر چہ مصنف عدم قضاء کے قائل ہیں تو یہ کہا جائے گا کہ یہاں پر ظن سے عند المصنف شک مراد ہے۔ ولو ظهر أنه أكل بعد: اگر کسی نے صبح صادق کے یقینی ہونے کے بعد سحری کھائی تو اس روزہ کی قضاء ضروری ہے کفارہ نہیں ہے۔ ولو شک في الغروب: اگر کسی کو غروب آفتاب میں شک ہو تو کچھ کھائے پیئے نہ اس لئے کہ اصل دن کا باقی رہنا ہے جو کہ یقینی چیز ہے اور غروب میں شک ہے۔ فان اكل و لم يستين له شيء: شک تھا کہ غروب آفتاب نہیں ہوا ہے پھر بھی افطار کر لیا بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ غروب ہوا نہیں تھا تو قضاء لازم ہے اور کفارہ کے متعلق دو روایتیں ہیں (۱) بدائع میں ہے کہ صحیح یہی ہے کہ کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ غروب کا احتمال باقی ہے اور احتمال اور شبہ کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ إِدَّعَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ عَدَمَ وُصُوْلِ النَّفَقَةِ وَالْكِسْوَةِ الْمُقَرَّرَتَيْنِ فِي مُدَّةٍ مَدِيْدَةٍ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ بَقَاءُهُمَا فِي ذِمَّتِهِ كَالْمَدْيُونِ إِذَا ادَّعَى دَفَعَ الدَّيْنِ وَأَنْكَرَ الدَّائِنُ وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَ الزَّوْجَانِ فِي التَّمْكِيْنِ مِنَ الْوَطْءِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ عَدَمُهُ وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَ فِي السُّكُوتِ وَالرَّدْ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ عَدَمُ الرِّضَا وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَا بَعْدَ الْعِدَّةِ فِي الرَّجْعَةِ فِيْهَا فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ عَدَمُ الرَّجْعَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ قَائِمَةً فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ الْإِنْشَاءَ فَيَمْلِكُ الْإِخْبَارَ. ترجمه: عورت نے شوہر کے خلاف نفقہ کا دعویٰ کیا جبکہ وہ لازم تھا اور اس (شوہر) نے نفقہ کے اس (بیوی) کے پاس پہنچ جانے کا دعوی کیا اور اس بیوی نے انکار کیا تو اس (بیوی) کا قول معتبر ہوگا جیسے قرض دینے والا جب قرض وصول ہو جانے کا انکار کرے اگر میاں بیوی کا وطی پر قدرت دینے میں اختلاف ہوا تو قول منکر کا ہوگا کیوں کہ اصل ولی نہ ہونا ہے اگر دونوں کا اختلاف رد اور سکوت میں ہوا تو قول عورت کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل عدم رضاء ہے اگر عدت کے بعد رجعت میں اختلاف ہوا تو قول عورت کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل رجعت نہ ہونا ہے اگر رجعت باقی ہو تو قول شوہر کا ہوگا کیونکہ شوہر رجعت کر سکتا ہے تو رجعت کی خبر کا اختیار بھی رکھتا ہے۔ تشریح کوئی عورت عدت میں بیٹھی تھی اس کی عدت لمبی ہو گئی اس نے شوہر سے متعلق دعوی کیا کہ اس نے مجھے نان و نفقہ نہیں دیا ہے تو اس عورت کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل یقینی چیز عدت کی بقاء ہے۔ كالمديون إذا ادعي: مقروض نے کہا میں نے تجھے تیری رقم دے دی تھی لیکن قرض خواہ کہتا ہے کہ ابھی نہیں دی تو قرض خواہ کی بات مع الیمین معتبر ہوگی۔ ولو إختلف الزوجان : اگر زوجین میں اختلاف ہو جائے کہ نکاح میں اجازت دی تھی انہیں شوہر کہتا ہے کہ اس نے اجازت دی تھی اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ میں نے انکار کر دیا تھا تو اب عورت کی بات مان لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ اصل عدم رضاء ہے جو کہ یقینی ہے۔ ولو إختلفا بعد العدة في الرجعة: عدت گزرنے کے بعد شوہر نے رجعت کا دعوی کیا اور عورت انکار کرتی ہے تو اب عورت کی بات معتبر ہوگی اس لئے کہ اصل عدم نکاح ہے۔ ولو كانت قائمة: اگر عدت نہیں گذری بلکہ عدت باقی ہے اور شوہر دعویٰ کر رہا ہے کہ رجعت ہوگئی اور عورت
Because the original (principle) is that the night remains, and similarly in wuquf. And it is better not to eat in case of doubt. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that the one who eats in case of doubt is sinful when his eyesight is weak or it is a moonlit night or the sky is cloudy or he is in a place where the dawn cannot be discerned. And if he has a prevailing presumption that dawn has broken, then he should not eat. If he eats and nothing becomes clear afterwards, according to Zahir al-Riwayah there is no qada on him. And if it becomes clear that he ate after dawn, then he should make qada and no kaffara. And if there is doubt about sunset, he should not eat anything because the original is that the day remains. Then if he eats and nothing becomes clear afterwards, he should make qada, and there are two narrations about kaffara, and its full detail is in the commentary of the book of Sawm. Explanation: It was the last part of the night and there was doubt whether dawn had broken or not, so his fast for that day is valid because the original is that the night remains and there is doubt about dawn, and the existence of night is certain, so mere doubt does not affect the fast. Similarly for the one standing (in wuquf): during Hajj, a person went to stand at Arafat at night and it was the last part of the night, and he doubted whether dawn had broken, then mere doubt does not invalidate the wuquf. And it is better not to eat: if a person doubts whether dawn has broken or not, then not eating is better. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa says that eating in such a case is disliked, because there is a possibility that the fast may not be valid, and this doubt usually occurs when one's eyesight is weak so he cannot discern dawn, or it is a moonlit night or cloudy, so the difference between night and morning is not known, similarly if he is in a place like a house, room, or train where the difference between day and night cannot be known; in any case, eating sahur in doubt is against precaution. And if he has a prevailing presumption: if a person has a strong presumption that dawn has broken, then he should not eat. If he eats and nothing becomes clear for him: he had a strong presumption of dawn but still ate sahur, but in his vision there was a difference and dawn did not appear, then qada is necessary on him, not kaffara, even though the author holds no qada; it will be said that here by 'dhann' the author means doubt. And if it becomes clear that he ate after: if someone ate sahur after being certain of dawn, then qada of that fast is obligatory, not kaffara. And if doubt about sunset: if someone doubts sunset, he should not eat or drink anything because the original is that the day remains, which is certain, and there is doubt about sunset. If he eats and nothing becomes clear: he doubted that sunset had not occurred but still broke his fast, and later it became clear that sunset had not occurred, then qada is necessary, and there are two narrations regarding kaffara. (1) In Bada'i it is said that the correct view is that kaffara is not obligatory because the possibility of sunset remains, and kaffara is not obligatory due to possibility and doubt. If the woman claims that the maintenance and clothing that were fixed were not delivered to her over a long period, then her statement is accepted because the original is that they remain in his liability, like the debtor who claims payment of the debt and the creditor denies. And if the spouses differ about [the wife's] enabling [the husband] for intercourse, then the statement of the denier is accepted because the original is non-existence. And if they differ about silence and rejection [regarding consent in marriage], then her statement is accepted because the original is lack of consent. And if they differ after the 'iddah about raj'a during it, then her statement is accepted because the original is non-existence of raj'a. And if [the 'iddah] is still ongoing, then his statement is accepted because he has the power to initiate [raj'a], so he has the power to inform about it. Translation: A woman claimed against her husband for maintenance while it was obligatory, and he claimed that the maintenance reached her, and she denied, then her statement is credible, like the creditor when he denies receipt of the debt. If the spouses differ about enabling for intercourse, then the statement of the denier is accepted because the original is non-existence. If they differ about silence and rejection, then her statement is accepted because the original is lack of consent. If they differ after the 'iddah about raj'a, then her statement is accepted because the original is non-existence of raj'a. If the 'iddah is still ongoing, then his statement is accepted because he has the power to initiate [raj'a], so he has the power to inform about it. Explanation: A woman was sitting in 'iddah, her 'iddah became long, she claimed from her husband that he did not give her bread and maintenance, then her statement is credible because the original certain thing is the continuity of 'iddah. Like the debtor when he claims: the debtor said 'I gave you your money' but the creditor says 'you have not given yet', then the creditor's statement with oath is credible. And if the spouses differ: if the spouses differ about permission in marriage, the husband says she gave permission but the wife says she refused, then the woman's statement will be accepted because the original is lack of consent, which is certain. And if they differ after 'iddah about raj'a: after 'iddah passes, the husband claims raj'a and the wife denies, then the woman's statement is accepted because the original is non-existence of marriage. And if it is still ongoing: if 'iddah has not passed but remains, and the husband claims that raj'a occurred and the woman...
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a practical expansion of the fundamental Hanafi qawida: 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt). The author, likely Ibn Nujaym or a commentator on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, demonstrates the maxim's application across multiple chapters of fiqh. The first set of furuat concerns fasting and the Hajj wuquf. The key principle is that the original state (asl) — night continuing, day continuing — is certain, and doubt about a change (dawn, sunset) does not disrupt that certainty. Thus, if one doubts whether dawn has broken, the fast is valid because the night's continuance is certain. Similarly, doubt during wuquf does not invalidate it. However, the author notes a nuance: if one has a strong presumption (ghalabah al-dhann) that dawn has broken, then it is better not to eat, and if he eats and it later becomes clear he ate after dawn, qada is required (though the author seems to distinguish between doubt and strong presumption in Zahir al-Riwayah). For sunset doubt, qada is required if he eats but kaffara is not obligatory due to the remaining possibility. The second set of furuat shifts to marital disputes. Here the same principle governs who bears the burden of proof (al-qawl li-man). In each case, the party whose claim aligns with the original state (asl) — such as the wife's claim that maintenance was not paid because the original is its remaining in the husband's liability, or the husband's claim that he enabled intercourse because the original is non-existence of tamkin? Actually careful: the text says for tamkin, the denier (i.e., the one who denies enabling, presumably the wife) is believed because the original is non-existence. So the maxim dictates that the person whose assertion aligns with the asl (the certain state) is given precedence, often with an oath. This illustrates that the qawida is not just about rulings in worship but also about procedural rules in evidence and claims. The passage is a rich source for understanding how Hanafi jurists derive logical consistency across diverse legal scenarios using a single maxim.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): The original, certain state that is presumed to continue until a change is proven (e.g., night continues, day continues, liability remains).
شک (shakk): Doubt that does not rise to certainty; the legal effect is that the certain state (asl) remains unchanged.
قول (qawl): The legal statement (claim) of a party; here, 'al-qawl li-...' means that party's statement is given precedence (with oath) because it aligns with the asl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between spouses where the wife claims she did not enable intercourse and the husband claims she did, whose statement is accepted according to the maxim?
A) The husband's, because he is the one who pays maintenance.
B) The wife's, because she is the one who enables.
C) The denier's, because the original is non-existence of tamkin.
D) Both with evidence, and the judge decides.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' ensures that certainty prevails over doubt, preserving the original state in both acts of worship and legal disputes.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
15 min
Applications of the Maxim 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt'
Applying istishab to disputes in fasting, marriage, and sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to resolve disputes in fasting, marriage, sales, and iddah, identifying when the maxim holds and when exceptions apply.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails over doubt: the burden of proof rests on the one claiming a change from the original certain state.

This lesson examines several fiqh disputes where the Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك) determines the burden of proof. By analyzing cases from fasting, marriage, sales, and iddah, you will see how Hanafi jurists apply this maxim—and where they make exceptions. The goal is to equip you to identify the 'original certain state' (al-asl) in any dispute and correctly assign the burden of proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original certain state (al-asl)
Before applying the maxim, determine what is certain and unchanged. For example, in a fasting dispute, the original state is that the fast was still in effect; in a sales dispute, the original state is permissibility (ibahah) of the transaction.
The 'asl' is the starting point: it is what is known for certain before any claim of change.
2
Determine which party claims a change from the asl
Identify the party whose claim would alter the original state. That party bears the burden of proof. For instance, if the wife claims maintenance is unpaid, she is asserting the asl (debt remains); if the husband claims he paid, he is claiming a change.
The claimant (mudda'i) is the one who asserts a departure from the asl; the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) is the one who affirms the asl.
3
Apply the maxim: preference is given to the party affirming the asl
In the absence of evidence, accept the statement of the party who affirms the original certain state. This is the core of the maxim: doubt does not overturn certainty.
Example: in a dispute over tamkin (submission for intercourse), the denier's word is accepted because the original state is absence of forced submission.
4
Check for exceptions (a) when one party has capacity to initiate (insha') or (b) when both parties present evidence
Exceptions arise when a party has the power to create a new state (e.g., husband's right to raj'ah overrides the asl), or when both parties have proof—in which case the evidence of the one claiming a departure from the apparent state is prioritized.
These exceptions show that the maxim is not absolute; it is tempered by other principles like 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a khilaf al-zahir' (evidence is on the one claiming the contrary of the apparent).
5
Derive the ruling for the specific case
Combine the asl, the parties' positions, and any applicable exceptions to reach the correct fiqh ruling. For example, in a dispute over meat being carrion, the buyer's claim (that it is still forbidden) is accepted because the asl of the animal is prohibition.
The ruling will often determine whose statement is believed and what the consequences are (e.g., qada, kaffarah, maintenance).

باقی رہنا ہے جو کہ یقینی چیز ہے اور غروب میں شک ہے۔
فان اكل و لم يستين له شی: شک تھا کہ غروب آفتاب نہیں ہوا ہے پھر بھی افطار کر لیا بعد میں تہ چلا کہ غروب ہوا نہیں تھا تو قضاء لازم ہے اور کفارہ کے متعلق دو روایتیں ہیں (۱) بدائع میں ہے کہ صحیح یہی ہے کہ کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ غروب کا احتمال باقی ہے اور احتمال اور شبہ کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
إِدَّعَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ عَدَمَ وُصُوْلِ النَّفَقَةِ وَالْكِسْوَةِ الْمُقَرَّرَ تَيْنِ فِي مُدَّةٍ مَدِيْدَةٍ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لَأَنَّ الأصْلَ بَقَاءُ هُمَا فِي ذِمَّتِه كَالْمَدْيُون إِذَا إِدَّعى دَفَعَ الدَّيْنِ وَأَنْكَرَ الدَّائِنُ وَلَوْ إِخْتَلَفَ الزَّوْجَانِ فِى التَّمْكِيْنِ مِنَ الْوَطْىءٍ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ لأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ عَدَمُهُ وَلَوْ إِخْتَلَفَ فِي السُّكُوتِ وَالرَّدْ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُ الرَّضَاءِ وَلَوْ اخْتَلَفَا بَعْدَ الْعِدَّةِ فِي الرَّجْعَةِ فِيْهَا فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لأَنَّ الأصَلَ عَدَمُ الرَّضَاءِ وَلَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا بَعْدَ الْعِدَّةِ فِي الرَّجْعَةِ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهَا وَلَوْ كَانَتْ قَائِمَةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ لأَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ الإِنْشَاءَ فَيَمْلِكُ الإِخْبَارَ. ترجمه: عورت نے شوہر کے خلاف نفقہ کا دعویٰ کیا جبکہ وہ لازم تھا اور اس (شوہر) نے نفقہ کے اس (بیوی) کے پاس پہنچ جانے کا دعوی کیا اور اس بیوی نے انکار کیا تو اس (بیوی) کا قول معتبر ہوگا جیسے قرض دینے والا جب قرض وصول ہو جانے کا انکار کرے اگر میاں بیوی کا وطی پر قدرت دینے میں اختلاف ہوا تو قول منکر کا ہوگا کیوں کہ اصل ولی نہ ہونا ہے اگر دونوں کا اختلاف ردا اور سکوت میں ہوا تو قول عورت کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل عدم رضاء ہے اگر عدت کے بعد رجعت میں اختلاف ہوا تو قول عورت کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل رجعت نہ ہوتا ہے اگر رجعت باقی ہو تو قول شوہر کا ہوگا کیونکہ شوہر رجعت کر سکتا ہے تو رجعت کی خبر کا اختیار بھی رکھتا ہے۔ تشریح کوئی عورت عدت میں بیٹھی تھی اس کی عدت لمبی ہو گئی اس نے شوہر سے متعلق دعوی کیا کہ اس نے مجھے نان و نفقہ نہیں دیا ہے تو اس عورت کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل یقینی چیز عدت کی بقاء ہے۔ كالمديون إذا ادعي: مقروض نے کہا میں نے تجھے تیری رقم دے دی تھی لیکن قرض خواہ کہتا ہے کہ ابھی نہیں نے کہامیں نے تھے تیری میری ہی تھی میں قرض کہا دیئے تو قرض خواہ کی بات مع الیمین معتبر ہوگی۔ ولو إختلف الزوجین : اگر زوجین میں اختلاف ہو جائے کہ نکاح میں اجازت دی تھی انہیں شو ہر کہتا ہے کہ و نے اجازت دی تھی اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ میں نے انکار کر دیا تھا تو اب عورت کی بات مان لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ افضل عدم رضاء ہے جو کہ یقینی ہے۔ ولو إختلفا بعد العدة في الرجعة: عدت گزرنے کے بعد شوہر نے رجعت کا دعوی کیا اور عورت انکار کرتی ہے تو اب عورت کی بات معتبر ہوگی اس لئے کہ اصل عدم نکاح ہے۔ ولو كانت قائمة: اگر عدت نہیں گذری بلکہ عدت باقی ہے اور شو ہر دعویٰ کر رہا ہے کہ رجعت ہوگئی اور عورت انکار کر رہی ہے تو شوہر کی بات مان لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ وہ انشاء کا مالک ہے چنانچہ وہ اختیار کا بھی مالک ہے۔ وَلَوْ اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَائِعَانِ فِي الطَّوْعِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمَنْ يَدَّعِيْهِ لأَنَّهُ الأَصْلَ وَ إِنْ بَرْهَنَا فَبَيِّنَةُ مَنْ يُدْعِي الإِكْرَاهُ أوْلى وَ عَلَيْهِ الْفَتَاوى كَمَا فِي الْبَزَّازِّيَّةِ وَلَوْ ادَّعَى الْمُشْتَرِى أَنَّ اللَّحْمَ لَحْمُ مَيْتَةٍ أَوْ ذَبِيحَةُ مَجُوسِى وَ انْكَرَ الْبَائِعُ لَمْ أَرَهُ الآنَ وَمُقْتَضَى قَوْلِهِمْ الْقَوْلُ لِمُدَّعِي البطلان لِكَوْنِهِ مُنْكِراً أَصْلُ الْبَيْعِ أَنْ يُقْبَلَ قَوْلُ الْمُشْتَرِى وَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ الشَّاةَ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهَا مُحَرَّمَةٌ فَالْمُشْتَرِي مُتَمَسْكَ بِاصْلِ التَّحْرِيمِ إِلَىٰ أَنْ يُتَحَقَّقَ زَوَالُهُ. ترجمہ: اور اگر بائع ومشتری کا خوشی سے بیچ میں اختلاف ہوا تو جو رضا ء سے بیچ کا دعویدار ہو قول اس کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل بیچ میں تراضی ہے اگر دونوں نے بیتہ قائم کیا تو جو جبر کا دعویدار ہے تو اس کا بینہ رائج ہو گا قومی اسی پر ہے بزاز یہ میں اسی طرح ہے۔ اگر خریدار نے دعوی کیا گوشت مردار یا مجوسی کا ذبیحہ ہے اور بائع نے انکار کیا تو اسکا حکم نہیں دیکھا اور فقہاء کے قول کا مقتضی بطلان کے دعویدار کا قول معتبر ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل بیع کا منکر ہے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کا قول مانا جائے اور اس اعتبار سے کہ بکری اپنی زندگی میں حرام مشتری اصل تحریم سے استدلال کر رہا ہے یہاں تک کہ تحریم کا زوال محقق ہو جائے۔ تشریح : بائع اور مشتری کے مابین رضا اور عدم رضاء پر اختلاف ہوا تو ایسی صورت میں اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی جو رضا مندی کا دعوی کر رہا ہے کیونکہ یہی چیز اصل ہے اور اگر دونوں نے بہینہ قائم کر دیا تو اس شخص کا بینہ مقبول ہوگا جو اگر او اور عدم رضاء کا دعوی کر رہا ہے اس پر فتویٰ ہے کیونکہ بینہ خلاف ظاہر چیز پر پیش کیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں اکراہ خلاف ظاہر ہے اور خلاف اصل ہے۔ ولو إدعى المشتری: مشتری نے دعوی کیا کہ خریدا ہوا گوشت مردار کا گوشت ہے یا مجوسی کا ذبیحہ ہے اور بائع اس کا انکار کر رہا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں فقہاء کے قول کے مطابق بطلان کے مدعی کی بات مانی جائے گی اور اس اعتبار سے بھی مشتری کی بات مانی جائے گی کہ بکری زندگی میں شرعی ذبح سے پہلے حرام ہے کیونکہ اصل بکری میں حرمت ہے جب تک کہ ذبح شرعی سے وہ حرمت نہ زائل ہو جائے تو مشتری گویا کہہ رہا ہے کہ یہ میتہ ہے یا ذبیحہ مجوسی ہے یعنی جو اصل حرمت تھی وہ زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے مشتری اصل حرمت سے استدلال کر رہا ہے کہ اس کا قول اصل کے مطابق ہے اس لئے مشتری کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا۔
ادَّعَتِ الْمُطَلَّقَةُ امْتِدَادَ الطَّهْرِ وَ عَدَمَ إِنْقِضَاءِ الْعِدَّةِ صُدِّقَتْ وَلَهَا التَّفَقَةُ لأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ بَقَائِهَا إِلَّا إِذَا ادْعَتِ الْحَبْلَ فَإِنَّ لَهَا النَّفْقَةَ إِلى سَنَتَيْنِ فَإِنْ مَّضَعًا ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ أَنْ لَا حَبْلَ فَلَا رُجُوعَ عَلَيْهَا كَمَا فِى فتح القَدِيرِ.
Remaining is the certain thing, and there is doubt about sunset. If one ate and it was not clear to him: he doubted that sunset had not occurred, yet he broke his fast; later it became clear that sunset had not occurred, so qada is obligatory. Regarding kaffarah, there are two narrations: (1) In al-Badai', the correct view is that kaffarah is not obligatory, because the possibility of sunset remained, and due to possibility and doubt, kaffarah is not obligatory. If a woman claims non-receipt of maintenance and clothing prescribed for a long period, her statement is accepted because the original state is that they remain a debt upon him, like a debtor who claims payment and the creditor denies. If the spouses dispute about enabling intercourse, the statement of the denier is accepted because the original state is its absence. If they dispute about silence and rejection, her statement is accepted because the original state is absence of consent. If they dispute after the iddah about revocation (raj'ah) within it, her statement is accepted because the original state is absence of consent. If they dispute after the iddah about revocation, her statement is accepted because the original state is its absence. If it (the iddah) is ongoing, his statement is accepted because he has the power of initiation, so he has the power of reporting. Translation: ... [Urdu commentary]. And if the two parties to a sale dispute about voluntariness, the statement of the one claiming it is accepted because it is the original state. If they both provide proof, the evidence of the one claiming coercion is given precedence, and upon it are the fatwas, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. If the buyer claims that the meat is carrion or a Magian's slaughter, and the seller denies, I have not seen it now. The import of their statement that the statement of the claimant of invalidity is accepted because he is a denier of the original sale, requires that the buyer's statement be accepted, and by considering that the sheep in its lifetime is forbidden, so the buyer is clinging to the principle of prohibition until its removal is verified. Translation: ... [Urdu commentary]. A divorced woman who claims continuation of purity and non-completion of the iddah is believed, and she has maintenance because the original state is its continuation, unless she claims pregnancy; then she has maintenance for up to two years. If she suckles, then it becomes clear that there is no pregnancy, there is no recourse upon her, as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a collection of practical applications of the second major maxim of Hanafi fiqh, 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك). The author presents several fiqh disputes where the burden of proof is determined by the 'asl' (original certain state). The first case concerns fasting: if one breaks the fast at sunset mistakenly, qada is obligatory because the original state is that the fast remained; but kaffarah is not imposed due to the doubt about sunset. The second set of cases involves marital disputes: a wife's claim for maintenance during iddah is accepted because the original state is that the debt of maintenance remains; similar reasoning applies to disputes about tamkin (submission for intercourse), where the original state is absence of consent or action. However, an exception occurs when the iddah is ongoing and the husband claims raj'ah: his word is accepted because he has the power to initiate raj'ah, thus his report is trusted. The third set involves sales: in a dispute over whether a sale was voluntary, the one claiming voluntariness is believed; but if both present evidence, the evidence of the one claiming coercion is preferred. In a dispute about meat being carrion or from a Magian slaughter, the buyer's claim is accepted because the original state of the animal is prohibition. Finally, a divorced woman's claim of continued purity and unexpired iddah is accepted, with maintenance, because the original state is that the iddah continues. The passage demonstrates how the maxim operates across chapters of fasting, marriage, and sales, with nuanced exceptions.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The prior certain state that is presumed to continue until proven otherwise.
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, the opposite of doubt, which is not removed by mere probability.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt, a state of uncertainty where neither side is more probable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between spouses over whether the husband performed raj'ah during the iddah period (the iddah is still ongoing), whose statement is accepted and why?
A) The wife's statement, because the original state is no raj'ah.
B) The husband's statement, because he has the power to initiate raj'ah.
C) The wife's statement, because she is the defendant.
D) The husband's statement, because he is the one claiming a change.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' is a foundational tool for burden of proof in Hanafi fiqh, with specific exceptions based on capacity to act and strength of evidence.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Applying Certainty to Doubts in Salah
Applying the maxim of certainty and doubt to specific salah scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to various doubts in salah and state the correct ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails over doubt — until after salah, doubts are generally ignored.

This lesson applies the foundational maxim al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk to specific situations of doubt during prayer. The Hanafi jurists have derived detailed rulings covering doubts about performing a prayer, about the number of rak'ahs, and about forgotten obligations. Understanding these rulings equips the mufti to address common questions about prayer doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of doubt
Categorize the doubt: about the entire prayer, a specific action, or the number of rak'ahs? This determines which rule applies.
2
Assess the timing
Is the doubt during the prayer or after completion? The ruling differs significantly based on timing.
Doubt after completion is generally ignored unless there is certainty of missing a fard.
3
Check frequency
Is this a first-time doubt or a recurrent one (waswās)? Frequent doubts trigger taharrī instead of starting over.
4
Apply the maxim
Return to the original certainty: the obligation remains until performed; missed actions must be repeated if still in prayer; after prayer, validity is presumed.
5
Handle the exception for missed fard
If a fard is known to be missing but not identified, a special corrective procedure is prescribed.
This is not a case of pure doubt but near-certainty of deficiency.

تَكَّ فِي صَلَوَةٍ هَلْ صَلَّاهَا أَمْ لَا أَعَادَ فِي الْوَقْتِ. شَكٍّ فِي رُكُوْعٍ أَوْسُجُوْدٍ وَهُوَ فِيْهَا الْعَادَ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَعْدَهَا فَلَا وَ إِنْ شَكَ أَنَّهُ كَمْ صَلَى فَإِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ إِسْتَأْنَفَ وَ إِنْ كَثُرَ تَحْوَى وَ إِلَّا أَخَذَ بِالأَقَلِّ وَهَذَا إِذَا شَكٍّ فِيْهَا قَبْلَ الْفَرَاغِ وَ إِنْ كَانَ بَعْدَهُ فَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا إِذَا تَذَكَّرَ بَعْدَ الْفَرَاغِ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ فَرْضًا وَ شَكٍّ فِي تَعْيِنِهِ قَالُوْا يَسْجُدُ سَجْدَةً وَاحِدَةً ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ ثُمَّ يَقُوْمُ فَيُصَلِّى رَكْعَةً بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ ثُمَّ يَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيْرِ. ترجمه کسی نماز کے بارے میں شک ہوا کہ وہ نماز پڑھ لی ہے یا نہیں تو اس کے وقت میں اس کو لوٹالے کسی رکوع یا سجد ہ میں شک ہوا حالانکہ وہ اس (نماز) ہی میں ہے تو اس کو لوٹالے اور اگر (شک )اس ( نماز ۹ کے بعد ہو نہ لوٹائے اور اگر شک ہوا کہ اس نے کتنی رکعت پڑھی ہیں تو اگر یہ پہلی مرتبہ ہوا تو از سر نو پڑھ لے اور اگر اکثر ایسا بھی ہو تو تری کرے رونہ پھر کم کو اختیار کرے اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب شک نماز پوری کرنے سے پہلے ہو اور مانیا (نماز) کے بعد ہو تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں الا یہ کہ فارغ ہو جانے کے بعد یاد آجائے کہ کوئی فرض چھوڑا ہے اور اس کی تعین میں شک ہو تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک سجدہ کرے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر کھڑا ہو پھر دوسجدوں کے ساتھ ایک بہت پڑھے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے کذافی فتح القدیر تشریح: ایک شخص کو نماز کے ادا کرنے میں شک ہو گیا کہ ادا کر لی ہے یا نہیں ؟ تو اگر وقت باقی ہے اس نماز کا اعادہ کرے۔ شک فی رکوع أو سجود : ایک شخص کو دورانِ نماز رکوع کے یا سجدہ کے بارے میں شک ہو گیا کہ کیا ہے نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں نماز کے اندر اعادہ کر لے اگر نماز پڑھ چکا ہے تو اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فإن شک انه کم صلی : ایک شخص کو شک ہو گیا کہ اس نے کتنی رکعتیں پڑھی ہیں تو ایسی صورت میں اگر پہلی منہاس کو یہ بات پیش آئی ہے تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھ لے اگر بار بار ایسا ہوتا ہے تو پھر تحری کر کے غالب گمان پر عمل کرے عید کر کسی ایک جانب گمان غالب نہ ہوتا ہو تو اقل کو اختیار کرے اور بقیہ کو پورا کرے یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ جبکہ
If one doubts in a prayer whether he prayed it or not, he repeats it within its time. If he doubts about a ruku' or sujud while he is in it, he repeats it (the action). If he doubts after finishing, he does not repeat. If he doubts how many rak'ahs he prayed, if it is the first time, he starts over; if it happens often, he tries to determine (taharrī) [and acts on his predominant presumption]; otherwise he takes the lesser amount. This is if the doubt occurs before completion. If it occurs after, nothing is required unless after completion he remembers that he left a fard and doubts which one. They said: He performs one sajdah, then sits, then stands, then prays one rak'ah with two sajdahs, then sits, then performs sujud al-sahw. So in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. [Urdu translation and explanation]
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a series of furuat (applications) of the maxim that certainty is not removed by doubt, specifically in the context of salah. The rulings are from Fatḥ al-Qadīr and cover various doubts:

1. Doubt about having performed a prayer: If one doubts whether he has prayed a particular prayer, and the time for it still remains, he must repeat it (because the original obligation is certain, and doubt does not remove it).

2. Doubt about a ruku' or sujud while still in the prayer: If during prayer one doubts whether he performed a ruku' or sujud, he must perform it again (since the certainty of having not done it is stronger). However, if the doubt arises after completing the prayer, he does not repeat it (since the prayer is presumed valid).

3. Doubt about the number of rak'ahs: If it is the first time this happens, he must start the prayer over (because of the principle that the original is not to have performed it). If it happens frequently (waswās), he should make a determination (taharrī) based on his predominant presumption; if no presumption prevails, he takes the minimum (the smaller number) and completes his prayer accordingly. This applies if the doubt occurs before finishing the prayer. After finishing, no action is required.

4. Exception for forgetting a fard: If after completing the prayer he remembers that he left out a fard (obligatory part) but doubts which fard, he performs a specific procedure: one sajdah, then sit, then stand, pray one rak'ah with two sajdahs, then sit again, then perform sujud al-sahw. This is according to Fatḥ al-Qadīr (a Hanafi work).

These rulings all demonstrate the Hanafi application of the maxim: certainty is preserved unless there is stronger certainty to the contrary.

Key Terms
تَحَرِّى (taharrī): Making a determination or judgment based on one's best assessment when in doubt.
سَجْدَة (sajdah): Prostration; in this ruling, a single sajdah is performed as part of the corrective procedure.
سَجْدَةُ السَّهْو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to rectify errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what should a person do if he doubts the number of rak'ahs he has prayed and this is the first time it happens?
A) He should continue building on his predominant presumption
B) He should take the smaller number and complete
C) He should start the prayer over from the beginning
D) He should perform sujud al-sahw and continue

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the validity of a completed prayer unless certainty of omission arises; doubts during the act require immediate correction.

Certainty Prevails Over Doubt: Missed Prayer Obligations
Ruling for person who remembers missing a fard or sajdah after prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to cases of uncertainty in prayer and construct the appropriate remedial actions for a missing fard or sajdah.

Core Idea
When certainty and doubt conflict, certainty prevails; the prayer is not repeated but compensated.

Imagine completing your prayer, then suddenly remembering you missed something—a fard act or a sajdah—but you're not sure which. Should you repeat the whole prayer? The Hanafi school, guided by the foundational maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt), provides a structured remedy that upholds the validity of your prayer while ensuring no deficiency remains. In this lesson, we explore how this maxim translates into a specific sequence of actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
The maxim is 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt). It is one of the five major (kubra) maxims of Hanafi fiqh and applies across all chapters, especially in acts of worship like prayer.
2
Understand the factual scenario
The person has certainty that they completed the prayer (yaqin) but doubt (shakk) about whether they omitted a fard or a sajdah. The maxim dictates that the certainty of prayer completion is not undermined by the doubt.
3
Determine the consequence
Since the prayer is valid, the missing element must be compensated, not by repetition but by a corrective sequence: one sajdah, sitting, one rak'ah, and sajdah sahw. This preserves the original prayer's validity.
4
Apply the maxim to this specific furu'
The maxim guides the ruling: do not break the prayer; instead, add the missing rak'ah and perform sajdah sahw to remedy any deficiency.
5
Note the istithna' (exceptions)
The qawida has exceptions; but in this case, the maxim applies directly without exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفراغ : ایک شخص کو نماز پڑھ لینے کے بعد یاد آیا کہ اس نے نماز کا کوئی فرض مشتار کو ٹ یا سجدہ چھوڑ دیا ہے لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کونسا چھوڑا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں یہ شخص ایک سجدہ کرے پھر قعدہ کرے پھر کھڑا ہو کر ایک پوری رکعت ادا کرے اور آخر میں سجدہ سہو بھی کرے۔
Al-Faragh: A person after having completed prayer remembered that he left out some obligatory (act) or prostration from the prayer, but he does not know which one. In such a case, this person should perform one prostration, then sit, then stand up and perform one full rak'ah, and at the end also perform the prostration of forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding uncertainty after completing a prayer. The person is certain that something was missed but unsure which specific obligatory act or prostration was omitted. The remedy prescribed maintains the integrity of the prayer by adding a prostration, sitting, a complete rak'ah, and the prostration of forgetfulness. This ensures that any deficiency is compensated without breaking the prayer's validity.

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Uncertainty about the occurrence or non-occurrence of an act
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is a pillar; its omission invalidates the prayer
سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration; a pillar of prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Perform one sajdah, sit, then one rak'ah, and sajdah sahw
C) Ignore the doubt
D) Perform only sajdah sahw

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' preserves the validity of prayer when only doubt exists, and a compensatory sequence suffices.

Ruling on Trustworthy Informant After Salam: Applying al-Yaqin la Yazul bi al-Shakk
Ruling when a trustworthy person informs after salam that Zuhr was four rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-yaqin la yazul bi al-shakk' to cases where a trustworthy person reports after prayer, and determine when the mufta bihi ruling requires a repeat.

Core Idea
Certainty is not removed by doubt: even a trustworthy report after salam only triggers a repeat if the prayer itself becomes doubtful.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates how one of the five major Hanafi maxims, 'Certainty is not removed by doubt,' governs real-life prayer scenarios. When a trustworthy informant contradicts one's recollection of rak'ahs, the ruling is not simply to accept the report; rather, the maxim interacts with the principle of precaution (ihtiyat) and the imam's authoritative certainty. Understanding this case trains the mufti in balancing textual rulings with the hierarchy of certainty.

Guided Path
1
State the governing qawida
Begin by reciting the maxim: al-yaqin la yazul bi al-shakk. Recognize that it has the rank of a kulliyya (comprehensive principle) applicable across fiqh.
This is one of the five major maxims; commit it to memory.
2
Identify the specific case and its elements
Break down the scenario: a trustworthy informant (adl) speaks after the salam; the worshipper doubts the informant's truthfulness; the issue is whether to repeat the prayer.
Note the condition that the informant must be 'adl; otherwise, his report carries no weight.
3
Apply the qawida to the worshipper's doubt
The worshipper's original certainty is that he completed the prayer. The informant's report introduces doubt. The maxim says certainty prevails, so no automatic repeat. However, the text says he repeats 'on precaution' (ihtiyatan). Why? Because the doubt is not about the prayer itself but about the informant? Actually the reasoning: 'doubt in his truthfulness is doubt in the prayer' — so the doubt attaches to the prayer, making it a case where precaution is needed. The maxim still holds: certainty is not removed, but precautionary action is recommended to resolve the doubt.
This is a nuance: the qawida does not prohibit precautionary repetition; it only prohibits discarding certainty based on doubt.
4
Examine the exception: imam's certainty
When the imam is certain of his own count, he does not repeat even if the congregation disagrees. This is a direct application of the maxim: the imam's certainty overrides the congregation's doubt.
This is an istithna' from the general rule of accepting the congregation's statement when the imam is uncertain.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling and note the adab
The mufta bihi: for the general worshipper doubting an 'adl's report, repeat on precaution. For an imam certain of his count, no repeat. The mufti should advise based on the hierarchy of certainty.
This case also teaches the mufti to consider the authority level: the ruling is from zahir riwayah (in al-Khulasa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَخْبَرَهُ عَدْلٌ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ أَنَّكَ صَلَّيْتَ الظُّهْرَ أَرْبَعاً وَ شَكٍّ فِي صِدْقِهِ وَ كِذْبِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يُعِيدُ إختِيَاطًا لأَنَّ الشَّكَ فِي صِدْقِهِ شَكٍّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَلَوْ وَقَعَ الإِخْتِلَافُ بَيْنَ الْإِمَامِ وَ الْقَوْمِ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْإِمَامُ عَلَى يَقِيْنِ لَا يُعِيدُ وَ إِنْ لَّا أَعَادَ بِقَوْلِهِمْ كَذَا فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ
And if a trustworthy person informs him after the salam: 'You prayed Zuhr as four rak'ahs,' and he doubts his truthfulness or falsehood, then he repeats it on precaution because doubt in his truthfulness is doubt in the prayer. And if disagreement occurs between the imam and the congregation, then if the imam is certain, he does not repeat; otherwise, he repeats due to their statement. So it is in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on handling external information after completing prayer. When a trustworthy person reports a specific number of rak'ahs and the worshipper doubts the report's accuracy, the school requires repeating the prayer out of caution. The reasoning is that doubt about the informant's truthfulness translates into doubt about the prayer itself, and certainty is not removed by doubt. The passage also addresses a conflict between imam and followers: the imam's certainty prevails, but if he is uncertain, he follows the congregation's report.

Key Terms
عدل (adl): A trustworthy, upright person whose testimony is acceptable

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a trustworthy person tells you after salam that you prayed four rak'ahs of Zuhr, and you doubt his truthfulness, what should you do?
A) Ignore him
B) Repeat the prayer on precaution
C) Ask another person
D) Accept it without repeat

Key Takeaway
When a trustworthy report contradicts certainty after prayer, the Hanafi school rules for precautionary repetition unless the imam is certain—applying the maxim that certainty is not removed by doubt.

Ruling on Changing Intentions Mid-Prayer with Doubt
Application of al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk to prayer intention doubts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to cases of persistent doubt about intention in prayer, and identify the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Certainty of original intention is not undone by subsequent doubts, no matter how many.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair applies the foundational maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to a hypothetical scenario where a worshipper experiences successive doubts about the identity of his prayer. The ruling affirms that the prayer remains valid as originally intended, demonstrating the practical force of qawaid in ifta.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Recall the Arabic and English of the maxim, and note that it is one of the five major (kubra) maxims.
Memorize: al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk.
2
Identify the certainty
The original intention for Zuhr is the established certainty. Note it clearly as the baseline.
3
Note each doubt
List the three doubts: in second rak'ah (Asr), third (nafl), fourth (Zuhr). Recognize they are mere doubts with no supporting evidence.
4
Apply the maxim
Each doubt is legally disregarded because certainty cannot be overcome by doubt. The original intention remains intact.
The phrase 'laysa bi shay'' in the source confirms the doubt is treated as nothing.
5
Derive the ruling
The prayer continues as valid Zuhr. No need for correction or repetition.
This ruling applies as long as the doubt does not amount to certainty of a change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ صَلَى رَكْعَةً بِنِيَّةِ الظُّهْرِ ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي الْعَصْرِ ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي التَّطَوُّعِ ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي الظُّهْرِ قَالُوْا يَكُوْنُ فِي الظُّهْرِ وَالشَّكُ لَيْسَ بِشَيْءٍ
And if he prayed one rak'ah with the intention of Zuhr, then doubted in the second whether he is in Asr, then doubted in the third whether he is in supererogatory prayer, then doubted in the fourth whether he is in Zuhr, they said: he is considered in Zuhr, and the doubt is nothing.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage illustrates the application of the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' in a complex scenario of shifting intentions. A person starts Zuhr but experiences successive doubts about the prayer's identity. Despite these doubts, the scholars rule that the prayer remains valid as Zuhr, because the original intention (certainty) is not overridden by subsequent doubts. Each doubt is disregarded as baseless. The ruling emphasizes that persistent wavering does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention to perform a specific prayer
شك (shakk): Doubt, uncertainty about the state of affairs
يقين (yaqin): Certainty, firm knowledge

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid
B) It counts as Zuhr
C) He must choose the most likely
D) He must restart

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' safeguards the validity of acts of worship when doubts are baseless.

Applying 'Certainty is not Removed by Doubt' to Missed Prostration Uncertainty
Ruling for uncertainty in prostration between two prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to a case of uncertainty in prayer and construct the mufta bihi ruling with its precautionary steps.

Core Idea
Certainty is not removed by doubt: when unsure which prayer a missed sajdah belongs to, perform taharri; if inconclusive, complete current prayer and repeat both on precaution.

This lesson examines a real furu' case from Hanafi fiqh where the general maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' meets the specific difficulty of determining the source of a missed prostration. The ruling balances the need to preserve the integrity of prayer with practical leniency, showing how qawaid operate in ifta'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt and its object
Determine what is uncertain: the person knows a sajdah was missed, but does not know whether it belongs to the previous Zuhr or the current Asr. This uncertainty triggers the need for a ruling.
The doubt is about the 'source' of the missed act, not about the act itself.
2
Apply the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt'
The original certainty is that each prayer was complete. The doubt does not invalidate that certainty. Therefore, the person cannot simply repeat everything without a procedure.
The maxim preserves the original completion of Zuhr and Asr until evidence overcomes it.
3
Execute taharri (reflection) as a first step
The person must reflect (taharri) to try to determine the most likely prayer where the sajdah was missed. This is an attempt to resolve the doubt through probability.
If taharri yields a conclusion, act accordingly. The text assumes it does not.
4
Default procedure when taharri fails
If taharri is inconclusive, complete the current Asr prayer – add one sajdah (since the missing sajdah might be from Asr) – then repeat both Zuhr and Asr as a precaution (ihtiyatan).
One sajdah suffices because the missing sajdah is single; if it were from Asr, it completes it; if from Zuhr, the repetition covers it.
5
Note the optional nature of repetition
If the person does not repeat the prayers, nothing is due upon him. This shows that the repetition is recommended (mustahabb) for precaution, not obligatory. The maxim's authority is softened by the sub-maxim 'hardship brings ease'.
This istithna' prevents undue hardship and reflects the leniency in Hanafi fiqh for such uncertainties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ تَذَكَّرَ مُصَلِى الْعَصْرِ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ سَجْدَةً وَلَمْ يَدْرِ هَلْ تَرَكَهَا مِنَ الظُّهْرِ أَوِ الْعَصْرِ الَّذِي هُوَ فِيهَا تَحَرَّى فَإِنْ لَّمْ يَقَعُ تَحَرِّيْهِ عَلَى شَىْءٍ يُتِمُّ الْعَصْرَ وَيَسْجُدُ سَجْدَةً وَاحِدَةً ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ الظُّهْرَ احْتِيَاطًا ثُمَّ يُعِيدَ الْعَصْرَ فَإِنْ لَّمْ يُعِدْ فَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ
And if a person praying Asr remembers that he left a prostration and does not know whether he left it from Zuhr or from Asr which he is in, he performs taharri (reflection). If his taharri does not settle on anything, he completes Asr and performs one prostration, then repeats Zuhr on precaution, then repeats Asr. If he does not repeat, nothing is due upon him.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a person remembers a missed prostration but is uncertain whether it belongs to the previous Zuhr prayer or the current Asr prayer. The Hanafi ruling prescribes taharri (seeking the most likely conclusion). If taharri yields no result, the worshipper completes the current Asr prayer, performs one additional prostration, and then repeats both Zuhr and Asr as a precaution. However, if he does not repeat, no sin or obligation remains, indicating leniency due to the difficulty of determining the exact error.

Key Terms
تحري (taharri): The act of reflecting and trying to determine the most likely state of affairs
سجدة (sajdah): Prostration; one unit of sujud in prayer
احتياطًا (ihtiyatan): As a precaution; an action recommended for extra certainty, not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if, after completing Asr prayer, they remember missing a sajdah but are unsure if it was from Zuhr or Asr?
A) Immediately repeat both prayers
B) Perform taharri; if unclear, complete Asr with one sajdah and repeat both prayers on precaution
C) Repeat only Asr
D) Ignore the memory

Key Takeaway
When uncertainty arises about which prayer a missed sajdah belongs to, the Hanafi ruling uses 'certainty is not removed by doubt' combined with 'hardship brings ease' to prescribe a taharri-based precautionary procedure that is not strictly obligatory.

Applying 'al-Yaqin la Yazulu bi al-Shakk' to Doubts in Prayer
Fatwa from al-Mujtaba on doubts in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to determine the fatwa for a mustafti who reports a first-time doubt versus habitual waswas regarding takbir, hadath, najasah, or wiping the head in prayer.

Core Idea
First-time doubt requires repeating the act; recurrent doubt is ignored.

This lesson examines a key fatwa passage from al-Mujtaba that applies the grand maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to common doubts in prayer. Understanding the distinction between a genuine first-time doubt and obsessive waswas is essential for a mufti to give correct guidance. The passage provides clear rulings for four scenarios: doubt about takbir, hadath (breaking wudu), najasah on clothes, and wiping the head during wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
State the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' and note that it governs all acts, especially prayer and purity.
This maxim is one of the five major maxims of Hanafi fiqh.
2
Extract the ruling for first-time doubt
From the passage, note that for each of the four scenarios, if the doubt is a first occurrence, the person must 'start over' (istaghbal) — i.e., repeat the doubted act.
First-time doubt triggers an obligation to re-establish certainty.
3
Extract the ruling for recurrent doubt
The passage clarifies that if the same doubt occurs repeatedly, it is considered waswas and should be ignored.
Recurrent doubt does not remove the original certainty.
4
Analyze the special case of doubt between takbir al-iftitah and qunut
If one doubts whether the takbir uttered was for opening or for qunut, the person is not considered to have started the prayer (la yasir shari'an).
This is because the intention for the opening takbir is missing.
5
Apply the maxim to a fatwa scenario
Given a mustafti's description, determine whether the doubt is first-time or recurrent, then advise accordingly.
Always ask whether this is the first time or if it happens often.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فِي الْمُجْتَبَىٰ إِذَا شَكٍّ أنَّهُ كَبَّرَ لِلإفْتِتَاحِ اوْ لَا أَوْ هَلْ أَحْدَثَ أوْ لَا أَوْهَلْ أَصَابَتِ النِّجَاسَةُ ثَوْبَهُ أَوْلَا أَوْ مَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ أَوْلَا اسْتَقْبَلْ إِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ وَ إِلَّا فَلَا إِنْتَهى وَلَوْ شَكٍّ أَنَّهَا تَكْبِيرَةُ الافْتِتَاح أو الْقُتُوْتِ لَمْ يَصِرْ شَارِعًا
In al-Mujtaba: When he doubts whether he said the takbir of iftitah or not, or whether he had an event (invalidating wudu) or not, or whether najasah touched his garment or not, or whether he wiped his head or not, he should start over if it is the first time; otherwise no. End. And if he doubts whether it is the takbir of iftitah or of qunut, he does not become a starter (of prayer).
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from al-Mujtaba addresses common doubts that arise during prayer regarding fundamental acts. The criterion is whether the doubt is a first occurrence or a recurrent waswas (whisper). If it is the first time, the person should act on the doubt and redo the act (e.g., repeat takbir, check for impurity). If the same doubt occurs frequently, it is considered waswas and should be ignored. Additionally, if someone doubts whether the takbir they uttered was the opening takbir or the qunut takbir, they are not considered to have commenced the prayer, because the intention tied to the opening takbir is essential.

Key Terms
تكرير (takrir): Repetition of an act due to doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Mujtaba, if a person doubts whether they said the opening takbir for the first time, what should they do?
A) Ignore it and continue
B) Repeat the takbir
C) Cancel the prayer entirely
D) Ask someone else

Key Takeaway
When in doubt about an act of worship, a mufti must first determine whether the doubt is a first-time occurrence (repeat the act) or recurrent (ignore it).

Applying the Qawida: Certainty Not Removed by Doubt in Fajr Prayer
Ruling for doubt in Fajr standing from al-Bazzaziyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-yaqin la yuzal bi al-shakk' to a case of doubt in prayer and identify the exception when later doubts are ignored.

Core Idea
In doubt, discard the uncertain and act on certainty; then ignore subsequent doubts.

This passage from al-Bazzaziyyah presents a practical application of the foundational Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.' In Fajr prayer, if a person stands up but doubts whether it is the first or second rak'ah, the ruling prescribes abandoning that standing and starting a fresh sequence. Moreover, any further doubt that arises after the prescribed action is taken is ignored. This illustrates both the primary rule and its boundary condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt scenario
Read the source: a person in Fajr prayer stands up but does not know if it is the first or second rak'ah. This is the core doubt.
The doubt is about the current standing (qiyam).
2
Apply the qawida: certainty not removed by doubt
The default state is that the prayer is incomplete. Since the person is uncertain, they cannot assume the rak'ah counts. Therefore they must abandon the standing and treat it as if it did not exist.
This is the primary rule: rafd (abandonment).
3
Follow the prescribed remedial steps
The mufti instructs: sit down, recite tashahhud (as if completing the second rak'ah), then pray two full rak'ahs with Fatihah and an additional surah, then complete the prayer with sajdah sahw. This restores certainty.
The procedure ensures the prayer is valid.
4
Recognize the istithna' (exception)
If later the person doubts whether a particular prostration belongs to the first or second rak'ah, they should continue and ignore the doubt. This is because the earlier doubt has been resolved by the action, so a new doubt on the same matter is not acted upon.
The text says 'yamdi fiha' (he continues in it).
5
Connect the case to the qawida and its rank
This case is a fur' of the kubra qawida 'certainty not removed by doubt'. The ruling demonstrates the primary application and the boundary (istithna') that prevents endless doubt.
The qawida governs all chapters, especially prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ شَكٍّ فِي الْقِيَامِ فِي الْفَجْرِ أَنَّهَا الْأَوْلى أَوِ الثَّانِيَةُ رَفَضَهُ وَقَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُّدِ ثُمَّ صَلَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ بِفَاتِحَةٍ وَصُوْرَةٍ ثُمَّ أَتَمَّ وَسَجَدَ لِلسَّهْوِ فَإِنْ شَكٍّ فِي سَجْدَتِهِ أَنَّهَا عَنِ الْأَوْلىٰ أَمْ عَنِ الثَّانِيَةِ يَمْضِيْ فِيْهَا
And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Doubt in the standing in Fajr whether it is the first or second rak'ah: he discards it and sits for the amount of tashahhud, then prays two rak'ahs with Fatihah and a surah, then completes and prostrates for forgetfulness. Then if he doubts in his prostration whether it is from the first or second, he continues in it.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazzaziyyah addresses a specific doubt during Fajr prayer: the person stands up but is uncertain whether it is the first or second rak'ah. The Hanafi ruling is to abandon that standing, sit down, recite the tashahhud (as if completing the second rak'ah), then pray two full rak'ahs with Fatihah and an additional surah, then complete the prayer with sajdah sahw. This procedure resolves the uncertainty by effectively treating the doubt as if the prayer was incomplete. Furthermore, if later he doubts whether a particular prostration was for the first or second rak'ah, he continues without action — the doubt is ignored.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): To discard or abandon the current standing due to doubt
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed at the end of prayer to compensate for errors

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from al-Bazzaziyyah, what should a person do if they doubt in Fajr whether the current standing is for the first or second rak'ah?
A) Continue standing based on the majority of cases
B) Abandon the standing, sit for tashahhud, pray two rak'ahs, and do sajdah sahw
C) Repeat the entire prayer from the beginning
D) Seek advice from another person before acting

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'certainty is not removed by doubt' dictates that in Fajr, an uncertain standing must be abandoned and replaced with two fresh rak'ahs; subsequent doubts are ignored.

Applications of the Maxim of Certainty in Doubt About Prayer and Hajj
Furuat of qawida concerning doubt in prayer and Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to cases of doubt in prayer and Hajj, distinguish between first-time and repeated doubt, and identify the muftā bihī position on doubt in Hajj pillars.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails until proven otherwise; first-time doubt demands action, repeated doubt is ignored.

This lesson presents a series of practical cases (furuat) from the Hanafi tradition illustrating the major qawida 'Certainty is not removed by doubt'. The passage, drawn from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazāʾir, walks through scenarios in prayer and Hajj where doubt arises, showing how the mufti applies the maxim to reach a ruling. You will see the maxim in action, distinguish between first-time and persistent doubt, and understand the intra-Hanafi disagreements on resolving doubt in Hajj pillars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt and the object of certainty
Determine what is in doubt (e.g., whether an act occurred) and what is known with certainty (e.g., the previous state).
Example: if unsure about hadath, the original certainty is purity.
2
Assess if the doubt is first-time or repeated
If it is the first occurrence of such doubt, the worshipper must act to resolve it (e.g., repeat the act). If it occurs repeatedly (waswasa), the doubt is ignored.
The text from al-Mujtaba states: 'if it is the first time, otherwise no'.
3
Apply the relevant furu‘ ruling
For doubt about the opening takbir, hadath, najasah, or wiping the head, repeat the act if first-time. For doubt about a missed sajdah between Zuhr and Asr, perform taharrī (seeking preponderance) and if no preponderance, repeat both prayers as a precaution.
If doubt concerns the number of rak‘ahs in Fajr, additional steps are taken (abandon standing, sit, pray two rak‘ahs, then sajdat al-sahw).
4
Handle doubt in Hajj pillars by identifying the muftā bihī view
Three views exist: taharrī (al-Khassaf), repeat the pillar (general mashāyikh), or build on the least (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah). The muftā bihī is building on the least.
The reason: repeating a pillar does not invalidate Hajj, but building on the least aligns with the principle of certainty.
5
Differentiate between doubt about verbal and action pillars in prayer
If one remembers leaving a verbal pillar (e.g., a dhikr wājib), the prayer is invalid. If leaving an action pillar (like rukū‘), treat it as leaving rukū‘: prostrate, sit, then pray an extra rak‘ah with sajdat al-sahw.
Verbal pillars cannot be compensated; action pillars can be remedied by adding a rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُعِيدُ الظُّهْرَ احْتِيَاطًا ثُمَّ يُعِيدَ الْعَصْرَ فَإِنْ لَّمْ يُعِدْ فَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ. وَ فِي الْمُجْتَبَىٰ إِذَا شَكٍّ أنَّهُ كَبَّرَ لِلإفْتِتَاحِ اوْ لَا أَوْ هَلْ أَحْدَثَ أوْ لَا أَوْهَلْ أَصَابَتِ النِّجَاسَةُ ثَوْبَهُ أَوْلَا أَوْ مَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ أَوْلَا اسْتَقْبَلْ إِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ وَ إِلَّا فَلَا. وَلَوْ شَكٍّ أَنَّهَا تَكْبِيرَةُ الافْتِتَاح أو الْقُتُوْتِ لَمْ يَصِرْ شَارِعًا. وَلَوْ شَكٍّ فِي أَرْكَانِ الْحَجِّ ذَكَرَ الْخَصَّافُ أَنَّهُ يَتَحَرَّى كَمَا فِي الصَّلوةِ وَ قَالَ عَامَّةُ مَشَائِحِنَا يُؤدِّى ثَانِيَاً لأَنَّ تَكْرَارَ الرُّكْنِ وَ الزِّيَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ لَا يُفْسِدُ الْحَجَّ وَ زِيَادَةُ الرَّكْعَةِ تُفْسِدُ الصَّلوةَ فَكَانَتْ تَحَرِّى فِى بَابِ الصَّلوةِ أَحْوَطُ كَذَا فِي الْمُحِيْطِ وَ فِي الْبَدَائِعِ أَنَّهُ فِي الْحَجِّ يَبْنِي عَلَى الأَقَلِّ فِي ظَاهِرِ الرَّوَايَةِ. وَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ شَكٍّ فِي الْقِيَامِ فِي الْفَجْرِ أَنَّهَا الأولى أوِ الثَّانِيَةُ رَفَضَهُ وَقَعَدَ قَدْرَ الصَّشَهدِ ثُمَّ صَلَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ بِفَاتِحَةٍ وَصُوْرَةٍ ثُمَّ أَتَمَّ وَسَجَدَ لِلسَّهْوِ فَإِنْ شَكٍّ فِي سَجْدَتِهِ أَنَّهَا عَنِ الأَوْلَىٰ أَمْ عَنِ الثَّانِيَةِ يَمْضِيْ فِيْهَا وَإِنْ شَكٍّ فِي السَّجْدَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ لأَنَّ إِثْمَامَهَا لَازِمٌ عَلى كُلِّ حَالٍ وَإِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ السَّجْدَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ قَعَدَ ثُمَّ قَامَ وَصَلىَ رَكْعَةً وَ أَتَمَّ بِسَجدَةِ السَّهو . وَإِنْ شَكٍّ فِي سَجْدَتِهِ أَنَّهُ صَلَى الْفَجْرَ رَكْعَتَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثًا إِنْ كَانَ فِي السَّجْدَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ فَسَدَتْ صَلَالُهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي السَّجْدَةِ الأَوْلى يُمْكِنُ إِصْلَاحُهَا عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٌ لأَنْ تَمَامَ الْمَاهِيَةِ بِالرَّفْعِ عِنْدَهُ فَتَرْتَفِعُ السَّجْدَةُ بِالرَّفْضِ ارْتِفَاعَهَا بِالْحَدَثِ فَيَقُوْمُ وَيَقْعُدُ وَيَسْجُدُ لِّلسَّهْرِ إِلَى أَنْ قَالَ نَوْعٌ مِّنْهُ تَذَكَّرَ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ رَكْنَا قَوْلِيًّا فَسَندَتْ صَلوتُهُ وَ إِنْ تَرَكَ فِعْلِيًّا يُحْمَلُ عَلَى تَرْكِ الرُّكُوعِ فَيَسْجُدُ ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ ثُمَّ يَقُوْمُ وَيُصَلِّى رَكْعَةً بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ.
He repeats Zuhr as a precaution, then repeats Asr; if he does not repeat, nothing is upon him. And in al-Mujtaba: when he doubts that he said the opening takbir or not, or whether he had an event, or whether impurity touched his garment, or whether he wiped his head, he repeats if it is the first time; otherwise no. And if he doubts whether it is the opening takbir or the qunut takbir, he does not become a starter. And if he doubts in the pillars of Hajj, al-Khassaf said he exercises ijtihad (taharrī) as in prayer, and the generality of our mashāyikh said he performs it a second time because repetition of the pillar and addition to it does not invalidate Hajj, whereas adding a rak'ah invalidates prayer, so taharrī in the chapter of prayer is more precautionary. Likewise in al-Muhīt, and in al-Badā'i' that in Hajj he builds upon the least according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. And in al-Bazzāziyyah: doubt about standing in Fajr whether it is the first or second [rak'ah] – he abandons it and sits to the extent of the tashahhud, then prays two rak'ahs with Fātiḥah and a sūrah, then completes and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he doubts about his prostration whether it is from the first or second, he continues in it; and if he doubts about the second prostration, because its completion is necessary in any case; and when he raises his head from the second prostration, he sits, then stands and prays one rak'ah and completes with the prostration of forgetfulness. And if he doubts about his prostration whether he prayed Fajr as two or three rak'ahs: if it is in the second prostration, his prayer becomes invalid; if it is in the first prostration, it can be rectified according to Muhammad because the completion of the essence is by raising (according to him), so the prostration is annulled by abandonment just as it is annulled by an event; so he stands, sits, and prostrates for forgetfulness, up to what he said: a type where he remembers that he left a verbal pillar – his prayer becomes invalid; and if he left an action pillar, it is taken to be leaving bowing, so he prostrates, then sits, then stands and prays one rak'ah with two prostrations.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) of the major Hanafi qawida 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك). The author presents several practical cases from prayer and Hajj to illustrate how the mufti applies this maxim. The first case involves doubt about missing a sajdah after completing Asr: the worshipper makes tahrīri (seeking a preponderant opinion) and then repeats Zuhr and Asr as a precaution; if he does not repeat, no sin lies on him. The second case, from al-Mujtaba, deals with doubt about the opening takbir, or about hadath, or about najasah on clothing, or about wiping the head – if it is the first time such doubt occurs, he must repeat the act; otherwise (if it happens frequently) he disregards it. This is a direct application of the maxim: the initial certainty is not overridden by a single doubt. The third case addresses doubt whether a takbir is the opening or for qunut – the person does not enter the prayer because the opening takbir is essential. Then the text moves to Hajj: al-Khassaf suggests tahrīri like in prayer, the general mashāyikh say repeat the pillar, and according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah one builds on the least (the smallest number of acts) because repetition does not invalidate Hajj as it does in prayer. The Bazzāziyyah citations give detailed rules for Fajr prayer: if one doubts whether the standing rak'ah is first or second, he abandons that rak'ah, sits for tashahhud, then prays two rak'ahs and does sajdat al-sahw. If he doubts about a single sajdah being from the first or second rak'ah, he continues it; but if he doubts about the second sajdah, he must complete it. This is because the second sajdah is integral to the rak'ah. Finally, if he doubts whether he prayed two or three rak'ahs in Fajr, if he is in the second sajdah the prayer is invalid, but if in the first sajdah, according to Imam Muhammad, he can rectify it by rejecting that sajdah (since its completion has not yet occurred) and then completing as usual. The passage ends with a note: if one remembers leaving a verbal pillar (e.g., a dhikr wajib), the prayer is invalid; if leaving an action pillar (like ruku'), he treats it as if he left ruku' and prostrates, sits, then prays an extra rak'ah with sajdat al-sahw. Each ruling consistently returns to the principle of basing action on certainty and ignoring doubt except when specified otherwise.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): A doubt about the occurrence or number of an act in worship; legal doubt that triggers the rule of building on certainty.
التحري (al-taḥarrī): The effort to reach a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-ẓann) when in doubt, by considering signs and probabilities.
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to rectify errors (like doubt, omission, or addition) in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' requires action on first-time doubt (repeat or rebuild on the least) and disregard for repeated doubt (waswasa), with the muftā bihī for Hajj being building on the least.

Doubting Missed Qira'ah: Applying Certainty Over Doubt
Example of applying 'certainty not removed by doubt' to missed qira'ah in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim "اليقين لا يزول بالشك" to doubts about omitted qira'ah in salah and determine which prayers must be repeated according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
If you doubt missing qira'ah, repeat only the minimum number of rak'ahs needed to resolve the doubt.

This passage shows how the great legal maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' governs a common scenario: after completing all five daily prayers, a person recalls omitting qira'ah in one rak'ah of an unknown prayer. Rather than repeating everything, the law requires only the minimum action to restore certainty. We'll explore the reasoning and the precise ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the governing maxim
Identify the qawida that controls this case: اليقين لا يزول بالشك (Certainty is not removed by doubt).
This is one of the five major legal maxims (al-qawa'id al-kubra).
2
Analyze the doubt scenario
The person is certain he performed all five prayers, but doubts whether he omitted qira'ah in one specific prayer. The doubt is about which prayer.
The certainty is that he prayed; the doubt is about a deficiency in one of them.
3
Determine the minimum required to remove doubt
Since the number of omitted rak'ahs (1 or 2) is smaller than the full set, only the prayers with the fewest rak'ahs are repeated to cover the possibility.
Fajr has 2 rak'ahs, Witr has 3 – together they total 5, covering the possibility of 1 or 2 rak'ahs.
4
Apply the distinction for 4 rak'ah doubt
If the doubt is about omitting qira'ah in four rak'ahs (i.e., an entire four-rak'ah prayer), then all four-rak'ah prayers must be repeated because each one could be the deficient prayer.
The four-rak'ah prayers are Zuhr, Asr, and Isha.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi ruling
The ruling is: for doubt of 1-2 rak'ahs, repeat Fajr and Witr; for doubt of 4 rak'ahs, repeat all four-rak'ah prayers.
This is based on the principle of taking the lesser obligation (akhdh bi al-aqall) when certainty cannot be achieved fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح: ایک شخص نے ایک دن کی پانچوں نمازیں پڑھیں اس کے بعد یاد آیا کہ اس نے کسی نماز کی ایک رکعت میں قرآت چھوڑی ہے لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کونسی نماز تھی تو ایسی صورت میں فجر اور وتر کا اعادہ کرے اگر یاد آیا کہ دو رکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑی ہے تو یہی حکم ہے لیکن چار رکعتوں میں ترک قرآت کے متعلق شک ہے تو پھر چاروں رکعتوں والی نمازوں کا اعادہ کرے۔
Explanation: A person prayed all five prayers of a day. Afterwards he remembered that he had omitted recitation in one rak'ah of one prayer, but he does not know which prayer it was. In such a case, he should repeat Fajr and Witr. If he remembers that he omitted recitation in two rak'ahs, the same rule applies. But if he doubts about omitting recitation in four rak'ahs, then he should repeat all the prayers that have four rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents a practical application of the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك). The person prayed all five daily prayers but later doubts whether he omitted qira'ah (recitation of Fatiha and a sura) in one of the prayers. Since Fajr and Witr each have a small number of rak'ahs (2 and 3 respectively), and the doubt is about missing recitation in one rak'ah, the ruling is to repeat only these two prayers. If the doubt concerns two rak'ahs, the same rule applies. If the doubt is about four rak'ahs, the person must repeat all prayers that consist of four rak'ahs (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). The logic is that the certainty of having prayed correctly is maintained until doubt arises; however, when doubt does arise, the minimum action required to remove the doubt is taken. This is a clear example of applying the principle of taking the lesser (اقل) when in doubt.

Key Terms
قرآت (qira'ah): Recitation of the Qur'an in prayer, specifically Fatiha and a sura.
اليقين لا يزول بالشك (al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk): A major legal maxim: 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.' It means that a state of certainty continues until it is replaced by another certainty, not by mere doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person finishes all five daily prayers and later recalls that he omitted qira'ah in one rak'ah of an unknown prayer. According to the passage, which prayers must he repeat?
A) All five prayers.
B) Only Fajr and Witr.
C) Only Dhuhr, Asr, and Isha.
D) Only Fajr.

Key Takeaway
When doubt arises about missing a wajib in salah, the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling is to repeat only the prayers with the fewest rak'ahs that cover the doubted deficiency, in accordance with 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك'.

Applying Certainty to Doubt in Talaq and Oaths
Application of certainty principle to doubt in talaq and talaq oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to various scenarios of doubt in talaq and oaths of talaq, and identify the mufta bihi position when there is an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Certainty of marriage remains; doubt about talaq is resolved by taking the minimum unless certainty overrides.

A mufti often faces cases where a husband is uncertain about his divorce or oath. This lesson applies the foundational maxim 'Certainly is not removed by doubt' to such scenarios, guiding the fatwa process. We will explore how to handle doubt about occurrence and number of talaq, and understand the minority view of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Establish the Principle
Recognize that the original state (marriage) is certain; doubt cannot remove it. The maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' is the foundation.
This is a kubra (major) maxim of Hanafi fiqh.
2
Distinguish Doubt Types
Separate doubt about whether any talaq occurred (no effect) from doubt about number (take minimum).
3
Apply Minimum to Quantity Doubt
If certain of at least one talaq but unsure of more, only one is effective unless certainty or dominant presumption of greater.
Exception: certainty or ghalabat al-zann overrides.
4
Incorporate Witness and Admission
Trustworthy witnesses may establish the number; husband's own admission of certainty also binds him.
Conditions: witnesses must be upright (adul).
5
Handle Oath of Talaq (Yamin bi al-Talaq)
Same principle applies: minimum unless certainty of more. Imam Abu Yusuf's view of tahari and ashadd is noted but not operative for fatwa.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf vs. general view.
6
Set Mufta Bihi
For fatwa, follow the general principle (minimum) in line with the maxim; the stricter view is not relied upon.
This is the position of the later authoritative texts (e.g., al-Bazzaziyya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
