Doubt in Milk Intake: Applying 'Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt'
Ruling on marriage prohibition when milk intake is uncertain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to cases of doubt in breastfeeding and identify the mufta bihi ruling on marriage prohibition.

Core Idea
Certainty of milk ingestion is required for marriage prohibition; doubt keeps the default of permissibility.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates a classic application of the master maxim that certainty is not removed by doubt. The question: does breastfeeding with uncertain milk intake create a marriage prohibition? The Hanafi answer relies on the principle that restrictions on fundamental permissions must be established with certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Marriage is fundamentally permissible. Breastfeeding can make it prohibited, but only if milk actually reaches the infant's stomach.
2
Identify the cause of doubt
The woman puts her nipple in the infant's mouth, but it is unknown if any milk came out and entered the stomach.
3
Apply the qawida
Since there is doubt, the original certainty (permissibility of marriage) remains. The prohibition, which would require certainty, cannot be established.
The qawida is 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk'.
4
Note the related qawida
The passage mentions that the full discussion will be under 'al-asl fi al-abda' al-hurmah' (the default in matters of marriage is prohibition), but note that here the doubt prevents even that default from being applied because the doubt pertains to whether the cause (ingestion) occurred.
5
State the mufta bihi
Marriage remains halal between the woman and the infant (when adult) unless there is certainty of milk ingestion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا لَوْ أَدْخَلَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ حِلْمَةَ تَدْيِهَا فِي فَمِ الرَّضِيْعَ وَلَا يَدْرِى أَدْخَلَ اللَّيْنِ فِي خَلْقِهِ أمْ لَا لَا يَحْرُمُ النِّكَاحُ لأنَّ فِي الْمَائِعِ شَكَّا كَذَا فِي الْوَلْوَالِحِيَّةِ وَ سَيَانِي تَمَامُهُ فِي قَاعِدَةِ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِي الْأَبْضَاعِ الْحُرْمَةُ.
And among them: if a woman puts her nipple in the mouth of an infant and it is not known whether milk entered his stomach or not, marriage is not prohibited, because there is doubt about the fluid. Thus in al-Walwalijiyyah, and its completion will come under the qawida 'the default in matters of marriage is prohibition'.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is an application of the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt (اليقين لا يزول بالشك). The specific rule here is that breastfeeding (rada') only establishes a prohibition of marriage if the milk actually reaches the infant's stomach. If there is doubt about whether any milk was ingested, the default is that marriage remains permissible. This is because the prohibition is a restriction on an otherwise permissible act, and restrictions require certainty. The commentator notes that more details will follow under the qawida 'al-asl fi al-abda' al-hurmah' (the default in matters of marriage is prohibition), meaning that even though marriage is fundamentally prohibited due to certain relationships, here the doubt prevents the prohibition from taking effect.

Key Terms
حرمة الرضاع (hurmah al-rada'): The prohibition of marriage due to breastfeeding relationships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman puts her nipple in an infant's mouth but is unsure if any milk came out. What is the ruling on marriage between the woman and the infant when he grows up?
A) Marriage is prohibited because of the possibility.
B) Marriage is permissible because of doubt.
C) Marriage is prohibited only if the infant is less than two years old.
D) Marriage is permissible only if the woman is not the infant's mother.

Key Takeaway
When milk ingestion is doubtful, the default permissibility of marriage remains; prohibition requires certainty.

Dispute over Possession of Sold or Leased Property: The Qawida 'Al-Asl 'Adam al-Qabd'
Qawida application to delivery disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-asl 'adam al-qabd' to resolve disputes over delivery in sales (buyu') and leases (ijarah) and identify the resulting ruling.

Core Idea
If parties dispute possession, the denier's word prevails because the default is non-possession.

When a seller claims the buyer took possession but the buyer denies it, or when a lessor claims the lessee took possession but the lessee denies it, how does the Hanafi school resolve the dispute? This lesson examines the legal maxim 'al-asl 'adam al-qabd' (the default is non-possession) as applied in such cases. Understanding this maxim sharpens your ability to allocate risk and liability in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contested fact
In a sale or lease, one party (seller/lessor) asserts that possession (qabd) has occurred; the other (buyer/lessee) denies it. Determine who is the 'claimant' (asserting a new fact) and who is the 'denier' (denying a change from the default).
The claimant bears the burden of proof.
2
Recall the default rule: al-asl 'adam al-qabd
The Hanafi school holds that the default state is that possession has not been transferred. This is a subsidiary maxim under 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' (things remain as they were). The property is presumed to remain with the owner until proven otherwise.
The opposing principle would be 'al-asl 'adam al-daman' (default is no liability), related but distinct.
3
Apply the rule to the dispute
Since the denier (buyer/lessee) asserts the default (non-possession), their statement is accepted without proof. The claimant (seller/lessor) must provide evidence. If no evidence, the ruling favors the denier.
This applies to both sale (buyu') and lease (ijarah) chapters.
4
Confirm the authority and scope
This ruling is cited from al-Hidayah's chapter on ijarah. It is a relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school. The maxim operates within the domain of contractual disputes over delivery.
The maxim does not apply if there is a written contract or witnesses establishing possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا لَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي قَبْضِ الْمَبِيْعِ أَوِ الْعَيْنِ الْمُوْجَرَةِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ كَمَا فِي إِجَارَةِ الْهَدَيْبِ.
And among them: if they dispute about the possession of the sold item or the leased asset, the statement is for the one who denies possession, as in Ijarah of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is another application of the qawida 'al-asl 'adam al-daman' (default no liability) and also the principle that the default is non-existence of a claim. In a sale (bay') or lease (ijarah), possession (qabd) is a legal fact that affects liability and risk. If the seller/lessor claims that the buyer/lessee took possession, and the buyer/lessee denies it, the statement of the denier is accepted because the default is that the property remained with the owner. The burden of proof is on the one who asserts possession. This ruling is taken from al-Hidayah's chapter on ijarah.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Physical or constructive possession of property; transfer of risk and liability.
الأصل عدم القبض (al-asl 'adam al-qabd): Legal maxim: the default ruling is that possession has not occurred.
المبيع (al-mabi'): The sold item (object of sale).
العين الموجرة (al-'ayn al-mujara): The leased asset (object of lease).
منكر (munkir): The one who denies a claim (the denier).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over possession of a leased house, the lessor claims the lessee took possession, but the lessee denies. Who must provide evidence, and whose statement is initially accepted?
A) The lessor must provide evidence; the lessee's denial is accepted initially.
B) The lessee must provide evidence; the lessor's claim is accepted initially.
C) Both must provide evidence; the judge decides.
D) The lessor's statement is accepted because he is the owner.

Key Takeaway
In sale and lease disputes over possession, the Hanafi rule is 'the default is non-possession'—the denier's word prevails until the claimant proves otherwise.

Debtor's Claim vs. Creditor's Denial: The Maxim of Continuity
Application of continuity maxim to debtor's defense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' to determine whose statement is accepted in debt-related furu' and identify the burden of proof.

Core Idea
Once a debt is proven, the default is that it remains unpaid unless the debtor proves payment or discharge.

This lesson introduces a practical application of a major legal maxim: 'The default is that things remain as they were.' When a debt is established—by admission or evidence—the law presumes it continues. If the debtor later claims to have paid or been discharged, his claim alone is insufficient; the creditor's denial is accepted. This preserves the reliability of established obligations and places the burden of proof on the party asserting a change.

Guided Path
1
Identify the established fact
Note that a debt has been proven either by the debtor's own admission or by evidence (bayyinah). This creates a certain obligation.
The default applies to any established obligation, not just debts.
2
Apply the maxim of continuity
The qawida 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' presumes the debt continues until a change is proven. Thus, the original state (debt exists) is the default.
This is a kubra (major) maxim covering all fiqh.
3
Determine burden of proof
Since the debtor claims a change (payment or discharge), he must bring evidence. The creditor's denial is accepted without proof because it aligns with the default.
This complements the qawida 'al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i.'
4
Derive the ruling
Therefore, the ruling: the creditor's statement (denial) is taken unless the debtor proves payment or discharge. This applies to both claims of payment (ada') and discharge (ibra').
Same ruling for both claims because both assert a change from the established state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا لَوْ ثَبَتَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنَ بِاقْرَارِ أَوْ بَيْنَةٍ فَادَّعى الأَدَاءَ أَوِ الإِبْرَاءَ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلدَّائِمِ.
And among them: if a debt is established against someone by admission or evidence, then he claims payment or discharge, the statement is for the creditor.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is another application of the qawida 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' (the default is that things remain as they were). Once a debt is proven (by the debtor's own admission or by proof), the default is that the debt remains unpaid. Therefore, if the debtor later claims he paid or was discharged (ibra'), his statement is not accepted; the creditor's denial is accepted unless the debtor brings evidence. The burden of proof shifts to the debtor because the original obligation is established. This ruling is common in all schools but Hanafi emphasizes the continuation of the original state.

Key Terms
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Discharge from a debt, releasing the debtor from obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man admitted in court that he owes Zayd $100. Later, he claims he paid but has no proof. Whose statement is accepted?
A) The debtor's, because payment is his personal act.
B) The creditor's, because the debt is already proven.
C) Neither, the case is dismissed.
D) The judge decides based on custom.

Key Takeaway
When a debt is proven, the law presumes it continues; the debtor alleging payment or discharge must provide evidence, and the creditor's denial is accepted.

8 min
Rule of Evidence in Disputes over Accidental and Essential Attributes
Explaining the legal presumption in disputes over accidental vs essential attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish accidental from essential attributes and apply the appropriate legal presumption (aṣl al-‘adam or aṣl al-wujūd) to determine whose word is accepted in a dispute.

Core Idea
The word of one denying accidental attributes or claiming essential attributes is accepted.

In Hanafi jurisprudence, when parties dispute over a stipulated attribute in a sale or other contract, the resolution depends on the nature of that attribute. This lesson introduces the key distinction between accidental and essential attributes and the legal presumptions attached to each. Through concrete examples, you will learn how to apply this maxim in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Classify the attribute
Determine if the attribute is accidental (ʿāriḍa) or essential (aṣliyya). Accidental attributes are not inherent, like a profession; essential attributes are intrinsic, like virginity.
Example: baking is accidental; virginity is essential.
2
Assign the presumption
For accidental attributes, the original (aṣl) is non-existence; for essential, the original is existence.
Remember: 'aṣl al-‘adam' for accidental, 'aṣl al-wujūd' for essential.
3
Identify the claimant
The party whose claim aligns with the presumption has their word accepted if no evidence. For accidental: the one denying it. For essential: the one claiming it.
4
Apply to the case
In sale, if the buyer denies an accidental attribute, his word is taken; if the seller claims an essential attribute, his word is taken.
Example: buyer denies slave is baker → buyer's word; seller claims slave-girl is virgin → seller's word.
5
Extend to other scenarios
The same logic applies to declarations of freedom and divorce: the word of the one claiming the essential attribute (slave-girl claiming virginity) or denying the accidental (master denying slave is baker) is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کا تب ہے اور مشترکی نے اس میں ان اوصاف کا انکار کیا تو اس (مشتری) کا قول معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ اصل ان دونوں کا نہ ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ دونوں صفاتِ عارضہ میں سے ہیں اور اگر کسی نے اس شرط پر باندی خریدی کہ وہ یا کرو ہے اور مشتری نے بکارت کے باقی رہنے سے انکار کیا اور بائع نے اس (قیام بکارت ) کا دعویٰ کیا تو بائع کا قول معتبر ہے اس لئے کہ اصل اس کا ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ صفت اصلیہ ہے۔ فتح القدیر کی خیار شرط کی بحث میں ایسا ہی ہے اور اس پر متفرع ہے اگر مولی نے کہا کہ میرا ہر وہ غلام جو روٹی بنانا جانتا ہو آزاد ہے کسی غلام نے اس کا نان بائی ہونے ) کی دعوی کیا اور آقا ء نے انکار کیا تو آقا ء کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
تشریح : اصل عدم ہے اس پر تفریح بیان کی جارہی ہے کہ ایک شخص نے غلام خریدا اس شرط پر کہ وہ نان بائی ہے یا کا تب ہے لہندا بائع کہتا ہے کہ وہ خباز ہے یا کا تب ہے اور مشتری اس کا انکار کرتا ہے تو مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ نان بائی ہونایا کا تب ہو نا صفات عارضہ میں سے ہے جو کہ اصل نہ ہونا ہے۔ ولو اشتراها على انها بکر : ایک شخص نے باندی با کرہ ہونے کی شرط پر خریدی پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ با کرو نہیں ہے اور بائع کہتا ہے کہ یہ باکرہ ہے تو بائع کی بات معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ مشتری کی کیونکہ بکارت صفات اصلیہ میں سے ہے کذافی فتح القدیر و على هذا تفرع لو قال کل مملوک لی : آقا ء نے کہا کہ میرا ہر نان بائی غلام آزاد ہے پھر ایک غلام نے نان بائی ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا اور آقا اس کا منکر ہے تو آقا ء کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل صفات عارضہ کا نہ ہوتا ہے۔ وَلَوْ قَالَ كُلُّ جَارِيَةٍ بِكُر لى فَهِيَ حُرَّةً فَادَّعَتْ جَارِيَةٌ أَنَّهَا بِكُرٌ وَ انْكَرَ الْمَوْلَىٰ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا وَ تَمَامُ تَفْرِيعِهِ فِي شَرْجِنَا عَلَى الكنز فِي تَعْلِيقِ الطَّلَاقِ عِنْدَ شَرْح قَوْلِهِ وَ إِنْ اخْتَلَفَا في وجود الشرط.
ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا میری ہر کنواری باندی آزاد ہے ایک باندی نے دعوی کیا کہ وہ کنواری ہے اور مولی منکر ہے تو باندی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس کی پوری تفریحات کنز پر ہماری شرح کی تعلیق طلاق کے باب میں اس قول کی شرح کے موقع پرو إن اختلفا في وجود الشرط کے مقام پر بیان کی گئی ہے۔ تشریح مولیٰ نے اپنی باندیوں کو مخاطب کر کے کہا کہ باکرہ باندی آزاد ہے تو ایک باندی نے اپنے باکرہ ہونے کا دعوی کیا تو یہاں پر باندی کی بات ہی معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ موٹی کی کیونکہ یہ صفات اصلیہ میں سے ہے جس میں اصل وجود ہے۔
And [the buyer] denied those attributes, so his statement is accepted because the original is the absence of both, since they are accidental attributes. And if someone bought a slave-girl on condition that she is a virgin, and the buyer denied the remaining virginity, and the seller claimed it, then the seller's statement is accepted because the original is its existence, as it is an essential attribute. In Fath al-Qadir, in the discussion of option of condition, it is similar. And derived from it: if the master said, 'Every slave of mine who knows how to make bread is free,' and a slave claimed he is a baker, and the master denied, then the master's statement is accepted. Commentary: The original is absence; the elaboration is being given: a person bought a slave on condition that he is a baker or weaver; the seller says he is a baker or weaver, and the buyer denies; then the buyer's statement is accepted because being a baker or weaver is among accidental attributes, for which the original is non-existence. 'And if he bought her on condition that she is a virgin': a person bought a slave-girl on condition that she is a virgin; later it became known she is not a virgin; the seller says she is a virgin; then the seller's statement is accepted, not the buyer's, because virginity is an essential attribute, as in Fath al-Qadir. And upon this is derived: if he said, 'Every slave of mine…': the master said, 'Every baker slave of mine is free'; then a slave claimed to be a baker and the master denied; then the master's statement is accepted because the original is the non-existence of accidental attributes. 'And if he said, 'Every virgin slave-girl of mine is free,' and a slave-girl claimed she is a virgin, and the master denied, then the statement is hers'; and the complete elaboration is in our commentary on al-Kanz in the chapter on suspended divorce at the explanation of his statement, 'and if they differ regarding the existence of the condition'. Translation: And if he said, 'Every virgin slave-girl of mine is free,' and a slave-girl claimed she is a virgin, and the master denied, then the slave-girl's statement is accepted; and its complete elaboration is in our commentary on al-Kanz in the chapter on suspended divorce at the explanation of the statement, 'and if they differ regarding the existence of the condition'. Commentary: The master addressed his slave-girls saying, 'The virgin slave-girl is free'; then a slave-girl claimed her virginity; here the slave-girl's statement is accepted, not the master's, because this is among essential attributes where the original is existence.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on disputes over attributes in sales, particularly when a condition is stipulated. The key principle is that the legal presumption (asl) differs based on the nature of the attribute. For accidental attributes (sifāt ‘āriḍa) such as being a baker or weaver, the original state is non-existence, so the buyer's denial is accepted. For essential attributes (sifāt aṣliyya) such as virginity, the original state is existence, so the seller's claim is accepted. The text illustrates this with three scenarios: 1) a slave sold with condition of being a baker/weaver – buyer's word; 2) a slave-girl sold as virgin – seller's word; 3) a master declaring freedom for baker slaves or virgin slave-girls – the word of the one claiming the essential attribute (slave-girl) or denying the accidental (master) is taken. This rule is derived from the broader maxim 'al-aṣl ‘adam al-‘āriḍ' (original absence of accidentals) and 'al-aṣl baqā’ mā kān‘ (original continuance of what was). The ruling is based on the principle of legal presumptions in evidence.

Key Terms
صفات عارضہ (sifāt ‘āriḍa): Accidental attributes that are not inherent in the essence, such as being a baker or weaver; the legal presumption is their non-existence.
صفات اصلیہ (sifāt aṣliyya): Essential attributes inherent in the entity, such as virginity; the legal presumption is their existence.
اصل عدم (aṣl al-‘adam): The legal presumption of non-existence applied to accidental attributes.
اصل وجود (aṣl al-wujūd): The legal presumption of existence applied to essential attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule for disputes over attributes, if a buyer buys a slave on condition that he is a weaver, and the seller claims he is a weaver while the buyer denies, whose statement is accepted?
A) The seller's, because he is the owner.
B) The buyer's, because the original is non-existence of accidental attributes.
C) The buyer's, because he paid the price.
D) The seller's, because the condition was part of the contract.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between accidental and essential attributes; the party claiming the non-existence of accidental or the existence of essential has their word accepted.

Attributing an Event to Its Nearest Time: The Maxim and Its Tahara Applications
Presents the maxim with examples from impurity, semen, urine, and blood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-aṣl iḍāfat al-ḥādith ilā aqrab awqātih' to resolve uncertainty in tahara cases and explain the Hanafi tarjih regarding ghusl for a semen stain.

Core Idea
When uncertainty meets impurity, attribute it to the last relevant event — that is the nearest time.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi maxim used when the timing of an impurity is unknown. The maxim presumes the event occurred at the nearest plausible time — such as the last sleep, urination, or nosebleed. We will explore its applications in tahara, including an intra-madhhab dispute on whether ghusl is required for a semen stain without memory of a wet dream. Understanding this maxim sharpens your ability to handle uncertainty in worship with principled reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the uncertain event
Start with the unknown: e.g., najasa on a garment, semen stain, urine spot, or bloodstain. The exact time of occurrence is not known.
The event must be a plausible cause (e.g., sleep, urination, nosebleed).
2
Determine the nearest relevant cause
Look for the last relevant event that could have produced the impurity. For example, the last time you slept (for semen), the last urination, or the last nosebleed.
If multiple events exist, choose the closest one that matches the impurity type.
3
Apply the maxim to derive the ruling
Attribute the impurity to that nearest time. Then repeat all prayers performed after that time, and if applicable (semen), perform ghusl.
The maxim yields a presumption; certainty overrides it if known.
4
Consider the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees on ghusl for semen without memory of wet dream because he considers it doubt. But the muftā bihī position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) requires ghusl out of caution.
The fatwa follows the cautious position; understand the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

قَاعِدَةُ : الأَصْلُ إضَافَةُ الْحَادِثِ إِلَى اقْرَبِ أَوْقَاتِه مِنْهَا مَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ فِيْمَا لَوْ رَاع فِي تَوْبِهِ نِجَاسَةٌ وَ قَدْ صَلَى فِيْهِ وَلَا يَدْرِكْ مَتى أَصَابَتْهُ يُعِيدُهَا مِنْ أخِرِ حَدَثٍ أَحْدَثَهُ وَ الْمَنِي مِنْ آخِرِ رُقَدَةٍ وَيَلْزَمُهُ الْغُسْلُ فِى الثَّانِيَةِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَ إِنْ لَّمْ يَتَذَكَّرُ إِحْتِلَامًا وَ فِي الْبَدَائِعِ يُعِيْدُ مِنْ آخِرِ مَا احْتَلَمَ.
ترجمه: قاعده پیش آمدہ امر کو سب سے نزدیک وقت کی طرف منسوب کرنا اصل ہے اور اس کی جزئیات میں وہ مسئلہ ہے جو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کپڑے میں نجاست دیکھی اور اس کپڑے میں نماز پڑھ چکا ہے اور معلوم نہیں کب لگی ہے نماز کو دوہرائے اس آخری حدث سے جو پیش آیا اور منی میں آخری بار سونے سے اور دوسرے مسلہ میں امام ابی حیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس پر غسل لازم ہوگا اگر چہاحتلام یاد نہ ہو اور بدائع میں ہے کہ جو آخری احتلام ہو اس وقت سے لوٹائے۔ تشریح ضابطہ نئے پیش آمدہ واقعہ کو اقرب ترین وقت کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا اسی اصل کو پیش نظر رکھ کرعلماء نے یہ مسئلہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر کسی کے کپڑے پر نجاست لگی ہوئی تھی لیکن اس کو یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ کپڑے پر نجاست کب لگی ہے اور اسی حالت میں اس نے نماز پڑھ لی بعد میں معلوم ہوا تو جب سے اس کو آخری حدث لاحق ہوا ہو اس وقت سے نماز دوہرائے گا کیونکہ یہی اقرب اوقات ہے۔ والمنى من آخر رقدة: کوئی شخص عبادت کر رہا تھا اس کو اپنے کپڑے پر منی کا دھبہ نظر آ گیا تو جب وہ آخری مرتبہ سویا ہو اس وقت سے نماز کا اعادہ کرے گا مثلاً ظہر یا عصر میں دیکھا تو آخری مرتبہ رات میں ہی سویا تھا تو فجر اور نمبر کا اعادہ کرے۔ اس مسئلہ میں طرفین کے نزدیک چونکہ سونے میں احتلام مان لیا گیا تو ظاہر ہے غسل بھی واجب ہوگا جبکہ امام یوسف کے نزدیک احتلام صرف شک ہے اور شک سے غسل واجب نہیں ہوتا لیکن طرفین کے قول میں احتیاط ہے اور وہی مفتی یہ ہے۔
صورت میں آخری مرتبہ نکسیر چلنے کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا۔
وَقِيلَ فِى الْمَوْلِ يُعْتَبَرُ مِنْ آخِرِ مَابَالَ وَ فِي الدَّمِ مِنْ آخِرِ مَا رَعُفَ . ترجمہ: اور کہا گیا کہ پیشاب کی صورت میں آخری مرتبہ پیشاب کرنے سے اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور خون کی تشریح کسی شخص نے دوران عبادت پیشاب کی چھینٹے دیکھی تو وہ چھینٹیں اس وقت کی شمار ہوں گی جب اس نے آخری مرتبہ پیشاب کیا ہو لہذا اس وقت سے جتنی عبادت کی ہو اس کو دہرالے۔ و في الدم من آخر ما رعف کسی شخص نے کپڑے پر خون کا دھبہ دیکھا تو یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ اس کو آخری مرتبہ کسی کب آئی تھی اسی وقت سے نماز کا اعادہ کرلے۔
Maxim: The principle is attributing an event to its nearest times. Among its instances is what we presented earlier: if one saw impurity on his garment and he had prayed in it, and he does not know when it affected him, he repeats [the prayers] from the last event that occurred to him. And for semen, from the last sleep. And ghusl becomes obligatory upon him in the second [instance] according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad even if he does not remember a wet dream. And in al-Bada'i': he repeats from the last wet dream. Translation: The principle is that an occurring matter is attributed to the nearest time. Among its details is the issue we mentioned earlier: if someone saw impurity on his garment and he prayed in that garment, and he does not know when it occurred, he repeats the prayer from the last event that happened. And for semen, from the last sleep. In the second issue, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, ghusl becomes obligatory upon him even if he does not remember a wet dream. In al-Bada'i': he repeats from the last wet dream. Commentary: The rule is that a newly occurring event will be attributed to the nearest time. Keeping this principle in view, the scholars mentioned this issue: if impurity is found on a garment and one does not know when it occurred, and he prayed in that state, later he discovers it; then he repeats prayers from the time of the last event that occurred to him, because that is the nearest time. 'And for semen from the last sleep': a person was worshipping and saw a semen stain on his garment; he repeats prayers from the last time he slept. For example, if he saw it at Zuhr or Asr, and he last slept at night, he repeats Fajr and... In this issue, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), since a wet dream is presumed during sleep, obviously ghusl becomes obligatory. According to Imam Yusuf, wet dream is merely doubt, and doubt does not necessitate ghusl. But the saying of the two contains caution, and that is the fatwa. In case of (urine), the last time of urination is considered. And it was said: for urine, it is considered from the last urination; and for blood, from the last nosebleed. Translation: And it was said: in the case of urine, consideration is from the last urination; and for blood, from the last nosebleed. Commentary: A person saw drops of urine during worship; those drops are counted from the time of his last urination, so he repeats whatever worship he performed since then. And 'for blood from the last nosebleed': a person saw a bloodstain on his garment; it will be seen when he last had a nosebleed, and he repeats prayers from that time.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage introduces the legal maxim 'al-aṣl iḍāfat al-ḥādith ilā aqrab awqātih' (the principle is attributing an event to its nearest time), which is a recognized qā‘ida fiqhiyya (sughrā) in the Hanafi school. The maxim applies when the exact time of an event (e.g., najāsa on clothes) is unknown; it is attributed to the closest possible time. The text provides several furū‘: 1) If impurity is found on a garment and one does not know when it occurred, he repeats prayers from the last time a relevant event (like sleeping or urinating) occurred. 2) For semen, the last sleep is taken as the time of janāba, and according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, ghusl becomes obligatory even if the person does not remember a wet dream, because sleep is a cause of janāba. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, saying it is mere doubt, but the fatwa is on the side of caution (the two imams). 3) For urine and blood (nosebleed), the last urination or nosebleed is considered. This maxim is a practical tool for resolving uncertainty in acts of worship, especially prayer repetition.

Key Terms
قاعده (qā‘ida): A general legal maxim encompassing derived cases.
الحادث (al-ḥādith): An event whose time of occurrence is uncertain, like najāsa on clothes.
اقرب اوقات (aqrab awqāt): The nearest time to which the event is plausibly attributed, e.g., last sleep, urination, or nosebleed.
حدث (ḥadath): An occurrence that breaks purification; here, the last event before discovering impurity.
منی (manī): Semen; its presence on clothing after sleep triggers the maxim and the ghusl dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person finds impurity on his garment after praying Maghrib. He does not know when it occurred, but he last slept before Fajr and last urinated after Zuhr. He also had a nosebleed just before Maghrib. According to the maxim, which event should he use to determine repeat of prayers?
A) Last sleep (before Fajr)
B) Last urination (after Zuhr)
C) Last nosebleed (before Maghrib)
D) The time of the first prayer after discovery

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim attributes an uncertain impurity event to its nearest plausible cause, enabling a clear ruling on prayer repetition and ghusl obligation.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

The Qawida of Attributing to the Nearest Time with Furu'at
Expounding a qawida with multiple furuat and a madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-amr al-ḥādith yuḍāf ilā aqrab awqātih' to cases of impurity discovery and evaluate the Hanafi ikhtilāf regarding its application to a well.

Core Idea
Attribute a new impurity to the nearest plausible time, but apparent physical evidence may override for caution.

In this lesson, we explore a classic Hanafi legal maxim that helps determine when to attribute an uncertain event. The qāʿida 'al-amr al-ḥādith yuḍāf ilā aqrab awqātih' is applied when a worshipper discovers impurity after prayer. However, not all cases are straightforward—an intra-madhhab dispute arises when physical evidence suggests a longer presence of impurity.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the qawida in Arabic and English, and understand that it applies to cases where the exact time of an impurity is unknown after prayer.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) qawida found in the Ashbah wa al-Nazair.
2
Examine the furūʿ for general impurity, semen, urine, and blood
For each type of impurity, note the nearest event to which the impurity is attributed (last impurity event, last sleep, last urination, last nosebleed).
The principle remains constant; only the reference event changes.
3
Analyze the jubbah case
Consider how the presence or absence of a hole in the cotton garment affects the attribution: no hole means the impurity has been there since the cotton was placed; a hole allows a later entry, so only three days are repeated.
This shows physical evidence can modify the nearest time.
4
Study the well case and the ikhtilāf
The Ṣāḥibayn apply the qawida strictly, attributing the mouse's fall to the time of discovery. Imam Abu Hanifa considers the mouse's condition (swollen/disintegrated) as evidence of longer presence, requiring repetition of three days or one day/night.
This ikhtilāf stems from weighing the qawida against caution (iḥtiyāṭ) based on apparent cause.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ and muftā bihī
In the semen case, the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is declared muftā bihī. For the well, the text does not give clear tarjīḥ; later practice often follows the Ṣāḥibayn for ease, but caution recommends Abu Hanifa when physical evidence is strong.
Tarjīḥ may depend on the strength of the apparent cause.

الموهوم احتياطا كالمجروح إذا لم يزل صاحب فراش حتى مات يحال به على الحرج.
The rule: Attributing a new event to the nearest time is the principle. Among its particulars is the issue we mentioned earlier: if someone sees impurity on his garment and has prayed in it, not knowing when it got there, he repeats the prayer from the last impurity that occurred. And for semen, from the last sleep. In the second issue, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, ghusl becomes obligatory upon him even if he does not recall a wet dream. And in al-Bada'i': he repeats from the time of the last wet dream. Explanation: The rule: a newly occurring event will be attributed to the nearest time. Keeping this principle in view, the scholars mentioned this issue: if someone's garment had impurity but he does not know when it got there, and he prayed in that state, later he finds out, then he repeats prayers from the time of the last impurity that befell him, because that is the nearest time. 'And semen from the last sleep': a person was worshipping and saw a semen stain on his garment; then from the time he last slept he repeats prayers. For example, if he saw it in Zuhr or Asr and he last slept at night, then he repeats Fajr and the following prayer. In this issue, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), since they assume a wet dream during sleep, obviously ghusl becomes wajib. But according to Imam Yusuf, a wet dream is only doubt and doubt does not make ghusl obligatory. However, the view of the two is cautious and it is the mufta bih. In the case of urine, the last time of urination is considered. 'And it was said regarding urine: it is considered from the last time he urinated, and regarding blood: from the last time he had a nosebleed.' Translation: And it was said that in the case of urine, consideration is from the last time he urinated. And regarding blood: if someone during worship sees drops of urine, those drops will be counted from the time he last urinated, so from that time he repeats whatever worship he performed. 'And regarding blood from the last time he had a nosebleed': if someone sees a blood stain on his garment, it will be seen when he last had a nosebleed; from that time he repeats the prayer. 'And if he tore open a cotton jacket and found a dead mouse in it, and he does not know when it entered, then if there is no hole, he repeats prayers from the day he put cotton in it; if there is a hole, he repeats from three days. And the two Sahibs acted upon this rule and thus ruled on the impurity of a well when a dead mouse is found in it from the time of knowledge of it without repeating anything, because its fall is a new event and is attributed to the nearest time. But Imam al-A'zam differed and approved repeating prayers of three days if it is swollen or disintegrated; otherwise from a day and a night, acting upon the apparent cause and not the imagined, out of caution, like the wounded man who remains bedridden until death, which is attributed to the wound.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the qawida: 'A new event is attributed to the nearest time.' The author first states the rule and then provides several furu' (applications). The first application: if a person finds impurity on his garment and has prayed in that state, he repeats prayers from the time of the last event that could have caused the impurity (e.g., a wet dream, sleep, etc.). The second application concerns semen: if a semen stain is found, the prayers after the last sleep are repeated. Here there is a subsidiary issue: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that ghusl becomes wajib because they presume a wet dream occurred during sleep, while Abu Yusuf considers it merely doubtful. The author notes that the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is cautious and is the mufta bih. The third and fourth applications deal with urine and blood: the nearest time for urine is the last urination, and for blood the last nosebleed. The fifth application is about a jubbah (cotton garment) with a dead mouse: if the garment has no hole, the mouse must have been there since the cotton was placed, so prayers repeat from that day; if there is a hole, it could have entered later, so only three days of prayers are repeated. The sixth application involves a well: the two Sahibs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) apply the same qawida, ruling that the well becomes impure only from the time of discovery, with no need to repeat past prayers. However, Imam Abu Hanifa takes a different approach: if the mouse is swollen or disintegrated, the impurity likely persisted longer, so he requires repeating prayers for three days; otherwise only one day and night. This is based on acting on the apparent cause (the condition of the mouse) rather than the imagined (the fall), as a caution (ihtiyat). The passage concludes with an analogy: a wounded person who remains bedridden until death is attributed to the wound.

Key Terms
قاعدہ (qāʿida): A legal maxim or principle that is generally applicable.
اقرب اوقات (aqrab al-awqāt): The nearest possible time to which an event can be attributed.
اعادہ (iʿāda): Repeating a prayer that was likely invalid due to impurity.
احتیاط (iḥtiyāṭ): Legal caution; choosing the more cautious ruling when evidence is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person finds a dead mouse in a well and the mouse is swollen and disintegrated, what does Imam Abu Hanifa rule regarding prayer repetition?
A) No prayers need to be repeated.
B) Repeat prayers from three days.
C) Repeat prayers from one day and night.
D) Repeat prayers from the time of discovery.

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'al-amr al-ḥādith yuḍāf ilā aqrab awqātih' is the default, but caution based on apparent cause can modify the ruling, as seen in the well case.

Maxim: Event Attributed to Nearest Possible Time with Applications
Explaining the maxim with applications and an exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-amr al-hadith yudaf ila aqrab awqatih' to resolve disputes of attribution, identify its furuat, and recognize its exception.

Core Idea
An event is attributed to the nearest possible time—but signs of prolonged presence may override the default.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi legal maxim that governs how we assign a point in time to a past event when the exact moment is unknown. The text illustrates the maxim with three concrete cases from purity, sales, and inheritance, and even includes a famous intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. By mastering this maxim and its limits, you will be able to resolve similar attribution conflicts in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
First, write down the maxim in Arabic and English. Note that it applies to events whose timing is unknown, particularly in cases of impurity, defects, and inheritance.
2
Examine the first furu': garment with a mouse
Analyze how the maxim is applied when a dead mouse is found in a garment. The presence or absence of a hole indicates the nearest possible time of entry.
No hole → entry at cotton placement; hole → entry within three days.
3
Analyze the well dispute: Sahibayn vs. Abu Hanifa
Compare the strict application of the maxim (Sahibayn: contamination only from discovery) with Imam Abu Hanifa's istihsan (considering signs of swelling). Understand the legal reasoning behind each.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether past prayers require repetition.
4
Apply to the slave’s eye and divorce cases
Work through two other furuat: (a) disputed injury to a slave's eye—buyer's statement accepted because the event is attributed to his ownership (nearest time). (b) wife claims divorce in terminal illness—her statement accepted, inherits.
In both, the maxim favors the party whose claim attributes the event to the most recent plausible time.
5
Identify the exception (kanz) and its implication
The text notes an exception: the 'treasure' case from judiciary matters (not detailed here). Recognize that no maxim is absolute; exceptions exist.
Exception shows the maxim is a general principle, not an invariable rule.

:ترجمہ: اور اگر کسی نے جبہ پھاڑا اور اس میں مری ہوئی چوہی ملی اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ وہ اس میں کب تھی تو اگر اس میں کوئی سوراخ نہ ہو تو جس روز اس میں روئی ڈالی تھی اس دن سے نماز لوٹائے اور اگر اس میں کوئی سوراخ ہوتو تین دن سے نماز لوٹائے اور صاحبین نے اس قاعدہ پر عمل کیا لہذا اگر کنویں میں مردہ چوہیا پائی جائے تو اس کے معلوم ہونے کے وقت سے کنویں کے ناپاک ہونے کا فیصلہ کیا ہے کچھ لوٹائے بغیر کیونکہ اس کا گرنا ایک امر حادث ہے اور قریب ترین وقت کی طرف نسبت کی جائے گی اور اس میں امام اعظم کا اختلاف ہے لہذا اگر وہ پھول یا چھٹی ہوئی ہیں انہوں نے تین دن کی نماز میں لوٹانے کو مستحسن قرار دیا ہے ورنہ تو موہوم کو چھوڑ کر سبب ظاہر پر عمل کرتے ہوئے ایک دن ایک رات کی نمازیں لوٹائی جائیں جیسے زخمی جب موت تک برابر صاحب فراش رہے تو اس کو اس زخم کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح: کسی کے پاس روئی کا جبہ تھا اس میں دیکھا کہ مری ہوئی چوہیا پڑی ہے اب اگر سوراخ نہیں ہے جس وقت سے اس نے اس میں روئی ڈالی ہے اسی وقت سے نمازیں لوٹائے اور اگر اس میں سوراخ ہے تو تین دن کی نمازوں کا اعادہ کرے۔ حضرات صاحبین نے اس قاعدہ پر عمل کرتے ہوئے فیصلہ کیا کہ اگر کنویں میں کوئی چوہیا پائی جائے تو جس وقت اس چوہیا کا پتہ چلا ہے اسی وقت سے وہ کنواں ناپاک ہوگا اور نماز میں وغیرہ جو اس سے پانی کر کے پڑھی ہیں واجب الاعادہ نہیں کیونکہ اس کو اقرب ترین کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا۔ جبکہ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر وہ چوہیا کنویں میں پھولی یا پھٹی ہوئی ہے تو تین دن کی نمازوں کا اعادہ واجب ہوگا ورنہ ایک دن اور ایک رات کی نماز میں لوٹانا ضروری ہوگا۔
كالمجروح: ظاہر سبب پر حکم لگتا ہے لہذا جب کوئی شخص زخمی ہونے کی حالت میں بستر پر پڑا ہے اور ان حالت میں مرجائے تو اس زخمی شخص کی موت کا سبب ظاہر وہی زخم ہوگا جس کی وجہ سے یہ صاحب فراش بناتھا۔
وَمِنْهَا لَوْ كَانَ فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ عَبْدٌ فَقَالَ رَجُلٌ فَقَاتُ عَيْنَهُ وَهُوْ فِيْ مِلْكِ الْبَائِعِ وَ قَالَ الْمُشْتَرِى فَقَاتَهُ وَ هُوَ فِي مِلْكِى فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُشْتَرِى فَيَأْخُذُ إِرْشَهُ وَمِنْهَا ادَّعَتْ أَنَّ زَوْجَهَا أبَانَهَا فِي الْمَرْضِ وَصَارَ فَارًا فَتَرِتُ وَ قَالَتِ الْوَرْثَةُ أَبَانَهَا فِي صِحَتِهِ فَلَا تَرِتُ كَانَ الْقُوْلُ قَوْلَهَا فَتَرِثُ وَخَرْجَ عَنْ هَذَا الْأَصْلِ مَسَألَةُ الْكَيْرِ مِنْ مَسَائِلَ شَتَّى مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ.
ترجمہ: اور اسی ضابطہ کے تحت یہ مسئلہ ہے ایک آدمی کے قبضہ میں ایک غلام ہے وہ آدمی کہہ رہا ہے اس غلام کی آنکھ میں نے پھوڑی جس وقت کہ وہ بائع کی ملک میں تھا اور مشتری کہہ رہا ہے اس کی آنکھ تو نے اس وقت پھوڑی جبکہ وہ غلام میری ملک میں تھا تو مشتری کے قول کا اعتبار ہوگا اور غلام کی دیت مشتری اس سے لے گا۔ اس میں سے یہ مسئلہ بھی ہے عورت نے دعوی کیا کہ اس کے شوہر نے اس کو مرض الوفات میں جدا کیا اور شوہر فار ہے اس لئے عورت کو وراثت ملنی چاہئے اور شوہر کے ورثہ کہتے ہیں کہ تندرستی کی حالت میں طلاق دی تھی اس لئے وہ وارث نہیں ہے تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور وہ وارث ہوگی۔
اس ضابطہ سے کنز کا وہ مسئلہ جو قضاء کے مسائل شتی میں سے ہے خارج ہے۔
And if someone ripped open a garment and found a dead mouse in it and did not know when it entered, then if there is no hole, he repeats the prayer from the day he put the cotton in it; and if there is a hole, he repeats from three days. And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) acted upon this rule, so they ruled regarding the well that if a dead mouse is found in it, it is considered impure from the time of discovery without repeating anything, because its falling is a new event, so it is attributed to the nearest time. And the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) differed: he deemed it commendable to repeat prayers of three days if it is swollen or decomposed, otherwise from one day and one night, acting on the apparent cause and avoiding the hypothetical, out of precaution, like the wounded person who remained bedridden until death, it is attributed to the wound. ... And from this rule: if a man has a slave in his hand, and another man says, 'I put out his eye while he was in the seller's ownership,' and the buyer says, 'You put it out while he was in my ownership,' then the buyer's statement is accepted, and he takes the compensation. And from it: a wife claimed that her husband divorced her during illness and became a 'farr' (fleeing from inheritance), so she should inherit; and the heirs said he divorced her in health, so she does not inherit; her statement is accepted, so she inherits. And an exception to this principle is the issue of the treasure from various judiciary matters.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi legal maxim: an event is attributed to the nearest possible time. The text first gives an example: a garment with a mouse. If no hole, the mouse likely entered when the cotton was placed; if a hole, it could have entered anytime within three days. The Sahibayn strictly apply the maxim: in a well, contamination is from discovery only, no past prayer repetition. Imam Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: if the mouse shows signs of being there longer (swollen), he requires repetition for three days; otherwise one day. This is precautionary, preferring the apparent cause over the hypothetical. The passage then applies the maxim to two other cases: (1) a slave's eye injury disputed between seller and buyer—the event is attributed to the buyer's ownership (the nearest time), so he gets compensation. (2) A wife claims divorce in terminal illness to inherit; heirs claim in health. The maxim favors the wife because the event (divorce) is nearer to death. Finally, an exception is noted: the 'treasure' case from judiciary matters where the rule does not apply.

Key Terms
الفار (al-fār): A dead mouse found in a garment or well, causing impurity.
الإرش (al-arsh): Compensation for a defect caused to a slave's body part.
الفار بالطلاق (al-fār bi-l-talāq): A husband who divorces his wife during terminal illness to exclude her from inheritance.
الكنز (al-kanz): Treasure; an exception to the maxim in judiciary matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the divorce case from the passage, whose statement is accepted and why?
A) The heirs' statement is accepted because they are more numerous.
B) The wife's statement is accepted because the event (divorce) is attributed to the nearest time (illness) by the maxim.
C) The court decides based on witnesses, not the maxim.
D) The wife's statement is accepted only if she provides two male witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The maxim attributes events to the nearest possible time, but istihsan and apparent signs can override the default, and there is an exception for the treasure case.

Exception to Attributing Event to Nearest Time: Dhimmi's Wife
Application of the maxim with an exception based on present circumstance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' and identify when Tahkim al-Hal overrides it.

Core Idea
An event is attributed to its nearest time unless the present circumstance demands otherwise – Tahkim al-Hal can override the maxim.

This lesson examines a classic furua (subsidiary case) from the Hanafi legal maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' (attributing an event to its nearest possible time). The case involves a dhimmi's wife who claims she converted after his death, while the heirs say she converted before. This case demonstrates a critical exception: when the present circumstance (Tahkim al-Hal) indicates a cause of deprivation (difference of religion) exists at the time of death, the maxim is overridden. We will explore the reasoning behind this exception and the ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its general application
The maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' means that when the time of an event is uncertain, it is attributed to the most recent possible time. In our case, if the wife's conversion is uncertain, the maxim would attribute it to after the husband's death (the nearest time), making her a non-Muslim at his death and thus eligible to inherit? Actually, in Hanafi law, a non-Muslim wife inherits from a dhimmi. So the maxim would favor the wife.
The maxim is a standard tool in Hanafi qawaid.
2
Identify the furua (subsidiary case) and the ikhtilaf
The case: a dhimmi dies. His wife says she converted after his death; the heirs say she converted before. According to the maxim, the wife's claim should be accepted (event attributed to nearest time after death). Imam Zufar held this opinion. However, the majority of Hanafis (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) accepted the heirs' claim, contrary to the maxim.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school (Zufar vs. jumhur).
3
Understand the exception: Tahkim al-Hal
The majority justified departing from the maxim due to Tahkim al-Hal (considering the present circumstance). The present circumstance is that at the time of death, there is a cause of deprivation (difference of religion) – the wife is a Muslim (as claimed by the heirs) and the husband was a dhimmi, so she does not inherit. Because this cause is established in the present (the wife is now Muslim), it is considered established for the past as well, meaning she must have converted before death.
Tahkim al-Hal gives weight to observable present facts over inferential attribution.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference) mechanism
The jumhur overrode the maxim because the present circumstance (existing difference of religion) is considered stronger evidence than the presumption of attributing to the nearest time. The principle 'Tahkim al-Hal' acts as a restricting (dabt) maxim on the first maxim.
The mufta bihi is the jumhur position.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider a case where a person testifies that he saw a woman commit a crime yesterday, but the woman claims she was in another city. Which maxim applies? The maxim of attributing event to nearest time may not apply if the present circumstance (her being seen elsewhere today) contradicts. Tahkim al-Hal would be used.
This demonstrates the broader scope of the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كنز كا وہ مسئلہ جو قضاء کے مسائل شتی سے اور اس ضابطہ یعنی اضافة الحادث إلى اقرب أوقاته سے فارق ہے اس کی مثال یہ ہے۔
وَإِنَّ مَاتَ ذِمِّيٌّ فَقَالَتِ زَوْجَتُهُ أَسْلَمْتُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ وَ قَالَتِ الْوَرَثَةُ أَسْلَمْتُ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُمْ مَعْ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ الْمَذْكُورَ يَقْتَضِى أَنْ يَكُوْنَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَهَا وَبِهِ قَالَ زُفَةٌ وَ إِنَّمَا خَرَجُوْا عَنْ هَذِهِ الْقَاعِدَةِ فِيْهَا لِأَجْلِ تَحْكِيمِ الْحَالِ وَهُوَ أَنَّ سَبَبَ الْحِرْمَانِ ثَابِتٌ فِي
الْحَالِ فَيَثْبُتُ فِيْمَا مَضى.
مثلا ذمی کا انتقال ہوا ذمی کے انتقال کے بعد اس کی بیوی یہ کہتی ہے کہ جس وقت میرے شوہر ڈمی کا انتقال ہوا میں بھی اس وقت زمیں تھی اور اسلام قبول نہیں کیا تھا جبکہ ذمی کے ورثہ یہ کہہ رہے ہیں کہ تو پہلے ہی اسلام قبول کر چکی تھی تو اس ضابطہ کے تحت عورت کا قول معتبر ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ وہ اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب ہے امام زفری کے قائل ہیں، جبکہ جمہور احناف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں شوہر کے ورثہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ دوسرے قاعدے کے پیش نظر اور وہ ہے تحکیم حال یعنی عورت کے وراثت سے محروم ہونے کا سبب اختلاف دینین ہے جو اس وقت موجودتھا جب شوہر کا انتقال ہوا اسی اختلاف دینین کو محوظ رکھتے ہوئے کہا جائے گا کہ وہ عورت اس ذمی کے مرنے سے پہلے مسلمان ہو گئی تھی ہاں اگر عورت بعینہ پیش کر دے تو اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی۔
This is the issue from Kanz that is distinguished from miscellaneous matters of qada and from this rule (attributing the event to the nearest of its times). Its example is: If a dhimmi dies and his wife says, 'I became Muslim after his death,' and the heirs say, 'She became Muslim before his death,' then the word is theirs (the heirs'), even though the aforementioned principle would require that her word be taken, and Zufar said that. They only departed from this rule in this case for the sake of considering the present circumstance, which is that the cause of deprivation is established in the present, so it is established for the past. For example, a dhimmi passed away. After his death, his wife says that at the time of her husband's death she was also a dhimmi and had not accepted Islam, whereas the dhimmi's heirs say she had already accepted Islam before. According to this rule, the woman's word should be accepted because it is attributed to the nearest time. Imam Zufar holds this. However, the majority of Hanafis say that in this case the word of the husband's heirs is accepted, due to another principle: considering the present circumstance (tahkim al-hal). That is, the reason for her deprivation from inheritance is difference of religion, which existed at the time of the husband's death. Preserving this difference of religion, it will be said that she became Muslim before the dhimmi's death. Yes, if the woman brings clear evidence (bayyina), then her word will be accepted.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents a furua (application) of the Hanafi legal maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' (attributing an event to its nearest possible time). The maxim generally states that when an event occurs at an uncertain time, it should be assigned to the most recent possible time. Here, a dhimmi dies, and his widow claims she converted after his death (so she remains a non-Muslim at his death and inherits from him? Actually, a non-Muslim wife inherits from a dhimmi husband in Hanafi law? Wait, the issue is whether she inherits at all. The text says 'سبب الحرمان' (cause of deprivation) is difference of religion. So if she converted after his death, she is a Muslim but he died as dhimmi, so she does not inherit because she was a non-Muslim at his death? Actually, the ruling is: if she says she converted after his death, she would inherit? The principle would attribute her conversion to the nearest time, which is after death, so she would be a Muslim at death? No, the principle attributes the conversion to the nearest time, which is after death, meaning she was still a non-Muslim at death. That would make her ineligible to inherit. But the majority of Hanafis say the heirs' claim that she converted before death is accepted, meaning she is a Muslim at death, so she does not inherit (since a Muslim does not inherit from a non-Muslim). So the principle would favor the wife (if we attribute conversion to after death, she inherits), but the majority departs from the principle due to tahkim al-hal: the present circumstance is that there is a cause of deprivation (difference of religion) at the time of death, so they rule that she converted before death, thus she does not inherit. Imam Zufar adhered to the principle. This shows that the maxim has an exception when the present circumstance indicates a different attribution.

Key Terms
إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته (Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih): A legal maxim meaning that an event of uncertain time is attributed to the most recent possible time.
تحكيم الحال (Tahkim al-Hal): Considering the present circumstance as evidence for the past; using the current state to determine what happened earlier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a dhimmi's death, why do the majority of Hanafis accept the heirs' claim that the wife converted before death, contrary to the maxim of attributing the event to the nearest time?
A) Because the heirs have direct evidence
B) Because of the principle of considering the present circumstance (tahkim al-hal)
C) Because the wife is lying
D) Because the maxim only applies to financial transactions

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' is not absolute; it is overridden by 'Tahkim al-Hal' when the present circumstance establishes a cause of deprivation.

Acknowledgment for Heir: Attributing to Nearest Time
Application of the maxim to a deathbed acknowledgment dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' to resolve disputes in acknowledgment during illness and identify the evidentiary rules that accompany it.

Core Idea
Attributing an event to its nearest time gives precedence to the heirs' claim of illness over health.

This lesson examines the application of the Hanafi legal maxim 'Attributing an event to its nearest possible time' to a specific case: a person on their deathbed acknowledges a debt or right for one of their heirs. The dispute arises when the beneficiary claims the acknowledgment was made in health (full enforceability) while the heirs claim it was made during the deathbed illness (limited to will rules). The maxim provides a clear resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core maxim
State the maxim: 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' (Attributing an event to its nearest time). Understand its purpose: to resolve temporal ambiguity by assuming the most recent possible time.
2
Analyze the scenario
A person (al-muqir) acknowledges for his heir (al-muqar lahu) then dies. Beneficiary claims health; heirs claim illness. Which time should be attached to the acknowledgment?
The acknowledgment is the 'event' (hadith) in question.
3
Apply the maxim
Apply the maxim: the event is attributed to the nearest time. Since death is the most recent, the nearest possible time for the acknowledgment is the deathbed illness. Therefore, the heirs' claim is accepted.
This is because the deathbed illness is the closest time before death.
4
Determine evidentiary rules
The beneficiary may still prove his claim with evidence (bayyina). If no evidence, he can demand an oath from the heirs. The evidence of the beneficiary is given weight because he claims an extra right (enforceability in health).
This balances the maxim with the principle of evidence.
5
Extract the practical ruling
Extract the mufta bihi ruling: When there is a dispute without evidence, the heirs' word prevails; if the beneficiary brings evidence, his evidence is accepted; he may also administer an oath.
This shows the interaction between the maxim and procedural law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِمَّا فَرَّعَتُهُ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ مَا فِي الْيَتِيْمَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا وَلَوْ أَقَرَّ الوَارِتُ ثُمَّ مَاتَ فَقَالَ الْمُقِرُّلَهُ أَقَرَّ فِي الصَّحَّةِ وَقَالَتِ الْوَرَثَةُ فِي مَرَضِهِ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الْوَرَثَةِ وَالْبَيِّنَةُ بَيْنَةُ الْمَقِرلَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُقِمْ بَيْنَتَهُ وَأَرَادَ إِسْتِحْلَافَهُمْ فَلَهُ ذَلِكَ إِنْتَهَى.
ترجمہ: اور اسی قاعدہ پر میں نے وہ مسئلہ نکالا ہے جو یتیمہ وغیرہ میں ہے اگر وارث کے لئے اقرار کیا پھر مر گیا مقرلہ نے کہا صحت میں اقرار کیا تھا اور ورثہ نے کہتے ہیں اپنے مرض میں اقرار کیا تھا تو قول ورثہ کا ہوگا ور مینہ مقرل کا ہو اگر مقر لہ بینہ قائم نہ کر سکا اور ورثہ سے قسم لینا چاہے تو ان سے حلف لے سکتا ہے
تشریح کسی شخص نے اپنے وارث کے لئے اقرار کیا اور مرگیا تو مقرلہ کہتا ہے کہ حالت صحت میں فرار کیا تھا جبکہ ورثاء کہتے ہیں کہ حالت مرض میں اقرار کیا تھا ورثاء کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ ورثاء کا قول اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب ہے۔
And from what I have branched off from the principle is what is in al-Yatimah and others: If a person acknowledges for an heir and then dies, and the beneficiary says, 'He acknowledged in health,' and the heirs say, 'He acknowledged in his illness,' then the word is the word of the heirs. The evidence (bayyina) is for the beneficiary. If he does not bring his evidence and wants to administer an oath to them, he may do so. End. Commentary: A person acknowledged for his heir and died; the beneficiary says he acknowledged in health, while the heirs say he acknowledged in illness. The heirs' word will be accepted because their word is attributed to the nearest time.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This is a second furua (application) of the maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih'. A person makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) for one of his heirs, then dies. The beneficiary claims the acknowledgment was made in health (so it is valid and enforceable from the estate before division), while the heirs claim it was made during the deathbed illness (marad al-mawt), which would make it subject to the law of wills (only valid up to one-third of the estate). According to the maxim, the event (the acknowledgment) is attributed to the nearest time, which is the deathbed illness because that is the most recent possible time. Hence, the heirs' claim is accepted. However, if the beneficiary produces evidence (bayyina) that it was in health, his evidence is accepted because he is claiming an extra right. If no evidence, he can request an oath from the heirs. This shows the maxim's application in inheritance and will-related cases.

Key Terms
اقرار (Iqrar): A legal acknowledgment of a right or debt, which can be made in health or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of an acknowledgment for an heir, when the beneficiary claims it was in health and the heirs claim illness, whose word is accepted according to the maxim?
A) The beneficiary
B) The heirs
C) The judge
D) The witnesses

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Idafat al-Hadith ila Aqrab Awqatih' resolves temporal disputes in inheritance-related acknowledgments by attributing the event to the nearest time, giving priority to the heirs' claim of illness.

Applying the Maxim: Conversion Timing and Inheritance
Application of the maxim to conversion timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Attributing an event to its nearest possible time' to determine the validity of a conversion claim in inheritance cases and explain why the heirs' statement prevails.

Core Idea
Attribution to the nearest time resolves conversion timing disputes in inheritance.

A Muslim husband dies leaving a Christian wife. She later converts to Islam and claims she converted before his death — which would entitle her to inherit. The heirs deny this, saying she converted after death. How does the Hanafi jurist resolve this? The maxim 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' (attributing an event to its nearest possible time) provides the key. In this lesson, we explore the application of this wusta (intermediate) maxim to the furua of inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event in dispute
The event is the wife's conversion to Islam. The timing is contested: before or after the husband's death?
The outcome determines inheritance rights.
2
Enumerate the possible times
There are two possibilities: the conversion occurred before death (wife's claim) or after death (heirs' claim). The maxim requires us to attribute the event to the nearest possible time.
Nearest here means the closest to the present moment of dispute.
3
Apply the maxim
Since the conversion is observed after death, the nearest time is after death. The maxim attributes the conversion to that time, unless there is evidence to the contrary. The heirs' claim aligns with the nearest time.
The wife bears the burden of proving an earlier conversion.
4
Derive the ruling
The wife's conversion is considered after death; she remains a non-Muslim at the moment of death. Therefore, she does not inherit from her Muslim husband. The heirs' statement is accepted.
This ruling is consistent with the principle of associating events with the closest possible time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِمَّا فَرَّعَتُهُ عَلَى هَذَا الْأَصْلِ قَوْلُهُمْ لَوْمَاتَ مُسْلِمٌ وَتَحْتَهُ نَصْرَانِيَّةٌ فَجَاءَتْ مُسْلِمَةٌ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ وَقَالَتْ أَسْلَمْتُ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ وَقَالَتِ الْوَرَثَةُ أَسْلَمْتُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُمْ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ فِي مَسَائِلَ شَى.
ترجمہ: اور اس قاعدہ پر یہ مسلہ بھی نکلا ہے کہ اگر مسلم مر گیا اس کے نکاح میں نصرانیہ ہے اسکی موت کے بعد اسلام کی حالت میں آئی اور کہا اس کی موت سے پہلے اسلام لائی اور ورثہ کہتے ہیں موت کے بعد اسلام لائی تو قول ورثہ کا ہوگا جیسے زیلعی نے مسائل شتی میں ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح کسی مسلم کے نکاح میں نصرانی عورت تھی اس کے انتقال کے بعد وہ اسلام لے آئی اس کے بعد وہ نصران یہ دعوی کرتی ہے کہ میں اس کی موت کے پہلے ہی اسلام لے آئی تھی جبکہ ورثاء کہتے ہیں کہ تو اس کی موت کے بعد اسلام لائی ہے تو اس صورت میں ورثاء کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ ان کا قول اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب ہے۔
And from what I have branched off from this principle is their saying: If a Muslim dies and under him is a Christian woman, then she comes (after his death) as a Muslim and says, 'I became Muslim before his death,' and the heirs say, 'She became Muslim after his death,' then the word is theirs (the heirs'), as al-Zayla'i mentioned in Masa'il Shatti. Commentary: A Muslim had a Christian wife; after his death she embraced Islam and then claimed that she had embraced Islam before his death, while the heirs say she embraced Islam after his death. In this case, the heirs' word is accepted because their word is attributed to the nearest time.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is a third furua (application) of the same maxim. A Muslim man dies leaving a Christian wife. After his death, she converts to Islam and claims she converted before his death. The heirs claim she converted after his death. The issue is inheritance: if she converted before his death, she might inherit? Actually, in Hanafi law, a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim and vice versa. Since the husband was Muslim and she was Christian at his death, she does not inherit. If she converted before his death, she would still not inherit because she was a non-Muslim at the time of his death? Wait, conversion during marriage: if a Christian wife converts to Islam before the husband's death, the marriage continues and she inherits as a Muslim wife. So her claim would entitle her to inheritance. The heirs claim she converted after death, so she remains non-Muslim at death and does not inherit. Applying the maxim, the event (conversion) is attributed to the nearest time, which is after death. Hence, the heirs' claim is accepted. This is consistent with the maxim.

Key Terms
نصرانية (Nasraniyya): A Christian woman, here a wife of a Muslim husband, whose conversion affects inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the heirs' claim prevail in the case of a Muslim husband with a Christian wife who converts after his death and claims she converted before?
A) Because the heirs have more witnesses
B) Because the maxim attributes the conversion to the nearest time (after death)
C) Because her conversion is invalid
D) Because she is lying

Key Takeaway
When the timing of a conversion is disputed, the maxim 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' attributes it to the nearest possible time, which in this case is after the husband's death, denying inheritance to the wife.

Exception to the Maxim: Judge's Statement After Dismissal
Exception to the maxim when a judge claims a past act after dismissal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the exception to the maxim of attributing an event to its nearest time when a dismissed judge's statement about a judicial act is contested, and identify the governing Hanafi legal principle.

Core Idea
A judge's post-dismissal claim of official action overrides temporal proximity because context negates liability.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement of the Hanafi legal maxim 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' (Attributing an event to its nearest possible time). The maxim generally requires that a recent event be ascribed to the closest moment in time. However, when a dismissed judge claims he took money as part of a judicial ruling, the authoritative Hanafi position accepts his statement as an exception. This exception is based on the judge attributing his action to a state of judicial authority, which is inconsistent with personal liability. This case illustrates how underlying legal context can override a presumptive temporal rule.

Guided Path
1
State the general maxim rule
Identify the maxim 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' and its typical application: events are presumed to have occurred at the nearest possible time. Understand its role in Hanafi fiqh as a presumptive rule.
The maxim is a wusta (intermediate) rank maxim.
2
Present the exceptional case
Here, a judge after dismissal says to a man, 'I took a thousand from you and gave it to Zaid, and I ruled it against you.' The man responds, 'You took it unjustly after dismissal.' The act is recent; according to the maxim, it should be attributed to the nearest time (dismissal), favoring the man.
The case involves a financial dispute between a former judge and a litigant.
3
Analyze the conflict between maxim and context
The maxim would reject the judge's later claim, but the judge attributes his action to his judicial capacity (a state inconsistent with liability). This creates a conflict: temporal proximity vs. context of official authority.
The judge's claim is that he acted as a judge, not as a wrongdoer.
4
Understand the tarjih reasoning
The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) awards the word to the judge. The reason: the judge's attribution to a state that negates liability (judicial authority) is given priority over the temporal maxim. The exception is thus established.
al-Sarakhsi preferred the maxim, but the majority view is the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِمَّا خَرَجَ عَنْ هَذَا الْأَصْلِ لَوْ قَالَ الْقَاضِي بَعْدَ عَزْلِهِ لِرَجُلٍ أَخَذْتُ مِنْكَ أَلْفَاً وَدَفَعْتُهَا إلَى زَيْدٍ قَضَيْتُ بِهَا عَلَيْكَ فَقَالَ أَخَذْتَهَا ظُلْماً بَعْدَ الْعَزْلِ فَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّ الْقَوْلَ لِلْقَاضِي مَع أَنَّ الْفِعْلَ حَادِتْ فَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُضَاف إلى أَقْرَبِ أَوْقَاتِهِ وَهُمْ وَقْتُ الْعَزْلِ وَبِهِ قَالَ الْبَعْضُ وَاخْتَارَهُ السَّرَحْسِى لَكِنَّ الْمُعْتَمِدَ الْأوْلُ لِأَنَّ الْقَاضِي أَسْنَدَهُ إِلَى حَالِةٍ منَا فِيّة لِلصَّمَان وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا زَعَمَ الْمَاخُوْذُ مِنْهُ أَنَّهُ فَعَلَهُ قَبْلَ تَقْلِيدِ الْقَضَاءِ.
ترجمه اور اس اصل سے وہ جزئیہ خارج ہے کہ اگر قاضی نے اپنے معزول ہو جانے کے بعد کسی آدمی سے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار روپے لیکر زید کو دئیے تھے اور اس کا میں نے تیرے خلاف فیصلہ کیا تھا اس پر اس آدمی نے کہا کہ تو نے وہ (ایک ہزار روپے) معزول ہو جانے کے بعد بطور ظلم لئے تھے تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ قاضی کا قول معتبر ہوگا حالانکہ وہ فعل حادث ہے تو مناسب تھا کہ اسے اس کے اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا اور وہ عزل کا وقت ہے چنانچہ بعض فقہاء اسی کے قائل ہیں اور علامہ سرخی نے اسی کو اختیار فرمایا ہے لیکن معتمد قول اول ہے اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس ( ایک ہزار) کو ایسی حالت کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جو ضمان کے منافی ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہے جب وہ شخص جس سے ایک ہزار روپے لئے گئے ہیں یہ گمان کرے کہ اس نے قاضی بنائے جانے سے پہلے اس سے لیکر اس کو دیئے ہیں۔
And from what is excluded from this principle: If the judge after his dismissal says to a man, 'I took a thousand from you and gave it to Zaid, and I ruled it against you,' and the man says, 'You took it unjustly after dismissal,' the correct view is that the word is the judge's, even though the act is recent and it would have been appropriate to attribute it to its nearest time, which is the time of dismissal. Some say this, and al-Sarakhsi chose it, but the relied-upon view is the first, because the judge attributed it to a state that is inconsistent with liability. And similarly if the person from whom the thousand was taken claims that he did it before appointment as judge. Commentary: This case is excluded from the principle. If a judge after his dismissal says to a man, 'I took a thousand from you and gave it to Zaid and gave judgment against you,' and the man says, 'You took it unjustly after dismissal,' the correct view is that the judge's statement is accepted, even though the act is recent and should be attributed to the nearest time (dismissal). Some jurists hold this view, and al-Sarakhsi chose it, but the relied-upon view is the first, because the judge attributes it to a state that negates liability. Similarly, if the person from whom the thousand was taken thinks that the judge did it before his appointment.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage presents an exception (istithna) to the maxim of attributing the event to the nearest time. A judge, after being dismissed, claims that during his tenure he took money from a man as a judgment. The man claims the judge took it unjustly after dismissal. According to the maxim, the event (taking) should be attributed to the nearest time, which is the dismissal (the act being recent), thus the man's claim would be preferred. However, the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is that the judge's word is accepted. The reason is that the judge attributes his action to a state of authority (judicial capacity) that is inconsistent with liability (i.e., he was acting as a judge, not unjustly). Some Hanafi scholars like al-Sarakhsi preferred the maxim, but the authoritative position is the exception. This shows that the maxim can be overridden when the context indicates a different legal characterization.

Key Terms
عزل (Azl): Dismissal from the position of judge; the time after removal from office.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a judge after dismissal, why is his statement about taking money during his tenure accepted over the maxim?
A) Because the judge is always truthful
B) Because he attributes the act to a state inconsistent with liability
C) Because the man's claim is weak
D) Because the maxim does not apply to judges

Key Takeaway
The maxim of temporal proximity is overridden when a judge's statement about an act during his tenure is made after dismissal, due to the context of judicial authority.
