6 min
Exception: Judge's Claim Overrides the Maxim of Temporal Proximity
Exception to the maxim: judge's claim of prior action is accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the exception to the maxim of attributing a recent event to its nearest time when a judge's claim of prior action is supported by the presumption of non-liability.

Core Idea
A judge's claim of lawful prior action is accepted over temporal proximity because it aligns with original non-liability.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a critical refinement to the established maxim that a new event is attributed to its nearest time. In the case of a dismissed judge, his claim that he took money during his tenure is accepted despite the recency of the event. The reasoning is based on the overriding principle of original non-liability (al-aṣl al-ʿadam), which gains precedence when the action is consistent with a prior state of authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim at stake
The general principle: a new event is attributed to its nearest possible time. Here, the taking of money is a new event occurring after dismissal; normally it would be attributed to the time of dismissal.
This maxim applies in many fiqh contexts, e.g., determining the time of a debt repayment.
2
Recognize the exception
The judge claims he took the money and passed judgment before dismissal. The correct view (الصحيح) accepts the judge's statement, contrary to the maxim.
Some jurists, including al-Sarakhsi, held the opposite view, but the relied-upon position is the first.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The judge attributes the act to a state (his tenure) that is inconsistent with liability (ضمان). During his tenure, he had authority to take and adjudicate; after dismissal, any taking is wrongful. The principle of original non-liability (al-ʿadam) supports his claim.
The principle of original non-liability is a stronger presumption than temporal proximity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some jurists, including al-Sarakhsi, chose the opposite view. But the relied-upon (المعتمد) is the first view because of the overriding presumption.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the first view.
5
Apply to the second scenario
Similarly, if the person claims the judge acted before his appointment, the same ruling applies: the judge's statement is authoritative if he attributes the action to a time of authority.
The same principle applies whether the claim is about a time before or after the tenure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِمَّا خَرَجَ عَنْ هَذَا الْأَصْلِ لَوْ قَالَ الْقَاضِي بَعْدَ عَزْلِهِ لِرَجُلٍ أَخَذْتُ مِنْكَ أَلْفَاً وَدَفَعْتُهَا إلَى زَيْدٍ قَضَيْتُ بِهَا عَلَيْكَ فَقَالَ أَخَذْتَهَا ظُلْماً بَعْدَ الْعَزْلِ فَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّ الْقَوْلَ لِلْقَاضِي مَع أَنَّ الْفِعْلَ حَادِتْ فَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُضَاف إلى أَقْرَبِ أَوْقَاتِهِ وَهُمْ وَقْتُ الْعَزْلِ وَبِهِ قَالَ الْبَعْضُ وَاخْتَارَهُ السَّرَحْسِى لَكِنَّ الْمُعْتَمِدَ الْأوْلُ لِأَنَّ الْقَاضِي أَسْنَدَهُ إِلَى حَالٍةٍ مَنَافِيَةٍ لِلصَّمَان وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا زَعَمَ الْمَاخُوْذُ مِنْهُ أَنَّهُ فَعَلَهُ قَبْلَ تَقْلِيدِ الْقَضَاءِ :ترجمه اور اس اصل سے وہ جزئیہ خارج ہے کہ اگر قاضی نے اپنے معزول ہو جانے کے بعد کسی آدمی سے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار روپے لیکر زید کو دئیے تھے اور اس کا میں نے تیرے خلاف فیصلہ کیا تھا اس پر اس آدمی نے کہا کہ تو نے وہ (ایک ہزار روپے) معزول ہو جانے کے بعد بطور ظلم لئے تھے تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ قاضی کا قول معتبر ہوگا حالانکہ وہ فعل حادث ہے تو مناسب تھا کہ اسے اس کے اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا اور وہ عزل کا وقت ہے چنانچہ بعض فقہاء اسی کے قائل ہیں اور علامہ سرخی نے اسی کو اختیار فرمایا ہے لیکن معتمد قول اول ہے اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس ( ایک ہزار) کو ایسی حالت کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جو ضمان کے منافی ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہے جب وہ شخص جس سے ایک ہزار روپے لئے گئے ہیں یہ گمان کرے کہ اس نے قاضی بنائے جانے سے پہلے اس سے لیکر اس کو دیئے ہیں۔
And from what is excepted from this principle: if a judge after his dismissal says to a man, 'I took a thousand from you and gave it to Zaid, and I passed a judgment against you regarding it,' and the man says, 'You took it unjustly after dismissal,' the correct view is that the judge's statement is authoritative, despite the fact that the action is new, so it should have been attributed to its nearest time, which is the time of dismissal. Some jurists hold this, and al-Sarakhsi chose it, but the relied-upon is the first because the judge attributed it to a state inconsistent with liability. Similarly, if the person from whom it was taken claims that he did it before the judge's appointment.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is an exception to the general maxim of attributing a recent event to its nearest time. The judge's claim is accepted because he attributes the action to a time when he had authority (his tenure), which is inconsistent with liability for wrongful taking. The principle of original non-liability (al-aṣl al-ʿadam) overrides the maxim. The position of al-Sarakhsi is noted but the relied-upon view is the first.

Key Terms
الاصل العدم (al-aṣl al-ʿadam): The original presumption is non-existence of liability.
المعتمد (al-muʿtamad): The relied-upon or preferred view within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the judge's statement accepted in the exception despite the event being recent?
A) Because the judge is inherently truthful.
B) Because he attributes the action to a state inconsistent with liability.
C) Because the event is not considered new.
D) Because the maxim does not apply to judges.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of original non-liability can override the maxim of temporal proximity when the claimant attributes the action to a state (such as a judge's tenure) that makes it lawful.

Exceptions to the Attribution Maxim: Slave, Master, and Agent Cases
Further exceptions to the maxim in agency and status disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of original non-liability (al-aṣl al-ʿadam) to determine whose statement is authoritative in disputes over timing of events involving slave status, master's collection, and agent's authority.

Core Idea
When timing of an event is disputed, the party whose claim aligns with original non-liability is believed, overriding the normal attribution-to-nearest-time maxim.

This lesson examines three exceptions to the maxim that events are attributed to the nearest time. In each case, a stronger presumption—that of original non-liability—tips the balance. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for a mufti to navigate conflicting claims in agency and status disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
For each case, identify the two conflicting claims about timing: one party asserts the event occurred while a certain status (slavery, agency) was in effect; the other claims it occurred after that status ended.
2
Identify the default ruling from the general maxim
The general maxim 'al-umūr tunazzalu ʿalā aqrab al-awqāt' would normally attribute the event to the nearest time, which would favor the party claiming the event happened later (e.g., after freedom or after dismissal).
Focus on what the maxim would dictate without exceptions.
3
Identify the overriding principle
Recognize that the principle of original non-liability (al-aṣl al-ʿadam) overrides the general maxim. Each party's claim is checked against the default state of non-liability: a slave is not liable for full damages, a master is not presumed to have taken money after freeing, an agent is not presumed to have acted after dismissal.
The stronger principle here is that the status quo ante (e.g., slavery, authority) is assumed until proven otherwise.
4
Apply the exception to each case
In the slave case, the former slave's claim of being a slave at the time of injury is accepted because he would otherwise be liable. In the master case, the master's claim of taking during slavery is accepted because the freed slave would otherwise have a claim. In the agent case, if the sold item is consumed, the agent's claim is accepted; if it exists, the principal's claim prevails because the goods can be returned.
The agent case has a nuance based on the possibility of restitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَخَرَجَ أَيْضاً عَنْهُ مَالَوْ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ بِغَيْرِهِ بَعْدَ الْعِلْقِ قَطَعْتُ يَدِكَ وَ أَنَا عَبْدٌ وَقَالَ الْمُقَولُهُ بَلْ قَطَعْتَهَا وَأَنْتَ حَرٌّ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ لَلْعَبْدِ وَكَذَا لَوْ قَالَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ وَقَدْ أَعْتَقَهُ أَخَذْتُ مِنْكَ عَلَّةَ كُلِّ شَهْرٍ خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَأَنْتَ عَبْدَ فَقَالَ الْمُعْتَقُ أَخَذْتَهَا بَعْدَ الْعِلْقِ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ الْمَوْلَى وَكَذَا الْوَكِيْلُ بِالْبَيْعِ إِذَا قَالَ بِعْتُ وَ سَلَّمْتُ قَبْلَ الْعَزْلِ وَقَالَ الْمَوَكَّلُ بَعْدَ الْعَزْلِ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ لِلْوَكِيْلِ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَبِيْعُ مُسْتَهْلَكَا وَإِنْ كَانَ قَائِمَا فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الْمُوَكَّلِ وَكَذَا فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْغَلَّة لَا يُصْدُّقُ فِي الْغَلَّةِ الْقَائِمَةِ .
And also excepted from it: if a slave after emancipation says to someone, 'I cut off your hand while I was a slave,' and the person says, 'Rather you cut it while you were free,' the slave's statement is authoritative. Likewise, if the master says to his slave after freeing him, 'I took from you for every month five dirhams while you were a slave,' and the freed slave says, 'You took them after emancipation,' the master's statement is authoritative. And likewise, if the agent for sale says, 'I sold and delivered before dismissal,' and the principal says, 'After dismissal,' the agent's statement is authoritative if the sold item is consumed; if it is still in existence, the principal's statement is authoritative. And similarly in the case of produce (ghallah), he is not believed regarding existing produce.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
These are further exceptions to the maxim of attributing events to the nearest time. In each case, the party claiming a state inconsistent with liability (e.g., slave status, agent authority) is given precedence because of the principle of original non-liability. The slave's claim of being a slave at the time of injury exempts him from full liability as a free person would have. The master's claim of taking during slavery avoids returning the money. The agent's claim of sale before dismissal is accepted if the goods are consumed, as returning them is impossible; if they exist, the principal's claim that the sale was unauthorized stands. This shows that the maxim is flexible and gives way to other principles.

Key Terms
الأصل براءة الذمة (al-aṣl barā'atu al-dhimmah): The principle that a person's liability is originally absent; they are free from obligation until proven otherwise.
تنزل الأمور على أقرب الأوقات (tunazzalu al-umūr ʿalā aqrab al-awqāt): The maxim that matters are attributed to the nearest time, used in determining the timing of events.
العلقة (al-ʿilq): Emancipation, the act of freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between an agent and principal about the timing of a sale, when is the agent's statement accepted?
A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if the sold item is consumed
D) Only if the principal agrees

Key Takeaway
The attribution maxim is overridden by the principle of original non-liability in disputes over timing when one party's claim aligns with the default legal status.

Maxim of Attribution to Nearest Time and Its Exceptions
Explaining the maxim and its exceptions with applied cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'idafat al-hadith ila aqrab awqatih' to given scenarios and identify when it is overridden by principles such as al-asl al-'adam, bara'at al-dhimma, and qawl al-amin.

Core Idea
The maxim yields to stronger presumptions: non-liability, innocence, and trustee's word.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents the Hanafi maxim that when a disputed event could have occurred at multiple times, we attribute it to the most recent possible time. However, the author immediately provides several exceptions where other procedural principles override this maxim. Understanding when and why these exceptions apply is crucial for a mufti evaluating conflicting claims in torts, contracts, and emancipation.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its default rule
Identify the maxim 'إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' (attribute event to nearest time). This means when two parties dispute the time of an event, the one who claims the more recent time is believed, because the event is presumed to have occurred at the nearest possible time.
This is a procedural presumption in evidence, not a substantive rule.
2
Analyze the first set of exceptions (slave and master cases)
Read the examples of the slave after emancipation and the master claiming rent. Note how in each case the maxim is not applied; instead, the party denying liability is believed. Identify which overriding principle applies: for the slave, it is 'al-asl al-'adam' (presumption of non‑existence of liability); for the master, it is 'bara'at al-dhimma' (presumption of innocence of the defendant).
In both exceptions, the 'nearest time' would favour the other party, but the denial of liability is given priority.
3
Examine the agency cases
Consider the agent for sale: if the agent claims he sold before revocation and the principal says after, the outcome depends on whether the sold item is consumed or still exists. When consumed, the agent's word is accepted due to 'qawl al-amin' (trustee's word is believed). When the item exists, the principal's word is accepted because the claim can be verified by returning the item.
This shows that the applicability of the maxim can shift based on factual circumstances (existence vs. consumption).
4
Contrast with the case from al-Nihayah (freed female slave)
This case tailwith the maxim, unlike the earlier slave case where the maxim was excepted. The distinction lies in the nature of the claim: the female slave is not denying liability (she is seeking compensation), so the presumption of non‑liability does not apply.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute and the relied-upon position
Note that Imam Muhammad disagrees with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the female slave case. He analogizes to the earlier slave case, arguing that slavery is a barrier to liability. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, as in al-Nihayah, is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. A mufti must know this tarjih.
The dispute shows how nuanced application of maxims requires understanding underlying ratios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَخَرَجَ أَيْضاً عَنْهُ مَالَوْ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ بِغَيْرِهِ بَعْدَ الْعِلْقِ قَطَعْتُ يَدِكَ وَ أَنَا عَبْدٌ وَقَالَ الْمُقَولُهُ بَلْ قَطَعْتَهَا وَأَنْتَ حَرٌّ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ لَلْعَبْدِ وَكَذَا لَوْ قَالَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ وَقَدْ أَعْتَقَهُ أَخَذْتُ مِنْكَ عَلَّةَ كُلِّ شَهْرٍ خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَأَنْتَ عَبْدَ فَقَالَ الْمُعْتَقُ أَخَذْتَهَا بَعْدَ الْعِلْقِ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ الْمَوْلَى وَكَذَا الْوَكِيْلُ بِالْبَيْعِ إِذَا قَالَ بِعْتُ وَ سَلَّمْتُ قَبْلَ الْعَزْلِ وَقَالَ الْمَوَكَّلُ بَعْدَ الْعَزْلِ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ لِلْوَكِيْلِ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَبِيْعُ مُسْتَهْلَكَا وَإِنْ كَانَ قَائِمَا فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الْمُوَكَّلِ وَكَذَا فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْغَلَّة لَا يُصْدُّقُ فِي الْغَلَّةِ الْقَائِمَةِ . وَمِمَّا وَافَقَ الْأَصْلُ مَا فِى الْنِهَايَةِ لَوْ اعْتَقَ أَمَةً ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهَا قَطَعْتُ يَدَكِ وَأَنْتَ أَمَتِي فَقَالَتْ هِيَ قَطَعْتَهَا وَأَنَا حُرَّةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهَا وَكَذَا فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ أَخَذَهُ مِنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةً وَأَبِي يُوسُفٌ ذَكَرَهُ قُبِيْلَ الشَّهَادَاتِ وَتَحْتَاجُ هَذِهِ الْمَسَائِلُ إِلَى نَظْرٍ دَقِيْقِ لِلْفَرْقِ بَيْنَهَا.
And there also falls outside it (the maxim) that if a slave after emancipation said to another: 'I cut your hand while I was a slave' and the person whose hand was cut said: 'Rather, you cut it while you were free,' the word is that of the slave. Likewise, if the master said to his slave after he had emancipated him: 'I took from you a monthly payment of five dirhams while you were a slave' and the freed slave said: 'You took it after emancipation,' the word is that of the master. Likewise, the agent for sale, if he said: 'I sold and delivered before revocation' and the principal said: 'After revocation,' the word is that of the agent if the sold item has been consumed; if it still exists, the word is that of the principal. Likewise, in the case of produce (ghalla): he is not believed regarding existing produce. And among what agrees with the original principle is what is in al-Nihayah: if a man emancipated a female slave then said to her: 'I cut your hand while you were my slave' and she said: 'You cut it while I was free,' the word is hers; likewise, regarding everything he took from her according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. He mentioned it before the chapter on testimonies. And these cases require precise scrutiny to differentiate between them.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi legal maxim 'attribute an event to its nearest possible time' (إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته). The author presents several furuat (applications) where this maxim is either excepted or confirmed. The first set of cases shows exceptions where the maxim is not applied because another principle takes precedence: the presumption of non-existence of liability (الأصل العدم) or the trustworthiness of the agent (قول الأمين). For instance, if a slave after emancipation admits to cutting off someone's hand but claims it happened while he was a slave, and the victim claims it was after emancipation, the slave's statement is credited. This is because the slave is denying guarantee (ضمان) in the sense that a slave's actions do not create liability for him (since property belongs to master). The nearest time (emancipation) would favor the victim, but the presumption of non-liability overrides. Similarly, when a master claims he took monthly rent from the slave while slave, and the freed slave claims it was after emancipation, the master's word is accepted because the master is denying the need to return the rent again (he is the defendant). In agency cases, if the agent claims he sold before revocation and the principal says after, the agent's word is credited if the item is consumed (because the agent is trusted, and the principal is claiming liability), but if the item still exists, the principal's word is accepted (since the item can be returned). For agricultural produce, a similar rule applies: if the produce is consumed, the claimant is believed; if it still exists, he is not believed. The second part presents a case from al-Nihayah that tailwith the maxim: a master frees a female slave then claims he cut her hand while she was a slave; she says after freedom. Here, the nearest time is freedom, so her word is accepted, making the master liable. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf extend this to everything he took from her. This case aligns with the maxim and contrasts with the first slave case. The author notes these cases require careful study to understand the distinctions.

Key Terms
إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته (Idafat al-hadith ila aqrab awqatih): A legal presumption that when a disputed event could have occurred at multiple times, it is attributed to the most recent possible time.
الأصل العدم (al-asl al-'adam): Presumption that something did not happen or does not exist; used to deny liability when the defendant denies the claim.
براءة الذمة (bara'at al-dhimma): Presumption of innocence from any liability; the defendant's word is accepted unless plaintiff proves otherwise.
قول الأمين (qawl al-amin): The word of a trustee is accepted regarding the subject of trust, unless there is evidence to the contrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of an agent for sale who claims he sold the item before being revoked, and the principal claims it was sold after revocation, the agent's word is accepted if:
A) The sold item has been consumed
B) The sold item is still in existence
C) The principal admits the agency
D) The agent has witnesses

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'attribute to nearest time' is a procedural presumption that yields to stronger principles when the denying party is a defendant or a trustee, and its application depends on the procedural roles and factual circumstances.

Applying Aqrab al-Awqat: Sick Slave and Umm Walad
Furu' applications of the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim of Aqrab al-Awqat to resolve uncertainty in timing and identify cases where a different principle (paternity and ownership) overrides it.

Core Idea
The maxim 'Aqrab al-Awqat' attributes an event to the nearest time, but paternity and ownership can override it.

This passage presents two branches (furu') derived from the maxim that an event is attributed to the nearest possible time (Aqrab al-Awqat). The first case involves a sick slave: the buyer cannot reclaim the full price because death is attributed to the aggravation of the illness after purchase. The second case involves a slave-girl who becomes umm walad after being purchased by her former husband; interestingly, this ruling is not based on the maxim, but on paternity established through marriage and subsequent ownership. Understanding when the maxim governs and when it is overridden by other principles is crucial for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and list the two scenarios described: (1) buying a sick slave who later dies, (2) marrying a slave-girl, buying her, and then she gives birth at an uncertain time.
Both involve uncertainty about the timing of an event.
2
Apply the maxim to the sick slave
Explain why the buyer cannot reclaim the full price. The death is attributed to the increase in illness after purchase, not to the pre-existing defect. The maxim attributes the event (death) to the nearest cause (the aggravated illness), not the earlier one.
The maxim resolves the uncertainty: the latest possible cause is chosen.
3
Analyze the umm walad case
Note that the maxim is explicitly stated NOT to apply here. Even if the child was born before purchase, the slave-girl becomes umm walad. The ruling is based on paternity (nasab) from the marriage and removal of the impediment of ownership.
The maxim is overridden because paternity and ownership provide a definitive basis.
4
Distinguish the principles
Contrast the illa (cause) in each case. In the sick slave, the cause is uncertain timing of death; the maxim resolves it. In the umm walad, the cause is certain paternity; the maxim is irrelevant.
The maxim applies only when there is no other established cause.
5
Formulate the mufti's guide
Summarize: When encountering uncertainty about timing, first check if another principle (e.g., paternity, ownership) definitively establishes the ruling. If not, apply Aqrab al-Awqat.
This prevents misapplication.

Source Text

وَمِمَّا فَرَّعَ عَلَيْهِ لَوْ اشْتَرى عَبْداً ثم ظهر أنَّهُ كَانَ مَرِيضًا وَمَاتَ عِنْدَ الْمُشْتَرِي فَأَنَّهُ لا يَرْجِعُ بِالثَّمَن لانَّ الْمَرْضَ يتزايد فَيَحْضُلُ الْمَوْتُ بِالزَّائِدِ فَلَا أَوْقَاتِه لأَنَّهَا لَوْ وَلَدَتْ قَبْلَ الشِّرَاءِ ثُمَّ مَلَكَهَا تَصِيْرُ أُمَّ وَلَدِهِ عِنْدَنَا ترجمه اس قاعدہ کی جزئیات میں وہ صورت نہیں کہ جب کسی نے کسی باندی سے نکاح کیا پھراتے خرید لیا پھر اس (باندی) کے بچہ ہوا تو احتمال ہے کہ وہ (وجود حمل ) خریدنے کے بعد ہوا ہو یا خرید نے سے پہلے ہوا ہو تو ہمارے نزدیک وہ بلا شبہ ام ولد ہو جائے گی اس وجہ سے نہیں کہ یہ ( وجود حمل ) امر حادث ہے جس کی نسبت سے ثابت ہو چکا ہے اس لئے نسب کے واسطے سے جزئیت ثابت ہوگئی ولادت کے وقت میں غیر کا مملوک ہونا ثبوت نسب کے لئے مانع تھا خرید لینے سے مانع زائل ہو گیا۔
And from what is derived from it: If one buys a slave and it later appears that he was sick and he dies with the buyer, he does not return the price because illness increases and death occurs by the increase, so it is not attributed to the earlier state, but he reclaims [the amount of] the defect, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. Translation: ... [Urdu commentary] ... And it is not from its furu' the case when one marries a slave-girl, then buys her, then she gives birth to a child that could have occurred after the purchase or before it; then there is no doubt with us that she becomes umm walad, not from the aspect that it is a new event attributed to the nearest time, because if she gave birth before the purchase and then he owned her, she becomes his umm walad with us. Translation: ... [Urdu commentary] ...
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage expands on the legal maxim that events are attributed to the nearest possible time. Two furu' (branches) are presented. First: If a slave is bought while ill and later dies, the buyer cannot reclaim the full price because the death is attributed to the aggravation of the illness after purchase, not the pre-existing defect. However, he may claim compensation for the diminution in value due to the defect (the difference between the price of a healthy and defective slave). Second: If a man marries a slave-girl, then buys her, and she gives birth at an uncertain time (before or after the purchase), she becomes his umm walad (mother of his child) even if the child was conceived before purchase. This is not because of the 'nearest time' principle, but because paternity is established from the marriage, and once he owns her, the impediment of her being owned by another is removed, so she becomes umm walad. The reasoning is that the connection (juz'iyya) is established through the child whose lineage is proven from the husband.

Key Terms
أَقْرَبَ الْأَوْقَاتِ (aqrab al-awqat): The principle that an event is attributed to the nearest possible time when there is uncertainty about its occurrence.
أُمَّ وَلَدٍ (umm walad): A slave-girl who has borne a child to her master, thus gaining certain rights and becoming free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of buying a sick slave who later dies, why does the buyer not get a full refund?
A) Because death is attributed to the aggravation of the illness after purchase.
B) Because the buyer was aware of the illness.
C) Because the seller is not liable after sale.
D) Because the slave died at the buyer's place.

Key Takeaway
The maxim Aqrab al-Awqat governs timing uncertainty, but it is overridden when a definitive cause like paternity and ownership is present.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Maxim: Original Rule in Private Parts is Prohibition
States a qawida and its applications to forgotten manumission and divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-asl fi al-abda' al-tahrim' to identify when taharri is prohibited and construct a fatwa for cases of forgotten manumission or divorce.

Core Idea
Private parts are originally prohibited; doubt does not allow estimation.

This lesson explores a crucial Hanafi qawida: the original rule concerning private parts is prohibition. This maxim restricts the general principle of permissibility in matters of marriage, divorce, and sexual relations. We will see how it applies to cases of forgotten manumission and divorce, and why taharri (estimation) is absolutely forbidden in these domains.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim
Identify the qawida in Arabic and English: 'الأصل في الأبضاع التحريم' – the original rule concerning private parts is prohibition.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim that restricts the general maxim of permissibility.
2
Identify its Scope
Determine which areas of fiqh this maxim governs: nikah, talaq, and all matters of sexual relations. It overrides the general ibaha.
It does not apply to other matters like food or trade.
3
Work Through the Furuat
Analyze the three applications from the passage: case of forgotten manumission, forgotten triple divorce, and judge’s erroneous ruling. For each, explain why taharri is prohibited and what the judge must do.
Notice the pattern: uncertainty leads to complete prohibition until certainty is achieved.
4
Identify the Istithna
The only exception is marriage itself, which is permitted out of necessity for procreation. But this does not extend to taharri.
The exception is narrow: it allows the original contract, not speculative methods.
5
Apply to Fatwa
As a mufti, you must rule that taharri is invalid in private parts. In the given cases, the man must refrain from all women until the specific one is known; the judge must intervene and administer an oath.
This maxim is decisive and leaves no room for ijtihad by estimation.

قَاعِدَة : الأَصْلُ فِي الأَبْضَاعِ التَّحْرِيمُ وَ كَذَا قَالَ فِي كَشْفِ الْأَسْرَارِ شَرْحِ فَخْرِ الإِسْلَامِ الأصْلُ فِى النِّكَاحِ الْحَظَرُ وَابِيْحَ لِلضَّرُورَةِ انْتَهى . فَإِذَا تَقَابَلَ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ حِلٌّ وَ حُرْمَةٌ غُلبَتِ الْحُرْمَةُ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوْزُ التَّحَرِّى فِي الْفُرُوجِ وَفِيْ كَافِي الْحَاكِمِ الشَّهِيدِ مِنْ بَابِ التَّحَرِّى وَلَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا لَهُ أَرْبَعُ جَوَارِيَ أَعْتَقَ وَاحِدَةً مِّنْهُنَّ بِعَيْنِهَا ثُمَّ نَسِيَهَا فَلَمْ يَدْرٍ أَيَّتَهُنَّ أعْتَقَ لَمْ يَسَعُهُ أَنْ يَتَحَرَىٰ لِلْوَطِئ وَلَا لِلْبَيْعِ وَلَا يَسَعُ لِلْحَاكِمِ أَنْ يُخَلَّى بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُنَّ حَتى تَبَيَّنَ الْمُعْتَقَةُ مِنْ غَيْرِهَا وَ كَذَا إِذَا طَلَّقَ إِحْدَى نِسَائِهِ بِعَيْنِهَا ثَلَاثَاً ثُمَّ نَسِيَهَا وَكَذَا لِكَ إِنْ مَيَّزَ كُلَّهُنَّ إِلَّا وَاحِدَةً لَمْ يَسَعْهُ أَنْ يَقْرُبَهَا حَتَّى يَعْلَمَ أَنَّهَا غَيْرُ الْمُطَلَّقَةِ وَكَذَلِكَ يَمْنَعُهُ الْقَاضِي عَنْهَا حَتَّى يُخْبَرَ أَنَّهَا غَيْرُ الْمُطَلَّقَةِ فَإِذَا أَخْبَرَ بِذلِكَ إِسْتَحْلَفَهُ الْبَيَّةَ أَنَّهُ مَا طَلَّقَ هَذِهِ بِعَيْنِهَا ثَلمَّا ثُمَّ حَلَى بَيْنَهُمَا فَإِنْ كَانَ حَلَفَ وَهُوَ جَاهِلٌ بِهَا فَلَا يَنْبَغِي لَهُ أَنْ يَقْرُبَهَا. فَإِنْ بَاعَ فِي الْمَسْئَلَةِ الأولى ثلاثاً مِنَ الْجَوَارِي فَحَكَّمَ الْحَاكِمُ فَإِنْ أَجَازَ بَيْعَهُنَّ وَكَانَ ذلِكَ مِنْ رَائِهِ وَجَعَلَ الْبَاقِيَة هي المعلقة ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ بَعْضُ مَنْ بَاعَ بِشِرَاءٍ أَوْهِيَةٍ أَوْ مِيرَاتِ لَمْ يَنْبَغِ لَهُ أَنْ يَطَاهَا لأَنَّ الْقَاضِي قَضَى فِيْهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ فَلَا يَنْبَغِي لَهُ أَنْ يُطَا شَيْئاً مِنْهُنَّ بِالْمِلْكِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَرَوْجَهَا فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا بَأسَ لأَنَّهَا زَوْجَتُهُ أَوْ أَمَتَهُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحَرِّى في الفُرُوحِ لأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ فِي كُلِّ مَاجَازَ لِلضَّرُورَةِ وَالْفُرُوْجُ لَا تَحِلُّ بِالضَّرُورَةِ انْتَهَى ثُمَّ قَالَ وَلَوْ أَعْتَقَ جَارِيَةً مِنْ رَقِيقِهِ ثُمَّ نَسِيَهَا وَمَاتَ لَمْ يَجُزُ لِلْقَاضِي التَّحَرُى وَلَا يَقُوْلُ لِلوَرَثَةِ اعْتَقَوْا أَيْنَهُنَّ شِيْتُمُ اوْ اعْتِقُوا الَّتِي اكْبَرُ ظَلَكُمْ أَنَّهَا حُرَّةً وَلَكِنَّهُ يَسْتَلُهُمْ فَإِن زَعَمُوا
Rule: The original rule concerning private parts is prohibition. Likewise it is stated in Kashf al-Asrar, the commentary of Fakhr al-Islam: The original rule in marriage is prohibition, and it was permitted out of necessity. End. So when in a woman permissibility and prohibition are in opposition, prohibition prevails. Therefore, taharri (estimation) is not permissible in private parts. And in Kafi al-Hakim al-Shahid, from the chapter of taharri: If a man has four slave women and he freed a specific one, then forgot her and does not know which one he freed, it is not permissible for him to practice taharri for intercourse or for sale, and it is not permissible for the judge to leave him alone with them until the freed one is distinguished from the others. Similarly, if he divorced a specific one of his wives with three divorces and then forgot her, and similarly if he identified all of them except one, it is not permissible for him to approach her until he knows that she is not the divorced one. Likewise, the judge shall prevent him from her until it is informed that she is not the divorced one. When he is informed of that, he shall make him take an oath that he did not divorce this specific one with three, then he may allow them to be together. If he took the oath while ignorant of her, then he should not approach her. If he sold three of the slave women in the first case, and the judge ruled, if he allowed their sale and that was from his opinion, and deemed the remaining one to be the freed one, then if some of those sold return to him by purchase or gift or inheritance, he should not have intercourse with them because the judge ruled without knowledge. So he should not have intercourse with any of them by ownership unless he marries her; then it is fine because she is his wife or his slave woman. And taharri is not permitted in private parts because it is permitted in everything that is allowed by necessity, but private parts are not made permissible by necessity. End. Then he said: If he freed a slave woman from his slaves and then forgot her and died, it is not permissible for the judge to practice taharri, nor should he say to the heirs: 'Free whichever you wish' or 'Free the one you think most likely to be free'; rather, he should question them. If they claim...
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational qawida in Hanafi fiqh: al-asl fi al-abda' al-tahrim (the original rule concerning private parts is prohibition). The author cites Kashf al-Asrar to reinforce that even marriage (nikah) is originally prohibited and only permitted out of necessity for procreation. When permissibility and prohibition conflict regarding a woman, prohibition prevails. Consequently, taharri (ijtihad by estimation) is not allowed in matters of private parts because doubt cannot override the original prohibition. The passage then provides two applications from Kafi al-Hakim al-Shahid. First, if a man forgets which of his four slave women he freed, he cannot have intercourse with any or sell them until the freed one is identified; the judge must separate them. Second, if a man forgets which wife he divorced, he cannot approach any wife until the divorced one is known; the judge takes an oath and only then permits. The passage further discusses a variant where the judge mistakenly deems a sold slave woman as the freed one and she returns to the owner—intercourse is still impermissible unless through a new valid marriage or ownership. The passage concludes by emphasizing that taharri is permissible in other matters where necessity allows, but never in private parts. This qawida limits the general principle of ibaha (permissibility) and is essential in rulings regarding marriage, divorce, and sexual relations.

Key Terms
الأبضاع (al-abda'): Private parts; specifically in this context, matters of sexual relations and marriage.
تحري (taharri): Legal estimation or ijtihad to determine the most likely ruling when certainty is absent.
فروج (furuj): Private parts (genitalia); used as a term for matters of sexual intercourse and related legal issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida discussed, what should a man do if he forgets which specific wife he divorced with three divorces?
A) He may practice taharri to determine the most likely divorced wife and then divorce her again.
B) He may approach any wife after performing istikhara.
C) He must refrain from all wives until the divorced wife is definitively identified, and the judge takes an oath.
D) He may divorce all wives and then remarry them.

Key Takeaway
The original rule in private parts is prohibition; taharri is absolutely forbidden, and certainty is required before any permissibility.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
The Maxim: Original Ruling in Sexual Matters is Prohibition
Introduces and explains the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'الأصل في النكاح الحظر', explain its meaning and scope, and identify why permissibility is granted only out of necessity.

Core Idea
In sexual matters, prohibition is the default; permissibility is the exception granted for necessity.

This lesson introduces a core Hanafi legal maxim: in all matters relating to marriage and ownership of slave-girls, the original ruling is prohibition (haram). Permissibility is an exception allowed only for the preservation of human lineage. Understanding this maxim is essential for a mufti when ruling on cases of uncertainty in sexual matters, as it determines the weight given to prohibition over permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its literal meaning
Read the Arabic maxim 'الأصل في النكاح الحظر و أبيح للضرورة'. Understand that 'النكاح' here refers broadly to sexual matters (marriage and slave-girl ownership).
The term 'النكاح' is used in the general sense of sexual relations, not solely marriage.
2
Analyze the rationale for the maxim
The maxim states that original ruling is prohibition, but permissibility is granted out of necessity (for procreation). This follows the principle that human actions are permissible in principle, except for sexual matters which are governed by stricter rules.
This is a departure from the general rule that everything is permissible unless proven otherwise.
3
Determine the scope of the maxim
The maxim applies to nikah (marriage), talaq (divorce), and milk al-yamin (ownership of slave-girls). It also extends to any situation where a woman's permissibility is in doubt.
The scope is limited to matters involving private parts (furūj).
4
Apply the maxim to a basic conflict scenario
When permissibility and prohibition conflict regarding a woman, prohibition is given precedence. This means if there is doubt whether a woman is lawful, she is considered prohibited until certainty is established.
This is the direct application of the maxim in case of doubt.

تشریح جنسی معاملات میں اصل حرمت ہے، جنسی معاملات میں یعنی وہ مسائل جن کا تعلق ملک بیبین یا ملک نکاح سے ہے اس طرح کے مسائل میں اصل حرمت ہے لہذا جب حرمت اور حلت آپس میں متعارض ہو جا ئیں تو حرمت کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ الأصل في النكاح الحظر و ابيح للضرورة: جنسی معاملات میں اصل حرمت ہے اس لئے اصل کے اعتبار سے نکاح ممنوع ہونا چاہئے لیکن ضرورت کی وجہ سے نکاح کی اجاز دی گئی ہے بقا ء نسل انسانی اور توالدہ کے لئے۔ وإذا تقابل في المرأة حل و حرمة: اگر کسی عورت کے بارے میں شک ہو جائے کہ یہ حلال ہے یا حرام؟ یعنی اس عورت سے ولی جائز ہے یا نہیں تو حرمت والی جہت کو تر جیح ہوگی اور اس عورت کے حرام ہونے کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ ولهذا لا يجوز التحری: جنسی مسائل میں چونکہ اصل حرمت ہے اس لئے جب حلت و حرمت متعارض ہو جا ئیں تو بلا کسی تردد کے حرمت کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اس میں رفع شبہ کے لئے تحری کا کوئی جواز نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ فروج ( شرمگاہوں ) میں تحری جائز نہیں ہے یعنی شرمگاہوں کے بارے میں تحرمی کی بنیاد پر کوئی حکم نہیں لگایا جاسکتا۔ وفي كافي الحاكم الشهيد: إذا طلق احدى نساء: اگر کوئی شخص اپنی متعدد بیویوں میں سے ایک متعینہ کو طلاق دیکر بھول جائے کہ کیس کو طلاق دی تھی تو اب اس کے لئے حلت و حرمت کی جہت متعین کرنے کے لئے تحری کی گنجائش نہیں ہوگی بلکہ یقینی طور پر متعین کرنا ہوگا اور جب تک مطلقہ غیر مطلقہ سے ممتاز نہ ہو جائے حاکم کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ شوہر اور بیوی کو تخلیہ کا موقع دے۔
فَإِنْ بَاعَ فِي الْمَسْئَلَةِ الأولى ثلاثاً مِنَ الْجَوَارِي فَحَكَّمَ الْحَاكِمُ فَإِنْ أَجَازَ بَيْعَهُنَّ وَكَانَ ذلِكَ مِنْ رَائِهِ وَجَعَلَ الْبَاقِيَة هي المعلقة ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ بَعْضُ مَنْ بَاعَ بِشِرَاءٍ أَوْهِيَةٍ أَوْ مِيرَاتِ لَمْ يَنْبَغِ لَهُ أَنْ يَطَاهَا لأَنَّ الْقَاضِي قَضَى فِيْهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ فَلَا يَنْبَغِي لَهُ أَنْ يُطَا شَيْئاً مِنْهُنَّ بِالْمِلْكِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَرَوْجَهَا فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا بَأسَ لأَنَّهَا زَوْجَتُهُ أَوْ أَمَتَهُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحَرِّى في الفُرُوحِ لأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ فِي كُلِّ مَاجَازَ لِلضَّرُورَةِ وَالْفُرُوْجُ لَا تَحِلُّ بِالضَّرُورَةِ انْتَهَى ثُمَّ قَالَ وَلَوْ أَعْتَقَ جَارِيَةً مِنْ رَقِيقِهِ ثُمَّ نَسِيَهَا وَمَاتَ لَمْ يَجُزُ لِلْقَاضِي التَّحَرُى وَلَا يَقُوْلُ لِلوَرَثَةِ اعْتَقَوْا أَيْنَهُنَّ شِيْتُمُ اوْ اعْتِقُوا الَّتِي اكْبَرُ ظَلَكُمْ أَنَّهَا حُرَّةً وَلَكِنَّهُ يَسْتَلُهُمْ فَإِن زَعَمُوا ان الميت اعتق هذه بعينها أعتقها واستخلفهم على عِلمِهِمْ فِي الْبَاقِيَاتِ فَإِن لَّمْ يَعْرِفُوا من ذلك شَيْئاً أَعْقَهُنَّ كُلُهُنَّ وَ اسْقَط عَنْهُنَّ قَيْمَةً إِحْدَاهُنَّ وَسَعَيْنَ فِيْمَا بَقِيَ انْتَهَى
Explanation: In sexual matters, the original ruling is prohibition. Sexual matters are those related to ownership of bondwomen or marriage. In such matters, the original ruling is prohibition. Therefore, when prohibition and permissibility conflict, prohibition is given precedence. The original ruling in marriage is prohibition, and it was permitted out of necessity for the preservation of the human race and procreation. When permissibility and prohibition conflict regarding a woman, the side of prohibition is given precedence, and she is judged to be prohibited. Hence, taharri (juristic speculation) is not permissible. Therefore, when permissibility and prohibition conflict, prohibition is given precedence without any hesitation. Taharri is not allowed to remove doubt because taharri is not permissible regarding private parts. In Kafi al-Hakim al-Shahid: If a person divorces one of his wives and then forgets which one, taharri is not allowed for him to determine permissibility and prohibition. Rather, he must determine with certainty, and until the divorced woman is distinguished from the non-divorced, it is not permissible for the judge to allow the husband and wife to be alone. If in the first issue he sold three of the slave-girls, and the judge ruled, and if he validated their sale based on his opinion and considered the remaining one to be the freed one, then if some of the sold slave-girls return to him through purchase, gift, or inheritance, he should not have intercourse with them because the judge ruled without knowledge. He should not have intercourse with any of them by ownership unless he marries her, then there is no harm because she is his wife or his slave-girl. And taharri is not permissible regarding private parts because it is permissible in everything that is permissible out of necessity, but private parts are not permissible out of necessity. Then he said: If he freed a slave-girl from his slaves and then forgot her and died, it is not permissible for the judge to use taharri, nor shall he say to the heirs: 'Free whichever of them you wish' or 'Free the one you most strongly think is free.' Rather, he shall question them. If they claim that the deceased freed this specific one, he frees her and takes an oath from them regarding their knowledge of the remaining ones. If they do not know anything about that, he frees all of them and drops the value of one of them, and they (the remaining) must seek emancipation by working.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage discusses a key legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh: 'الأصل في النكاح الحظر' (the original ruling in sexual matters is prohibition). The author explains that in all matters related to marriage and ownership of slave-girls, the default ruling is prohibition (haram). Permissibility is granted only out of necessity for procreation. Therefore, when uncertainty arises—whether a particular woman is permissible or prohibited—the cautious approach is to give precedence to prohibition. This is why juristic speculation (taharrī) is not allowed in matters concerning private parts (furūj). The text provides two practical applications from Al-Kāfī by al-Ḥākim al-Shahīd: First, if a man divorces one of his wives but forgets which one, he cannot rely on taharrī; he must determine certainty, and the judge must separate them until the matter is resolved. Second, if a man frees one of his slave-girls and forgets which one, then dies, the judge cannot ask the heirs to guess; rather, the judge must question them. If they specify, that is accepted; otherwise, all slave-girls are freed, and one's value is waived, while the others must work to earn their freedom. This illustrates the principle that in sexual matters, certainty is required, and conjecture is insufficient.

Key Terms
تحری (taharrī): Juristic speculation or conjecture to determine the correct ruling when faced with uncertainty.
فروج (furūj): Private parts; specifically, the genitals, and by extension, all sexual matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the original ruling (hukm asli) in sexual matters according to the Hanafi maxim?
A) Permissibility (ibahah)
B) Recommendation (nadb)
C) Prohibition (hurmah)
D) Neutral (mubah)

Key Takeaway
The original ruling in sexual matters is prohibition; permissibility is granted only out of necessity, and in cases of doubt, prohibition prevails over permissibility.

Applying the Maxim: Prohibition of Taharrī and Case Rulings
Applies the maxim to cases of uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim to specific cases of uncertainty in sexual matters, explain why taharrī is prohibited, and derive the correct rulings for forgotten wife and manumitted slave-girl cases.

Core Idea
In sexual matters, certainty is required; taharrī is impermissible.

This lesson builds on the maxim by examining its direct application to practical cases. The text from Al-Kāfī illustrates how the maxim operates when a person forgets which wife he divorced or which slave-girl he freed. The main takeaway is that in all matters involving private parts, conjecture (taharrī) is not a valid method; only certainty suffices. Understanding these applications is crucial for a mufti when dealing with real-world queries.

Guided Path
1
Review the maxim and the prohibition of taharrī
Recall that the maxim gives precedence to prohibition. Taharrī is disallowed because it is a form of conjecture, and private parts require certainty.
The dabt 'لا يجوز التحري في الفروج' is the key.
2
Analyze the first case: forgotten divorce
If a man divorces one of his wives and forgets which one, he cannot rely on taharrī. He must determine with certainty. The judge must separate them until the identity of the divorced wife is known.
This prevents any possibility of illicit relations.
3
Analyze the second case: sold slave-girls and mistaken ruling
If a judge mistakenly validates a sale and considers the remaining slave-girl as the freed one, the returned slave-girls cannot be used for intercourse. Only through marriage can she become permissible.
The judge's ruling was without knowledge, so it is not binding for permissibility.
4
Analyze the third case: forgotten manumission after death
When a man frees one slave-girl and forgets which one, then dies, the judge cannot ask heirs to guess. He must question them directly. If they specify, that is accepted; otherwise, all are freed and adjustments made.
No reliance on conjecture even from heirs.

A) He may perform taharrī and act on his strongest guess.

Certainty vs. Necessity: The Exception for Marriage When Wet Nurse Identity is Unknown
Commentary on doubt in manumission and breastfeeding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' and its exception (rukhsah) to cases of doubt in manumission and breastfeeding.

Core Idea
Certainty remains until doubt is overcome; but necessity can open a door that doubt would otherwise close.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates a key tension between two major maxims: 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' and 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir.' Through two case studies—doubt over the identity of a freed slave and doubt over the wet nurse of a child—the commentator shows when the first maxim governs strictly and when the second allows a concession. Understanding this interaction is essential for a mufti weighing competing principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default principle
The core qawida: certainty is not removed by doubt. This governs the manumission case: when the identity of the freed slave is unknown, all must be freed and compensation paid; no taharrī (speculation) is allowed.
2
Note the manumission application
The passage details that if the master died without specifying which slave girl he freed, the heirs cannot guess; they must free all and subtract the value of one, with the slaves working to pay the rest.
This preserves the rights of the manumitted slave and avoids arbitrary selection.
3
Recognize the exception for breastfeeding
From Fatawa Qazi Khan: if a baby girl is breastfed by many village women and the identity of the wet nurse is unknown, a man from that village may marry her, as a rukhṣah to prevent the door of marriage from closing.
This exception is justified by necessity ('mashaqqah'), not by a weakening of the qawida itself.
4
Analyze the ruling from Al-Kafi
The passage also cites a case where multiple men own slave girls and one frees his; each man may continue intercourse with his own slave until certainty of which is freed arises. A mere strong assumption does not make it forbidden.
This shows that permissibility (ibāḥah) remains until prohibition is certain, consistent with the default principle.
5
Understand the rationale for the exception
The breastfeeding exception is based on preventing total blockage of marriage. If every potential marriage was prohibited due to doubt, the institution would suffer. Hence, necessity overrides the default restriction.
This is not a general license; it is a specific concession (rukhṣah) tied to necessity.

ان الميت اعتق هذه بعينها أعتقها واستخلفهم على علمهم في الباقيات فإن لم يعرفوا من ذلك شيئاً أعتقونهن كلهن واسقط عنهن قيمة إحداهن وسعين فيما بقي. ولو أعتق جارية من رقيقه فنسيها ومات لم يجز للقاضي التحري في الباقيات ولا يقول للورثة اعتقوا أيتكم شئتم أو من غلب على ظنكم أنه المعتق ولكن يسألهم فإن غلب على ظنهم أنه أعتق هذه بعينها أعتقها واستخلفهم على علمهم في الباقيات فإن لم يعرفوا من ذلك شيئاً أعتقونهن كلهن واسقط عنهن قيمة إحداهن وسعين فيما بقي. وخرج عن هذا الأصل مسألة في فتاوى قاضي خان صبية أرضعها قوم كثير من القرية أقلهم أو أكثرهم ولا يدرى من أرضعها وأراد واحد من أهل تلك القرية أن يتزوجها قال أبو القاسم الصفار إذا لم تظهر له علامة ولا يشهد أحد له بذلك يجوز نكاحها وهذا من باب الرخصة كيلا ينسد باب النكاح فلو اختلطت الرضيعة بنساء يحصون لم أره الآن ثم رأيت في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد ما يفيد الحلة. ولفظه ولو أن قوماً كان لكل منهم جارية فأعتق أحدهم جاريته ولم يعرفوا المعتقة فلكل واحد منهم أن يطأ جاريته حتى يعلم أنها المعتقة بعينها وإن كان أكثر رأي أحدهم أنه هو الذي أعتق فأحب إلي أنه لا يقرب حتى يستيقن ذلك ولو قرب لم يكن ذلك حراما.
If the deceased freed a specific one (of his slave girls), he frees her, and he asks them (the heirs) about their knowledge regarding the remaining ones. If they know nothing about that, he frees all of them, and drops the value of one of them, and they (the slaves) work to pay for the rest. And if a man frees a slave girl from his slaves, then forgets her and dies, it is not permissible for the judge to make an effort (taharrī) regarding the remaining ones, nor does he say to the heirs: 'Free whomever you wish or the one you strongly think is the freed one.' Rather, he asks them. If they strongly think that he freed a specific one, he frees her and asks them about their knowledge regarding the remaining ones. If they know nothing about that, he frees all of them, drops the value of one of them, and they work to pay for the rest. Excepted from this principle is a case in Fatawa Qazi Khan: A baby girl who was breastfed by many people of the village, the least or most of them, and it is not known who breastfed her, and a man from that village wants to marry her. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said: If no sign appears to him and no one testifies for him regarding that, her marriage is permissible. This is from the chapter of concession (rukhsah) so that the door of marriage is not closed. If the breastfed girl is mixed among countable women, I have not seen it now. Then I saw in al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid what indicates permissibility. And his wording: 'If a group of men each have a slave girl, and one of them frees his slave girl and they do not know the freed one, then every one of them may have intercourse with his slave girl until he knows that she is the freed one specifically. If one of them strongly thinks that he is the one who freed, I prefer that he does not approach her until he is certain; but if he approaches, it is not forbidden.'
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on doubt (shakk) regarding which slave girl was freed, and an exception (istithnā’) based on necessity. The original principle is that when the identity of the freed slave girl is unknown, the heirs must not engage in taharrī (speculation) but must free all and compensate. This protects against violating the rights of the manumitted slave. However, from this principle an exception is derived from Fatawa Qazi Khan: a baby girl breastfed by multiple women of a village (with no knowledge of who her milk-mothers are) may be married by any man from that village according to Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar. This is a rukhṣah (concession) to prevent the door of marriage from closing completely due to overwhelming doubt. The author also cites a case from al-Kafi: if multiple men own slave girls and one frees his without identification, each man may continue intercourse with his own slave until certainty of identity arises; a mere strong assumption does not make it forbidden. This shows that the default ruling (ibāḥah) remains until certainty of prohibition is established, which is a manifestation of the qāʿidah 'al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). Yet the exception for the breastfed girl prioritizes necessity ('al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysīr') to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Effort to determine the correct identity of the freed slave or wet nurse through speculation or guesswork
شك (shakk): Doubt as to which specific slave was freed or which woman breastfed the child
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession allowing marriage despite doubt to prevent the complete closure of marriage possibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a man from a village where many women breastfed a baby girl and he wishes to marry her, if no sign or testimony is available?
A) The marriage is forbidden due to uncertainty.
B) The marriage is permissible as a concession to avoid blocking marriage.
C) The man must perform taharrī to identify the wet nurses.
D) The marriage is valid only if the girl is not among the counted women.

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' is overridden by the necessity maxim when doubt would otherwise block a vital social good like marriage.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Exception to the Rule of Certainty in Prohibition
Explains the limitation of the maxim 'certainty of prohibition prohibits all' and its exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim regarding definite cause (sabab muhqaq) to cases of breastfeeding and manumission, and identify when the exception applies due to doubt.

Core Idea
The rule that uncertainty prohibits all only applies when the cause is definite; if the cause itself is doubtful, the rule is suspended.

This passage expands a key Hanafi qa'idah: when a definite cause of prohibition (e.g., breastfeeding or manumission) exists but the specific prohibited person is unknown, all potential persons are prohibited until identification. However, what happens when the cause itself is uncertain? The authors present a crucial exception: if the cause of prohibition is not definitely established, the prohibition is lifted to prevent hardship and closure of marriage. This lesson walks you through the maxim, its exception, and its practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its condition
State the maxim: 'This rule applies only when there is a definite cause of prohibition regarding a woman.' Understand that the maxim requires a certain (muhqaq) cause.
The cause must be qat'i al-thubut; doubt in the cause invalidates the rule.
2
Recognize the exception: cause uncertain
When the cause itself is doubtful (e.g., unknown breastfeeding), the rule does not apply. The text calls this a 'concession to prevent closing the door of marriage.'
This aligns with the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' and 'Hardship begets facility.'
3
Apply to the breastfeeding case
A girl breastfed by many women in a village—unknown who nursed her. Marriage to a man from the village is permissible until a sign or testimony identifies the foster-mother.
The prohibition (mahramiyyat) cannot be established because the cause is uncertain.
4
Apply to the manumission cases
Multiple slave girls, one freed but unknown. Each owner may have intercourse until the freed one is identified (cause is certain, but specific person unknown). Different ruling for a single buyer purchasing all vs. all except one.
Here the cause (freedom) is definite, so the general rule applies until identification.
5
Synthesize: When does the exception apply?
The exception applies only when the cause of prohibition itself is doubtful (e.g., unknown breastfeeding). If the cause is certain but the specific person is unknown, the general prohibition remains until identification.
This distinction is critical for correct fatwa.

في المرأة سبب محقق للحرمة فلو كان في الحرمة شك لم يعتبر ولذا قالوا لو أدخلت المرأة حلمة ثديها في فم رضيعة ووع...
And there is excluded from this principle a case in Fatawa Qazi Khan: A girl who was breastfed by many people of the village, few or many, and it is not known who breastfed her. A man from that village wants to marry her. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said: If no sign appears to him and no one bears witness for him, her marriage is permissible. This is from the chapter of concession, to prevent closing the door of marriage. If the nursling mixes with countable women, I have not seen it now. Then I saw in al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid what indicates permissibility. Urdu translation: And from this principle, a case from Fatawa Qazi Khan is excluded... Explanation: This case is formally outside this rule, but in reality it does not fall under this rule because in this case there is no testimony that would establish definite prohibition; it is only a matter of prohibition, so leniency is given because marriage is a necessity. This case is from the chapter of concession. So when many village women breastfed a girl, then the girl forgot who they were, if a man from that village wants to marry her, he may do so as long as no sign appears and no testimony is given. Because if permission to marry were not given, the door of marriage would close. Therefore, there is concession in this case as Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said. 'For if the nursling mixes': If the nursling girl mixes with other girls, then in al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid it is stated that he may marry whichever he wishes, because if permission were not given, the door of marriage would be closed. And his wording: 'If there are people, each of whom has a slave girl, and one of them frees his slave girl and they do not know the freed one, then each of them may have intercourse with his slave girl until he knows that she is the specific freed one. And if the predominant opinion of one of them is that it was he who freed, then I prefer that he not approach until he is certain. If he does approach, it is not unlawful.' Urdu translation: If some people each have a slave girl, then one of them frees his slave girl and the freed one is unknown, then each of them may have intercourse with his slave girl until it becomes known which specific one is freed. If one of them has a dominant opinion that he freed his slave girl, then I prefer that he not approach until he is certain. If he does approach, it is not unlawful. Explanation: When several people each have their own slave girls, and one of them frees his slave girl but it is not known which one, then when it is known with certainty, he must stop using her. Objection: When each person has one slave girl, it is obvious that each knows his own slave girl; so what does 'they do not know the freed one' mean? Answer: The commentator says that upon reflection it becomes clear that they owned the slave girls through a representative, so each was not specified individually. Then someone freed his slave girl and forgot which one he freed. In that case, no one knows the freed one, neither the freed one nor the manumitter is specified. 'And if one man bought them all, knowing that, it is not permissible for him to approach any of them until he knows the freed one. And if he bought all except one, intercourse with them is permissible. Then if he does so and then buys the remaining one, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with any of them, nor to sell them until he knows the freed one among them.' End. Urdu translation: If one man bought all these slave girls, knowing that one of them was freed but not specifically, then it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with any of them because each is in the position of the freed one. But if he bought all except one, intercourse is permissible. If he has intercourse with one from the bought ones and then buys the remaining one, then until it becomes known, neither is intercourse permissible nor is buying and selling permissible. 'Then know that this rule applies only when there is a definite cause of prohibition regarding a woman. If there is doubt concerning the prohibition, it is not considered. Thus they said: If a woman put the nipple of her breast into the mouth of a nursling and...'
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a legal maxim (qa'idah) with its applications and exceptions. The author discusses the rule that when there is a definite cause (sabab muhqaq) for prohibition (e.g., freeing a slave girl or breastfeeding), but the specific prohibited person is unknown, then all potential persons are prohibited until the specific one is identified. However, an exception exists when the cause of prohibition itself is uncertain. The first case from Fatawa Qazi Khan illustrates this: a girl breastfed by many women in a village, with no knowledge of who nursed her. Since the prohibition (mahram relationship) cannot be established definitively, marriage is permissible as a concession to avoid closing the door of marriage. The second case involves multiple slave girls where one is freed but unknown. Here, the cause of prohibition (freedom) is certain, but the specific freed girl is unknown. The ruling differs: each owner may continue marital relations with his slave girl until certainty; if a buyer purchases all, he may not approach any until identification, but if he buys all except one, he may approach the bought ones. The passage concludes by clarifying that the rule applies only when the cause of prohibition is definite; if there is doubt, the rule does not apply, as in the breastfeeding case where the cause itself is doubtful.

Key Terms
سبب محقق (sabab muhqaq): A certain and established cause that creates a legal prohibition, e.g., breastfeeding that establishes mahramiyyat or manumission that prohibits intercourse.
رضيعة (radi'ah): A female nursling, i.e., a girl who was breastfed.
معتقة (mu'taqah): A female slave who has been manumitted (freed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from Fatawa Qazi Khan, why is marriage permissible for a man from the village to a girl who was breastfed by many unknown women?
A) Because the breastfeeding is considered void in Hanafi law.
B) Because the cause of prohibition (specific breastfeeding relationship) is not established with certainty.
C) Because the girl consented to marriage.
D) Because the man has a predominant opinion that she is not his foster-sister.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim applies only when the cause of prohibition is definite; if the cause itself is doubtful, the prohibition is lifted as a concession.
